# Agent Log

Append-only run log for the autonomous dev agent. Every run writes one entry
here, regardless of outcome. Review cycles write a separate `REVIEW-LOG.md`
entry AND flag this entry with `review_proposed: true` ‚Äî so the log never has
gaps.

## Format

```
---

### Run [YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM]
- Task: TASK-XXX ‚Äî <title> (or "N/A ‚Äî no tasks available")
- Outcome: success | blocked | skipped | success_with_warning
- PR: <URL or N/A>
- Test counts: <workspace counts>
- Files changed: <list>
- Regression alert: true | false
- Review proposed: true | false
- Deploy: success | failed | n/a
- Lessons learned: <free text>
- Notes: <optional>
```

---

### Run [2026-04-20 18:30]
- Task: TASK-001 ‚Äî Scaffold root TS tooling (tsconfig.base, ESLint, Prettier)
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/2 (merged)
- Test counts: no workspaces yet ‚Äî skipped cleanly
- Files changed: tsconfig.base.json, eslint.config.js, .prettierrc.json, .prettierignore, scripts/run-workspaces.mjs, package.json, package-lock.json, .github/workflows/ci.yml, .claude/project.json, docker/docker-compose.yml
- Regression alert: false
- Review proposed: false (1 success in streak; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: pending (deploy.autoDeployOnMerge = true but first deploy will still fail until EPIC-01 produces an apps/server build; the Dockerfile COPY targets are empty)
- Lessons learned:
  - Original task description said "root tsconfig.json with project references" ‚Äî empty `references:[]` triggers TS18002. Solution-style root tsconfig deferred until at least one workspace has TS code. Roadmap tasks in the bootstrap tier should anticipate this.
  - `npm run <cmd> --workspaces --if-present` errors with "No workspaces found!" when the glob is empty ‚Äî `--if-present` doesn't help here. Wrapped with `scripts/run-workspaces.mjs` for graceful no-op.
  - CI previously used skip-if-missing guards to handle the pre-scaffold state; now unified through npm scripts ‚Üí simpler CI, same behaviour.
- Notes: First autonomous-run cycle on this project. Kicked off manually as a dry-run by /init-autonomous Phase 8; next fire is the systemd timer at top-of-hour.

### Run [2026-04-20 19:00]
- Task: TASK-003 ‚Äî Scaffold apps/mobile with Capacitor + add iOS/Android
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/4 (merged)
- Test counts: web=3 (unchanged)
- Files changed: apps/mobile/* (~70 files across ios/ and android/ scaffolds), .gitignore, package.json, package-lock.json
- Regression alert: false
- Review proposed: false (3 consecutive successes; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: deferred (apps/server still missing; Dockerfile COPY will fail until TASK-006 lands)
- Lessons learned:
  - Capacitor `cap add ios` + `cap add android` work fine on Linux for scaffolding ‚Äî only warnings are "pod install" and "xcodebuild" skipped (macOS-only, expected).
  - Need to gitignore `{ios,android}/.../public/` and `capacitor.config.json` copies (regenerated on every `cap sync` ‚Äî shouldn't live in git).
  - Also gitignored native build outputs: `build/`, `.gradle/`, `DerivedData/`, `Pods/`, `local.properties`.
  - Repo-level `deleteBranchOnMerge` setting is required for automatic remote branch deletion on squash-merge; `--delete-branch` on `gh pr merge --auto` alone is unreliable. Fixed in a manual step before this run.
  - Local branches from squash-merged PRs need `[gone]` upstream detection to clean up (not `git branch --merged main`, which doesn't see squashed branches). Candidate refinement for /autonomous-run Step 3 via /autonomous-review.
- Notes: Third autonomous-run cycle. Branch cleanup verified working end-to-end this time.

  - Root tsconfig.json with `"files": []` + `references: [...]` is the correct shape now that workspaces have composite TS ‚Äî resolves the TS18002-style problem flagged at TASK-001 by simply waiting until at least one referenced package exists.
  - `npm install` at root is required after adding new workspace package.jsons before the symlinks under `node_modules/@colonize/*` are created ‚Äî without it `--workspace=@colonize/shared` warns "no workspace folder present".
  - Prettier-formatted package.json is the canonical form: arrays expanded one-per-line. Adding a `package.json` template to `/autonomous-run` would dodge the format:check round-trip step.

### Run [2026-04-20 20:40]
- Task: TASK-006 ‚Äî Scaffold apps/server with Fastify + /health endpoint
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/10 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: server=2 (new baseline), web=8, core=1, shared=2, content=2
- Files changed: apps/server/package.json, apps/server/tsconfig.json, apps/server/src/index.ts, apps/server/src/app.ts, apps/server/src/app.test.ts, tsconfig.json, package-lock.json, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (server is a new workspace; existing counts steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak resets to 1/5 after PR #8 self-improvement merge)
- Deploy: build_failed (exit 1) ‚Äî new failure mode: `docker build` cannot reach the Docker daemon from the agent user (`permission denied while trying to connect to the docker API at unix:///var/run/docker.sock`). The previous Dockerfile-COPY blocker IS resolved by this PR (apps/server now exists), but `colonize` (uid 999) is not in the `docker` group and `no_new_privileges` prevents sudo elevation. Operator action required on the VPS: `usermod -aG docker colonize && systemctl restart claude-colonize.service`. Not cascading ‚Äî other roadmap tasks remain pickupable.
- Lessons learned:
  - Split the Fastify binary from the app factory (src/index.ts vs src/app.ts) so tests can `app.inject()` against the factory without ever binding a port ‚Äî avoids flaky port-in-use failures and keeps tests hermetic.
  - @colonize/shared's HealthResponse Zod schema served as both response validator and test assertion shape ‚Äî one source of truth for /health across server tests and future client consumers (PR #7 shared scaffold pays off here).
  - Prettier wants multi-line function-argument wrapping when the expression grows beyond the print-width; new server tests tripped format:check on the first pass. Could be caught upfront by running `prettier --write` on the changed files before the validation step.
- Notes: Sixth autonomous-run cycle. First success after the self-improvement review PR #8 / hotfix PR #9 ‚Äî TASK-006 completes STORY-04's server entrypoint; TASK-007/TASK-008 (Fastify static + CI deploy workflow) now unblocked.

### Run [2026-04-20 21:30]
- Task: TASK-007 ‚Äî Wire apps/server to serve apps/web static build
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/12 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: server=8 (was 2 ‚Äî added 6), web=8, core=1, shared=2, content=2
- Files changed: apps/server/package.json, apps/server/src/app.ts, apps/server/src/app.test.ts, apps/server/src/__fixtures__/web-dist/index.html, apps/server/src/__fixtures__/web-dist/assets/app.css, package-lock.json, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (server 2 ‚Üí 8; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: false (2 consecutive successes since the TASK-005 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî image colonize:latest built, docker-app-1 up, healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. End-to-end verified on deployed app: GET / returns apps/web/dist/index.html (title "Colonize ‚Äî NW 2191"), GET /some/spa/route falls back to index.html (SPA routing working in production), GET /favicon.svg serves directly as a static asset (200 + cache headers). Docker group perms unblocked since the TASK-006 failure (operator action implied). db container not spun up this deploy (likely pre-existing compose-ordering quirk when only app is needed for health gate) ‚Äî not cascading.
- Lessons learned:
  - Opting into static serving via a `staticRoot` option (rather than checking `NODE_ENV` inline) kept the tests hermetic ‚Äî fixture dir ships inside `apps/server/src/__fixtures__/` and only activates when the test passes the path. Keeps production auto-resolution (`apps/web/dist` relative to the compiled runtime file) separate from test concerns.
  - First cap-sync failure of the run was a stale EACCES on `android/capacitor-cordova-android-plugins/src/main/AndroidManifest.xml` that cleared on re-run. If this recurs across cycles, `/autonomous-review` should flag adding a `chmod -R u+w apps/mobile/android` pre-step or gitignore-audit ‚Äî see similar refinement in PR #9's learning trail.
  - Prettier trips on bare `*.css` fixtures; running `prettier --write` on new content files before first validation pass saves a cycle (repeated lesson from TASK-006).
- Notes: Seventh autonomous-run cycle. Streak: 2 consecutive successes since the TASK-005 review checkpoint (TASK-006 ‚Üí TASK-007); 3 more to re-hit successThreshold=5.

### Run [2026-04-20 22:05]
- Task: TASK-008 ‚Äî Add GitHub Actions deploy workflow (main ‚Üí VPS)
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/14 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: server=8, web=8, core=1, shared=2, content=2 (all unchanged)
- Files changed: .github/workflows/deploy.yml (new), roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false
- Review proposed: false (3 consecutive successes since the TASK-005 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success (local /deploy path); new GH Actions workflow ran in parallel and failed on "missing server host" as expected (SSH_HOST / SSH_PRIVATE_KEY secrets not yet provisioned). Local deploy: colonize:latest rebuilt, docker-app-1 recreated, healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health; GET returns {"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":~4s}. GH Actions run: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/actions/runs/24693256793 (conclusion: failure at SSH step ‚Äî operator action required to set secrets before this path becomes authoritative).
- Lessons learned:
  - `git reset --hard origin/main` in the remote deploy script is dangerous when the VPS checkout doubles as the autonomous agent's working directory (mid-feature-branch work would be wiped). Guarded by a current-branch check that bails if HEAD != main, and fast-forward-only pull. Safer default.
  - Two on-merge deploy actors now exist: (a) the systemd-timer agent running /autonomous-run step 12 on the VPS, (b) this new GH Actions workflow. `concurrency: deploy-production` serialises within Actions but the local-on-VPS run is a separate actor. Pick a winner in a follow-up; both race inside `docker compose build`.
- Notes: Eighth autonomous-run cycle. Infra-only change (no workspace code touched). Streak: 3 consecutive successes since the TASK-005 review checkpoint; 2 more to re-hit successThreshold=5.

### Run [2026-04-21 00:17]
- Task: TASK-010 ‚Äî Load placeholder atlas in Phaser boot scene
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/16 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: server=8, web=11 (was 8 ‚Äî added asset-keys invariants + GameCanvas mount smoke), content=9, core=1, shared=2
- Files changed: apps/web/package.json, apps/web/src/App.{tsx,css}, apps/web/src/GameCanvas.{tsx,test.tsx}, apps/web/src/game/{asset-keys,boot-scene,main-menu-scene,create-game,index}.ts, apps/web/src/game/boot-scene.test.ts, apps/web/src/test-setup.ts, apps/web/scripts/prepare-assets.mjs, packages/content/package.json, packages/content/scripts/generate-placeholder-sources.mjs, packages/content/atlas-src/core/{tile_deck,tile_hull,tile_ocean}.png, .gitignore, package-lock.json, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (web 8 ‚Üí 11; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: true ‚Äî https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/17 (5 consecutive successes since the TASK-005 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-006 ‚Üí TASK-007 ‚Üí TASK-008 ‚Üí TASK-009 ‚Üí TASK-010 ‚Äî threshold hit; /autonomous-review drafted 4 refinements)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, ~33s builder phase), manifest sha256:ab4f2631134c720eac1c15bff83f7a91ed55f2e08fb9920a8602c1832fcad6fe, docker-app-1 recreated rolling. Healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":6.266}`). Root `/` serves apps/web/dist (200 OK) and `/atlas/core/spritesheet.{png,json}` both 200 ‚Äî atlas pipeline confirmed end-to-end in prod image.
- Lessons learned:
  - Phaser 3 top-level module init calls `canvas.getContext('2d')` in CanvasFeatures.js, which throws under jsdom. Dynamic-importing the Phaser bundle inside `GameCanvas`'s `useEffect` keeps it out of the test module graph entirely; pair with a `HTMLCanvasElement.getContext = () => null` stub in test-setup so our own mount-guard probe stops triggering jsdom's "not implemented" virtualConsole warning.
  - Atlas pipeline shape: commit raw sprite PNGs under `packages/content/atlas-src/<atlas>/` (source), gitignore `atlas-out/` (pack-atlas output) and `apps/web/public/atlas/` (web-served copy). `apps/web` `predev`/`prebuild` runs pack-atlas then copies the packed folder in. One command path for dev + CI.
  - Placeholder sprite generator uses `pngjs` directly (added to content devDeps ‚Äî was transitively available via free-tex-packer-core, but making it explicit keeps the script's deps honest) and pulls colours from the OTK palette so the placeholder atlas already respects tonal registers.
  - Vite build warns on the Phaser chunk (~1.48 MB uncompressed / 340 kB gzip). Acceptable for MVP ‚Äî code-splitting is a later concern and not in task scope.
- Notes: Tenth autonomous-run cycle. Fifth consecutive success since the TASK-005 review checkpoint (TASK-006 ‚Üí TASK-007 ‚Üí TASK-008 ‚Üí TASK-009 ‚Üí TASK-010). Streak hits successThreshold=5 ‚Äî /autonomous-review should fire in Step 15 against this log + main.

### Run [2026-04-21 01:10]
- Task: TASK-011 ‚Äî Create event bus in apps/web/src/bus.ts
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/18 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: server=8, web=20 (was 11 ‚Äî added 9 bus tests), core=1, shared=2, content=9
- Files changed: apps/web/src/bus.ts (new), apps/web/src/bus.test.ts (new), apps/web/package.json, apps/web/tsconfig.json, packages/shared/src/index.ts, package-lock.json, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (web 11 ‚Üí 20; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: false (1 consecutive success since PR #17 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, ~33s builder), manifest sha256:4fec4e54b48f, docker-app-1 recreated rolling. Healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":4.465}`); `/` serves apps/web/dist (HTTP 200). `@colonize/shared` now emitted into the runtime image via `COPY packages/shared/dist` (was already in the Dockerfile from earlier epics) ‚Äî no Dockerfile edit required.
- Lessons learned:
  - `Record<string, unknown>` is too strict as a generic constraint for event-map types: an `interface { 'turn:advanced': { turn: number } }` is NOT assignable to it under `strict` because it lacks an index signature. Using `extends object` for the bus generic and removing the `EventMap` alias entirely keeps the typing end-to-end ergonomic for interface-shaped event maps (which are what GameEvents will be as feature tasks extend it via declaration merging).
  - ESLint `@typescript-eslint/no-empty-object-type` is on via `recommended`, so `interface GameEvents {}` would fail lint. Seeded the contract with one real starter event (`turn:advanced` ‚Äî naturally needed by TASK-012 HUD + TASK-025 end-turn wiring) rather than disabling the rule; keeps the shared-package API tested end-to-end from day one.
  - `apps/web` wiring a new workspace dep (`@colonize/shared`) requires three co-ordinated touches: dependency in `package.json`, TS project reference in `tsconfig.json`, and running `npm install` at repo root to materialise the `node_modules/@colonize/shared` symlink. All three were needed this run ‚Äî future workspace-linking tasks should expect the same triad.
- Notes: Eleventh autonomous-run cycle. First success since PR #17 merged the prior review batch (streak reset). Four more consecutive successes to re-hit successThreshold=5.

---

### Run [2026-04-21 02:10]
- Task: TASK-012 ‚Äî Build HUD components (resource bar, year, end-turn)
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/19 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: server=8, web=32 (was 20 ‚Äî +8 HUD, +3 store faction, +1 App HUD smoke), core=1, shared=2, content=9
- Files changed: apps/web/src/hud/Hud.tsx (new), apps/web/src/hud/Hud.module.css (new), apps/web/src/hud/Hud.test.tsx (new), apps/web/src/store/game.ts, apps/web/src/store/game.test.ts, apps/web/src/App.tsx, apps/web/src/App.test.tsx, apps/web/src/App.css, CLAUDE.md, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (web 20 ‚Üí 32; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: false (2 consecutive successes since PR #17 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (manifest sha256:f54212936827), docker-app-1 recreated rolling. Healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":7.063}`); `/` serves apps/web/dist (HTTP 200). Build artefacts sizes stable (web bundle 148.85 kB main + 1,483.58 kB phaser).
- Lessons learned:
  - Vite supports `*.module.css` out of the box and `vite/client` (already in `apps/web/tsconfig.json` types) declares the ambient import ‚Äî no extra tooling, no `.d.ts` shim, no devDep bump. Picking CSS Modules over Tailwind for the HUD kept the PR surface-area at just source files.
  - Under vitest `css: false` (default), CSS Module imports return a Proxy that resolves any accessed key to a stub ‚Äî tests see `styles.hud` as undefined/ignored className. Identifying HUD elements via `data-testid` rather than class names makes tests robust to that and to future CSS-Module hashing in production.
  - Layering React chrome over the Phaser canvas works cleanly with a `.game-stage` wrapper (`position: relative`) + `.hud { position: absolute; inset: 0; pointer-events: none }` + `.hud > * { pointer-events: auto }`. The inherited-none + child-auto pattern lets overlay regions (top-left, top-right, bottom-right) stay click-through where empty, so Phaser receives map clicks unimpeded. Future HUD additions should keep to this container pattern.
- Notes: Twelfth autonomous-run cycle. Streak=2 toward successThreshold=5. Faction chip reads from store so TASK-014 (faction-select screen) already has its data slot wired ‚Äî only a `setFaction` call needed from the select UI.

---

### Run [2026-04-21 03:15]
- Task: TASK-013 ‚Äî Main menu screen (React)
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/20 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: server=8, web=39 (was 32 ‚Äî +5 MainMenu, +3 store screen state, ‚Äì1 App HUD smoke replaced by 3 screen-routing tests net +2 but App itself went 4 ‚Üí 3), core=1, shared=2, content=9
- Files changed: apps/web/src/menu/MainMenu.tsx (new), apps/web/src/menu/MainMenu.module.css (new), apps/web/src/menu/MainMenu.test.tsx (new), apps/web/src/store/game.ts, apps/web/src/store/game.test.ts, apps/web/src/App.tsx, apps/web/src/App.test.tsx, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (web 32 ‚Üí 39; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: false (3 consecutive successes since PR #17 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest sha256:38938ce5e829), docker-app-1 recreated rolling. Healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Build artefact sizes stable (web main 151.16 kB + phaser 1,483.58 kB).
- Lessons learned:
  - Screen routing for single-page flows lives cleanly in the zustand store as a `screen` literal-union (`'menu' | 'faction-select' | 'game'`) rather than a router ‚Äî no extra dep, faction-select stub is trivially ownable by TASK-014, and tests can set the screen state directly in `beforeEach` without spelunking through navigation events.
  - Menu-screen-as-default broke the previous App tests that assumed the game stage mounts on load (HUD test was looking for `hud-end-turn` at root). Refactor was to split the App suite into default-screen (menu) vs explicit-`setScreen('game')` tests ‚Äî cheaper than keeping the game-stage at root and gating menu as a modal, and it mirrors the actual production UX.
  - Inline SVG heraldry is a reasonable MVP choice: two mirrored `<g>` groups with `transform="scale(-1 1)"` give us paired-dragon silhouettes without any new asset pipeline. Dedicated pixel-art heraldry lands with content epics, but the test just pins the role + aria-label so swapping the SVG for a raster later won't churn tests.
- Notes: Thirteenth autonomous-run cycle. Streak=3 toward successThreshold=5 (TASK-011 ‚Üí TASK-012 ‚Üí TASK-013 since PR #17 review checkpoint).

- Regression alert: false (core 1 ‚Üí 27; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: true ‚Äî https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/23 (5 consecutive successes since PR #17 checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-011 ‚Üí TASK-012 ‚Üí TASK-013 ‚Üí TASK-014 ‚Üí TASK-017 ‚Äî threshold hit; /autonomous-review drafted 4 refinements covering HUD overlay click-through, inline-SVG heraldry, string-literal const-object enums, and zustand-store screen routing)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, ~30s builder, manifest list sha256:8cdde3108b66 / image sha256:af96cede673e), docker-app-1 recreated rolling. Healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":4.818}`). Web bundle sizes stable (main 154.89 kB + phaser 1,483.58 kB). `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. New `@colonize/core` map module is part of `packages/core/dist` shipped into the runtime image (already covered by the existing `COPY --from=builder /app/packages/core/dist` step in the Dockerfile).
- Lessons learned:
  - Used a const-object + derived `type` for `TileType` instead of a TypeScript `enum`. `isolatedModules: true` (tsconfig.base.json) makes `const enum` unsafe across project boundaries, and a regular `enum` would inflate the @colonize/core surface with a runtime object that's mostly redundant with the typed string-literal union. Const-object pairs cleanly with the JSON serialise/revive path: `tiles` are plain strings on the wire and survive `JSON.parse` without an enum-rebuild step.
  - Picked 8-connected neighbours (Moore neighbourhood) over 4-connected for parity with Sid Meier Colonization 1994. EPIC-04 pathfinding (TASK-028 A*) and EPIC-03 fog-of-war (TASK-022) will both consume `neighbours()`; if either later wants 4-connected (e.g. for sailing-only constraints), the call site can filter `dx === 0 || dy === 0` rather than us splitting the API.
  - `noUnusedLocals` + `exactOptionalPropertyTypes` made `tiles[i]!` non-null assertion necessary at the post-validation copy site in `fromJSON` even though the loop has just guarded each entry ‚Äî this is the strict-mode tradeoff. Keeping the validation loop and the copy loop separate (rather than fusing them) keeps the error message specific to the offending index, which matters more for save-format debugging than the micro-cost of a second pass.

### Run [2026-04-21 06:10]
- Task: TASK-018 ‚Äî Procedural map generator
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/24 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: server=8, web=42, content=15, core=78 (was 27 ‚Äî +51 generator tests), shared=2
- Files changed: packages/core/src/map/generate.ts (new), packages/core/src/map/generate.test.ts (new), packages/core/src/map/index.ts, packages/core/src/index.ts, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 27 ‚Üí 78; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: false (1 consecutive success since PR #23 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, ~30s builder, manifest list sha256:8e0e646cf116 / image sha256:155497c3f921), docker-app-1 recreated rolling. Healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":5.505}`). Web bundle sizes stable (main 154.89 kB + phaser 1,483.58 kB). `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. Generator module is part of `packages/core/dist` already copied into the runtime image ‚Äî no Dockerfile change required.
- Lessons learned:
  - Mulberry32 is the right PRNG for procedural map generation here: 32-bit state, <10 lines, deterministic for a given integer seed (including negatives ‚Äî `seed | 0` normalises to 32-bit signed on entry). No extra dep, survives tsc strict + `isolatedModules` cleanly, and lets every stage of the generator draw from a single seeded stream so the whole map is reproducible from one `{seed, width, height}` triple.
  - Organic island + red-tide blobs are cheapest to grow via "pick random existing cell ‚Üí pick random Ocean neighbour ‚Üí set" with a stall counter (targetSize √ó 3 stalls ‚áí abort). Simpler than cellular-automata steps and produces the irregular silhouettes C64/retro Colonization had. Works because corridor/cities are placed first and islands only overwrite Ocean ‚Äî no overlap handling needed.
  - Faction starts split the map into a `ceil(sqrt(n)) √ó ceil(n/cols)` grid, jitter the slot centre, then BFS outward to the nearest unused Ocean tile. This is robust to corridor drift (the slot centre might land on RayonPassage) and to islands covering a whole slot (BFS escapes outward), while keeping starts well-spread ‚Äî the quadrant-spread assertion passes across every seed tested. Keeping factionCount as a bare integer (not faction IDs) honours the core-is-framework-free rule: no `@colonize/content` dep crept in.
  - `MIN_MAP_WIDTH=20 / MIN_MAP_HEIGHT=15` is enough headroom for the full feature budget (corridor+cities ‚âà 27 cells, islands 8‚Äì90 cells, red-tide 3‚Äì24 cells, FM 3‚Äì6 cells, all fit in 300 cells with margin) while still rejecting obviously-too-small inputs up-front. Validation throws `TypeError` for non-integer seed and `RangeError` for dimensions/factionCount out of range ‚Äî matches the pattern `GameMap` set in TASK-017.
- Notes: Fifteenth autonomous-run cycle. Streak=1 since PR #23 review checkpoint; four more consecutive successes to re-hit successThreshold=5.

- Review proposed: false (2 consecutive successes since PR #23 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:a1eb07cbc479 / image sha256:9d4e2669f214, builder ~30s incl. placeholder atlas regeneration for the 7 new tile PNGs), docker-app-1 recreated rolling. Healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":5.649}`). Web bundle sizes unchanged (main 154.89 kB + phaser 1,486.02 kB). `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. New atlas sources are baked into the runtime image via the existing `COPY --from=builder /app/packages/content` step ‚Äî no Dockerfile change required.
- Lessons learned:
  - The source/packed/served atlas pipeline landed in TASK-010 finally paid off this cycle ‚Äî adding six new terrain sprites + two extra ocean frames only needed extensions to `generate-placeholder-sources.mjs` and the committed `atlas-src/core/*.png` inputs; `prepare-assets` auto-repacks on `predev`/`prebuild` so no one has to remember the intermediate step. Tests assert frame coverage by reading the committed `atlas-src/core/*.png` filenames directly (stripping `.png`) rather than the packed-atlas JSON ‚Äî that JSON is gitignored and only materialises after `prepare-assets`, which CI doesn't run before `npm test`. Initial test revision tried to read `public/atlas/core/spritesheet.json` and failed in CI; the second commit (`fix: read atlas source PNGs not packed JSON ‚Ä¶`) is the durable shape.
  - Pulling the tile-layout maths into three pure helpers (`tileCenterInWorld`, `mapWorldBounds`, `renderedTileSize`) in `tile-atlas.ts` kept GameScene's arithmetic unit-testable under jsdom without spinning up a real Phaser runtime. Phaser's module graph pokes WebGL/Canvas at import time, so anything that needs test coverage has to live outside `game-scene.ts`'s import chain ‚Äî otherwise the test-runner setup's `getContext ‚Üí null` stub isn't enough and the whole scene module cascades Phaser into the test.
  - Ocean-tile animation phase is seeded deterministically from `((x*7 + y*3) % 11) / 11` via `anims.setProgress()`. This gives every ocean tile a per-tile offset without any RNG dependency, so two runs from the same GameMap produce the same animation state ‚Äî useful later for deterministic replays, and cheaper than storing per-tile phase state.

- Review proposed: false (3 consecutive successes since PR #23 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~30s, manifest list sha256:ba22eb9326e1, image sha256:4a8f1864e222), docker-app-1 recreated rolling. Healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":4.915}`). Web bundle sizes stable (main 154.99 kB + phaser 1,488.69 kB). `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile change required ‚Äî the new camera-controls module is part of `apps/web/dist` already copied into the runtime image.
- Lessons learned:
  - Pure-TS camera math (clampZoom, applyWheelZoom, applyPinchZoom, keyPanDelta, pointerDistance) lives in its own `camera-controls.ts` module so it stays out of `game-scene.ts`'s Phaser-importing module graph and is unit-testable under jsdom. Same pattern as TASK-019's tile-atlas helpers ‚Äî anything that needs test coverage in apps/web has to live outside any module Phaser-importing module's transitive closure, otherwise the test-runner's `getContext ‚Üí null` stub isn't enough and Phaser's WebGL/Canvas init cascades into the test environment.
  - The follow-target sprite from TASK-019 stays as the programmatic "jump-to" mechanism, but manual user input (drag, pinch, wheel, arrow keys) calls `cam.stopFollow()` so the user is always in control once they touch the camera. `setCameraFocus()` re-engages follow so the next programmatic recenter still glides ‚Äî this gives both APIs a clean coexistence without either fighting the other.
  - Cursor-anchored wheel zoom (the world point under the pointer stays under the pointer) makes the wheel feel native ‚Äî without it, zooming in zooms toward the screen centre and the player loses their bearing. The math is straightforward (compute world coord under pointer pre-zoom, set new zoom, re-pan to keep that world coord under pointer) and self-contained inside `handleWheel`.
  - Per-game camera memory persists in the zustand store (`cameraView: { scrollX, scrollY, zoom } | null`) rather than localStorage. Reset clears it so a new game starts at the default focus; persistence across browser reloads will fall out for free if/when EPIC-08's save system serialises the store. No new dependencies required.
- Notes: Seventeenth autonomous-run cycle. Streak=3 since PR #23 review checkpoint (TASK-018 ‚Üí TASK-019 ‚Üí TASK-020); two more consecutive successes to re-hit successThreshold=5.

### Run [2026-04-21 09:55]
- Task: TASK-021 ‚Äî Visibility model in core (unseen / seen / visible)
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/31 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: server=8, web=77, content=15, core=105 (was 78 ‚Äî +27 visibility tests covering type registry, construction, get/inBounds, reveal Chebyshev geometry + clipping + rejection, demoteVisibleToSeen idempotence + turn-loop re-reveal, toJSON/fromJSON round-trip + validation), shared=2
- Files changed: packages/core/src/visibility/visibility.ts (new), packages/core/src/visibility/visibility.test.ts (new), packages/core/src/visibility/index.ts (new), packages/core/src/index.ts, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 78 ‚Üí 105; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: false (4 consecutive successes since PR #23 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~31s, manifest list sha256:1e4d12357813466a3afe0f8b8f036875d31c855ffe8e231c19416fcd5fe1968a, image sha256:063f2745b9ea). The compose stack was recreated from scratch this cycle (network + db-data volume both created fresh ‚Äî the previous compose project had evidently been torn down between cycles; no impact since the db schema is empty pre-EPIC-09). docker-app-1 came up clean, healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":9.958}`). Web bundle sizes held steady (main 154.99 kB + phaser 1,488.69 kB). `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile change needed ‚Äî `packages/core/dist` already ships the new `visibility/` module via `tsc -b`.
- Lessons learned:
  - Visibility as a save-format-bound const-object keeps the wire format stable ‚Äî `{unseen | seen | visible}` are the string literals that land in serialized save JSON. Followed the same pattern as TileType: const object + derived union + `ALL_VISIBILITY_STATES` readonly array + `isVisibility` narrowing guard used cell-by-cell inside `fromJSON`. Any future rename becomes a save-version migration, not a refactor.
  - Split the turn-loop into two explicit ops instead of baking it into `reveal`: (a) `demoteVisibleToSeen()` ‚Äî every currently-visible cell drops to `seen`; (b) re-apply `reveal(pos, sight)` from each unit/colony. The turn manager (TASK-024) and the movement/colony-placement callers (TASK-026+) orchestrate this; the visibility module stays a pure primitive with no notion of "turn". This is the standard Civ-style fog-of-war recompute pattern and avoids the contribution-count bookkeeping that an incremental scheme would demand.
  - Chebyshev distance for the sight circle (square in screen space) ‚Äî matches the 8-neighbour semantics `GameMap.neighbours` already exposes, so a unit's `sight=1` radius exactly covers its immediate neighbours. Simpler than Euclidean, and the extra corner tiles at diagonal distance ‚àö2 are cheap narrative "you spotted something in the distance" territory.
  - Line-of-sight blockers (terrain that obstructs vision, e.g. fog banks, red-tide obscuring ships behind it) are deliberately deferred ‚Äî the task scope is the *model* (TASK-021), not the LoS algorithm. Adding blocker-aware flood fill now would entangle the primitive with TileType semantics before the movement/unit systems land.
- Notes: Twentieth autonomous-run cycle. Streak=4 since PR #23 review checkpoint (TASK-018 ‚Üí TASK-019 ‚Üí TASK-020 ‚Üí TASK-021); one more consecutive success to re-hit successThreshold=5 and arm `/autonomous-review`.

  - Split the fog into two modules ‚Äî `fog-overlay-state.ts` (pure TS, imports only @colonize/core, fully unit-testable under jsdom) and `fog-overlay.ts` (Phaser wrapper, untestable under jsdom per the "browser-only libraries under jsdom" note in CLAUDE.md). Mirrors the same separation already used for camera math (`camera-controls.ts` tested + `game-scene.ts` untested). All 17 new tests live in the pure module; the Phaser wrapper is verified at build-time via typecheck + ships unverified to Playwright territory, as CLAUDE.md mandates ("Phaser scene tests are hard; prefer logic-first tests").
  - Chose `RenderTexture.fill(color, alpha, x, y, w, h)` per tile inside a single RenderTexture GameObject over a `BitmapMask` on the terrain layer. The task brief said "single render-texture mask rather than per-tile sprites" ‚Äî the "single" part is satisfied (one overlay GameObject, O(W*H) fillRect calls per redraw, no sprites). Going the BitmapMask route would have forced the "seen" dimming into terrain-layer alpha, coupling the overlay's rendering to the terrain's blend stack. Keeping fog as a top-layer tinted texture lets "seen" be a simple alpha-0.5 black tint that composites cleanly on top of whatever the terrain layer draws (including the animated ocean).
  - Unseen‚Üíseen and unseen‚Üívisible animate over 400ms; demotions (visible‚Üíseen) and re-reveals of known terrain (seen‚Üívisible) snap instantly. The task text said "animated reveal when a tile transitions unseen‚Üíseen" ‚Äî only the *revelation* moment (first exposure to a tile) reads as a "reveal" to the player. Demotions happen as a whole-faction batch at turn end and would look noisy if each one faded. Re-reveals of already-seen terrain don't surprise the player with new information, so a fade is wasted motion. Kept the policy symmetric in the code (the `before === Visibility.Unseen` predicate in `FogOverlayState.sync`) so it's trivial to flip later if play-testing disagrees.
  - `GameSceneInitData.visibility` is optional. No existing caller passes it (the web UI currently only invokes `createGame()`, not `startGameScene()`), so the overlay is opt-in until the turn-advance / faction-bootstrap flows land. `GameScene.syncFogOverlay(visibility)` is exposed for that future wiring; for now it's a public hook with no caller, which keeps the scope of this PR to "the overlay exists and works when given a visibility model" rather than sweeping in the turn-loop integration.
  - `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` (set in tsconfig.base) forbids writing `{ foo: undefined }` into a type where `foo?` is declared. Tripped on `startGameScene`'s spread-options pattern; fixed by conditional object spread (`options.visibility ? { ...data, visibility } : data`) rather than passing the value through as-maybe-undefined. Worth remembering for any future task that threads optional fields through a config object.
  - Prettier's `--write` on new files is a must before `format:check` ‚Äî ran it up front this cycle and the check passed first try, no fix-cycle needed. Consistent with TASK-006/007/010 learning in Step 8 of the skill.
- Notes: Twenty-first autonomous-run cycle. Streak=5 since PR #23 review checkpoint ‚Äî `successThreshold` hit; `/autonomous-review` arms at Step 15 after the merge + deploy land.

- Review proposed: false (streak=1 since PR #33 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~31s, manifest list sha256:87b3d3e37871077d812e9cb29ebf6c415ece8aed8fe0a7a82be5f33398b1dcac, config sha256:b20a39ff5913b96f1171b9215926ec9cfa22634b35ac551414e0a586788ad6e8). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":5.495}`). Web bundle sizes steady (main 154.99 kB + phaser 1,491.69 kB). `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî the new `turn/` module ships in `packages/core/dist` via the existing `tsc -b` step.
- Lessons learned:
  - TurnPhase is save-format-bound ‚Äî serialized state round-trips `{turn, phase}` through JSON, so the phase identifiers (`start`, `player-action`, `ai`, `world-events`, `end`) are the wire format. Followed the same string-literal const-object pattern as TileType and Visibility: const object + derived union + `ALL_TURN_PHASES` readonly array + `isTurnPhase` narrowing guard used inside `fromJSON`. Renames become save-version migrations, not refactors.
  - Turn counter increments on the **End ‚Üí Start** transition rather than on phase 0 of the new turn. This means hooks registered on `exit:end` see the *old* turn number (the one that just finished) and hooks on `enter:start` see the *new* turn number ‚Äî the natural semantics for "end-of-turn cleanup" vs "start-of-turn setup". Documented and tested both.
  - Hooks are not serialized. `TurnManager.fromJSON` returns a fresh manager with empty hook buckets ‚Äî revived game state carries phase/turn only, and the loading code re-wires hooks from whatever systems need them (visibility demote, AI step, world events). Same separation-of-concerns as React component state vs event handlers: serializable state lives in the class, behaviour attaches at runtime. Added a test proving a revived manager's hooks are independent of the source's.
  - `advance()` snapshots the hook list before iteration (`[...hooks]`) so a hook that unsubscribes itself (or registers a sibling) mid-invocation doesn't mutate the iteration order. Cheap insurance ‚Äî the cost is one array copy per phase transition, which is negligible ‚Äî and it eliminates an entire class of order-dependent bugs that would only surface under a specific hook-registration pattern (e.g. "lazy one-shot" hooks that detach themselves on first fire).
  - Deliberately did NOT make `TurnManager` depend on a specific game-state shape. The hook context carries only `{turn, phase, event}` ‚Äî callers bridge to their own state in their closures. Alternatives considered: (a) generic `TurnManager<TState>` with state passed to hooks, (b) event-emitter pattern with a dedicated bus. Rejected (a) because the phase transitions are pure per CLAUDE.md's "`packages/core` is framework-free TS" rule and game state spans many modules; rejected (b) because the existing `apps/web/src/bus.ts` lives in the web app, not in core. Keeping TurnManager lean means upcoming TASK-025 (end-turn button ‚Üí advanceToNextTurn) and TASK-026 (unit movement-point regen on Start-enter) both just register a hook without having to satisfy a generic state type.
  - Included `advanceToNextTurn()` as a guard-bounded convenience wrapper. The guard (`PHASE_SEQUENCE.length + 1` iterations) protects against an accidental phase-sequence edit that would otherwise loop forever ‚Äî cheap safety net that makes any future phase-sequence mutation fail loudly at test time rather than hang.
- Notes: Twenty-second autonomous-run cycle. First task in EPIC-04 (turn engine). Streak=1 since PR #33 review checkpoint.

- Review proposed: false (streak=2 since PR #33 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~31s, manifest list sha256:78add1f3f9bbc7d4340c8699eb6989d5a89b39e502097809c80cb76a56492f7e, config sha256:3ad7379dc6d1735ca7cd24e024eb8e75739c7b78e6d8af74db6e089226b9e4f3). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":11.172}`). Web bundle sizes steady (main 157.90 kB + phaser 1,491.69 kB). `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî new `turn-controller.ts` module ships inside the existing `apps/web/dist` Vite bundle.
- Lessons learned:
  - TurnManager instance lives in `apps/web/src/game/turn-controller.ts` rather than the zustand store. Kept the manager out of the store because (a) zustand is for serialisable state snapshots and the manager carries hook closures that don't serialise, (b) React re-renders on every `set()`, so binding a mutable manager into the store would bait renders that shouldn't happen. Instead the controller owns the manager and *mirrors* phase + turn into the store via enter-hooks, so React components stay driven by plain store reads.
  - The microtask cadence in `endPlayerTurn()` (`manager.advance()` sync + `queueMicrotask(() => { ‚Ä¶four more advances‚Ä¶ })`) is deliberate. The first advance happens synchronously so the click's React state update and the AI-phase render paint in the same commit ‚Äî this is what makes the "AI thinking‚Ä¶" indicator actually flash. If all five advances ran synchronously the player would never see `phase === 'ai'` because React batches store updates within the click handler. Microtask gives React one commit at `phase='ai'` before the rest of the cycle closes.
  - Phase guard in `endPlayerTurn()` is implicit via `manager.phase !== TurnPhase.PlayerAction` ‚Äî no separate `pending` flag. Once the first advance fires, phase is 'ai', so any subsequent click (or programmatic call) during the microtask bails early. Removed the pending-flag approach in favour of this since the state machine already expresses the constraint; adding a parallel flag is redundant and drift-prone.
  - `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` bit on the `TurnPhase` re-export: couldn't write `import { TurnPhase } from '@colonize/core'` and use it both as type and value without aliasing, because `TurnPhase` is both a `const` object and a type alias (same name, different namespaces). Worked around by `import type { TurnPhase }` for the type + `TurnPhase as TurnPhaseEnum` for the value inside the store module. Kept the public API surface clean ‚Äî outside the store, code imports `{ TurnPhase }` normally and both meanings resolve.
  - Act warnings during tests turned out to come from the microtask advance running *outside* act ‚Äî `fireEvent.click` wraps the sync portion but not the scheduled microtask. Fixed by awaiting `waitFor` on the post-cycle state in every test that clicks. Silences all warnings and matches real user semantics ("the turn either completed or the test lied").
  - `AiThinkingIndicator` uses `role="status"` (polite ARIA live region) so screen readers announce "AI thinking‚Ä¶" when it appears without hijacking focus. Small a11y touch ‚Äî no cost, future-proofs for accessibility-audit tasks later in the roadmap.
- Notes: Twenty-third autonomous-run cycle. Second task in EPIC-04 (wiring TurnManager into HUD). Streak=2 since PR #33 review checkpoint.

- Review proposed: false (streak=3 since PR #33 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~31.5s, manifest list sha256:1be821aa363b8082233b4ed9573b7bb0333c0e889c83224a2a6a62880cfa011b, config sha256:dd9cb9c9ad07a257a27b4f96ee37ceb4b5a8b595f701944a6afe71b798b7cced). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":5.923}`). Web bundle sizes steady (main 157.90 kB + phaser 1,491.69 kB). `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî new `unit/` module ships in `packages/core/dist` via the existing `tsc -b` step.
- Lessons learned:
  - `UnitType` follows the save-format-bound string-literal const-object pattern (CLAUDE.md Tier 3 ‚Äî same shape as TileType, Visibility, TurnPhase). Kept the seed minimal (Scout, Settler) because TASK-027 is the dedicated task that appends ship classes (Sloop/Brig/Frigate/ShipOfTheLine/Privateer) with their own stats (hull, guns, crew capacity). Appending literals to the const object is additive and non-breaking ‚Äî no save-format migration required for TASK-027.
  - `FactionId` left as an opaque `string` brand in `packages/core` rather than pulled in from `@colonize/content`. Core must import nothing game-specific per the dependency-direction rule, and `@colonize/content`'s `PlayableFactionId` is a literal union that narrows a `string` cleanly at the app layer. This means the Unit class doesn't need to know which factions are playable ‚Äî the responsibility sits in content, and core stays reusable for AI or world-event units that aren't tied to the four MVP factions.
  - Stats kept to *just movement* in this task. STORY-14 mentions supplies and condition but the task description explicitly scopes to "id, faction, pos, type, stats. Movement points set at turn start per unit type. Deduct on move." Resisted the temptation to stub out supplies/condition because (a) CLAUDE.md Tier 1: "Only implement exactly what is requested", (b) adding optional fields now would force premature decisions about default values that future stat-balancing tasks will want to make, and (c) `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` means every added optional ripples through every constructor call site.
  - `resetMovement()` is a primitive the Unit exposes ‚Äî deliberately NOT wired to a `TurnManager` Start-enter hook in this PR. Wiring will come when a unit roster/collection exists (iterating all owned units at turn start). Keeping the primitive and the wiring separate lets the roster task (not yet on the board) own the iteration choice ‚Äî per-faction vs global, eager vs lazy, with or without blocked-unit skip logic.
  - `moveTo` spends movement *before* mutating position, so a RangeError from `spendMovement` leaves the unit's position unchanged. Covered by a dedicated test. The alternative (mutate-then-spend or wrap in try/catch) would either produce an illegal state on throw or silently swallow the invariant ‚Äî both worse. Ordering guarantees atomicity under exception without any explicit rollback code.
  - `UnitInit.movement` stays `number | undefined` via the optional-field pattern, but I threaded it through `fromJSON` with `data.movement` (required in `UnitJSON`, so never undefined at the call site). This avoids the `exactOptionalPropertyTypes` trap where `{ ...base, movement: maybeUndef }` would be rejected ‚Äî the JSON schema locks in a definite number, and only the `new Unit({...})` public-API constructor accepts omission. Test harness `makeScoutArgs` conditionally spreads the movement field to respect the same constraint.
- Notes: Twenty-fourth autonomous-run cycle. Third task in EPIC-04 (first task in STORY-14, units). Streak=3 since PR #33 review checkpoint.

Sourced names+descriptions from ¬ß9 of `lore/OTK.md` (the six canonical ships); each description is one sentence of `[ESTABLISHED]` flavour with a "Reserved as an OTK Legendary slot; not yet rebuilt" tail so any UI that shows them today reads as deliberate pre-MVP placeholder rather than missing data.

### Run [2026-04-21 15:10]
- Task: TASK-028 ‚Äî A* pathfinding with tile cost modifiers
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/38 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: core=179 (was 167 ‚Äî +12 in `pathfind.test.ts`: tileCost returns 1 for Ocean/RayonPassage/FataMorgana/FloatingCity, Island is Infinity regardless of flags, RedTide is Infinity unless `redTideImmunity` is set; findPath start==goal returns single-tile path with cost 0, straight-line 5√ó1 ocean row walks 4 steps at cost 4, 4√ó4 diagonal move 0,0 ‚Üí 3,3 takes 3 Chebyshev steps, 5√ó3 Red Tide wall forces a non-RedTide route for non-immune units, same wall spanning all rows lets an immune unit cut straight through at cost 4 (and the path actually includes a RedTide cell) while a non-immune unit gets null, Island wall with no gap returns null, impassable goal tile returns null, out-of-bounds start/goal each throw RangeError, 5√ó5 map with partial Island wall detours around it), content=29, web=108, shared=2, server=8
- Files changed: packages/core/src/map/pathfind.ts (new), packages/core/src/map/pathfind.test.ts (new), packages/core/src/map/index.ts, packages/core/src/index.ts, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 167 ‚Üí 179; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: true ‚Äî https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/39 (merged; 3 refinements landed: rules-vs-flavor split across core/content + exhaustive-switch save-format tripwire + publish-primitive-defer-wiring seam. Streak=5 since PR #33 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-023 ‚Üí TASK-024 ‚Üí TASK-025 ‚Üí TASK-026 ‚Üí TASK-027 ‚Üí TASK-028 ‚Äî reset to 0 after this review checkpoint)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~33.2s, manifest list sha256:b8de1f93bafe96415881679213458fb2f2229a16a7c69e4b79514b86901e0ce5, config sha256:ec78f5df68b1ccf3e79e65d3056d4b625ab2d1d6ec6bc5668c7801983c963693). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":6.182}`). Web bundle sizes steady (phaser chunk 1,491.69 kB). `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî new pathfind module ships via the existing `tsc -b` step.
- Lessons learned:
  - A* keyed on a packed `y * width + x` integer rather than a `Coord` object so the open-set MinHeap + closed-set maps avoid object identity pitfalls and can use `Map<number, number>` instead of a structural-equality-keyed container. Reconstruction unpacks the integer back to `{x, y}` at the end. This matches `GameMap`'s internal `indexOf` and sidesteps the "two different `{x:0, y:0}` objects don't compare equal" trap that na√Øve A* implementations fall into with a JS `Map<Coord, T>`.
  - Inlined a tiny MinHeap class in `pathfind.ts` rather than adding a dependency or a shared util. A* without a priority queue is O(n¬≤ log n) on a simple array sort, and the 100-ish LOC heap is the single standard implementation ‚Äî keeping it local keeps `@colonize/core` dep-free (zero runtime deps still) and puts the non-trivial arithmetic under the same test coverage as the pathfinder itself. Considered a sibling `min-heap.ts` module for future reuse, but per CLAUDE.md Tier 1 "don't design for hypothetical future requirements" ‚Äî the first other caller can extract it.
  - 8-connected neighbour set (matches `GameMap.neighbours()`) with a Chebyshev heuristic `max(|Œîx|, |Œîy|)` ‚Äî admissible and monotone on a uniform-cost 8-grid, so A* is guaranteed optimal. Switched *against* Manhattan (would overestimate for diagonals and break optimality on an 8-grid) and *against* Euclidean (admissible but slightly less informed than Chebyshev here since unit step on a diagonal also has cost 1, not ‚àö2). The heuristic choice is load-bearing for correctness, not just speed ‚Äî tests pin the total cost on the 4√ó4 diagonal (3) and 5√ó1 straight line (4) so a regression to the wrong heuristic would fail loudly.
  - `tileCost(type, flags)` exported alongside `findPath` so future callers (UI path-preview tooltips, move-range highlighters, AI cost estimates) can read per-tile cost without round-tripping through a pathfinder run. The switch is exhaustive over `TileType`; adding a new tile kind will surface as a TS compile error at the `switch`, which is the right tripwire for a save-format-bound enum.
  - Cost convention: entering a tile costs `tileCost(thatTile)` ‚Äî the start tile is free. Start==goal returns cost 0 and a single-element path. Goal tile impassable ‚Üí null (the unit can't *finish* on an Island or non-immune RedTide). Start tile impassable is allowed to proceed ‚Äî it's theoretically unreachable from legal game states, but forbidding it would make the function crash on already-corrupt saves instead of just routing away from the bad cell. The "only validate at boundaries" rule (CLAUDE.md Tier 1) says core helpers should trust internal inputs; the explicit OOB RangeError is the only boundary check.
  - `PathfindFlags` is the right seam for future modifiers (windward bonus, Kraken Talisman, scout terrain-ignoring) ‚Äî a single struct passed through instead of positional booleans. Added just `redTideImmunity` per the task description; expanding the interface later is additive and won't require changing the `findPath` signature. Named `redTideImmunity` rather than a more abstract `ignoreImpassableKinds: TileType[]` because the game-design language already talks about unit traits in named-immunity terms (per lore ¬ß9: OTK Kraken Talisman grants RedTide immunity), and a typed flags object catches typos at the call site.
- Notes: Twenty-sixth autonomous-run cycle. First task in STORY-15 (pathfinding + sailing rules). Streak=5 since PR #33 review checkpoint ‚Äî crosses threshold, review will be proposed in Step 15 after deploy completes.

- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~31.6s, manifest list sha256:072a680256fb1acf3a8c8abe478111815c531441f274ae0c9b90a0e9802cf12b, config sha256:4bed76205b98f4348f2ef7f8fcde1d6fe28175ab46c5b54c48b3fd2ddc98c007). Web bundle sizes steady (main 162.25 kB + phaser 1,494.84 kB). `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî new unit-rendering modules ship in `apps/web/dist` via the existing Vite build step.
- Lessons learned:
  - Pre-art-epic visuals chose Phaser primitives (Rectangle / Circle / Container with Text label) over a sprite-atlas extension. Reasons: zero asset-pipeline pressure (no new `unit_*.png` source files, no atlas regen, no Capacitor sync churn), one PR per visual surface, and an obvious swap-point later ‚Äî replace `createUnitContainer` body with `this.add.sprite(x, y, atlas, frameForUnit(type))` once the art epic ships. Mirrors the inline-SVG heraldry pattern in CLAUDE.md ("Heraldic / crest visuals are inline SVG until the art epic ships"). Per-faction tint as a 24-bit RGB integer matches Phaser's `setFillStyle(color)` argument shape directly ‚Äî no string‚Üíhex parsing at the draw call.
  - Two pure siblings landed before the scene wiring: `unit-visuals.ts` owns the per-UnitType visual spec + faction-color table, `unit-input.ts` owns the world‚Üítile + roster-pick logic. Phaser is in neither's transitive closure, so both are unit-tested in jsdom without flaking on canvas-feature-detection probes. The scene file (`game-scene.ts`) is wiring-only and remains untested per CLAUDE.md's pure-sibling rule. This is the same split as `camera-controls` (tested) + `game-scene` (untested) and `tile-atlas` (tested) + scene-side rendering.
  - Stored unit roster as `readonly UnitJSON[]` (plain data) in zustand rather than `Unit` class instances. Rationale: zustand state must be cloneable for devtools/time-travel and `Unit`'s private mutable fields don't survive the round-trip; the eventual roster owner (a future task) reconstitutes `Unit` instances on demand for game logic, and renderers + HUD only need the JSON shape. Saves a PR-wide constraint that the store would otherwise inherit from `Unit`'s mutability.
  - Tap-vs-drag disambiguation uses a screen-pixel displacement threshold (6 px) measured between `pointerdown` and `pointerup`, *not* a Phaser pointer-input on each unit sprite. Two reasons: (a) the existing camera drag handler is already on the global pointer stream ‚Äî putting per-sprite hit detection on Container would require enabling input on every unit and dealing with the drag handler stealing the gesture mid-stroke; (b) clicking *empty water* must clear selection, which a per-sprite handler can't observe. The pure-sibling `pickUnitIdAtTile(tile, units)` then resolves the tile to a unit id (or null) without the scene needing to maintain a parallel sprite‚Üíid index.
  - Selection-id `===` short-circuit in `handleMapClick` (`if (previous === unitId) return`) prevents emitting `unit:selected` when the player taps the already-selected tile ‚Äî both saves a no-op store update and matches the "single, intentional event per real selection change" semantic that listeners (HUD, future audio cue, future move-range overlay) want. Same shape as the `setPhase` no-op short-circuits in `turn-controller.ts`.
  - `selectionRing` is a single `Phaser.GameObjects.Graphics` redrawn on selection change, not a per-unit ring child of each container. Cheaper (one draw vs N invisible rings), correct depth ordering (60 between units at 50 and fog at 100), and the `clear ‚Üí lineStyle ‚Üí strokeCircle ‚Üí setVisible(true)` flow is small enough to sit inline in the scene without a sibling. The body/ring/depth constants live in `unit-visuals.ts` (`UNIT_BODY_SCALE`, `SELECTION_RING_SCALE`, `SELECTION_RING_COLOR`) so the scene's wiring stays free of magic numbers.
  - Subscriptions to the zustand store (`useGameStore.subscribe`) are torn down on `Phaser.Scenes.Events.SHUTDOWN` *and* `DESTROY` ‚Äî both fire under different lifecycle paths (scene swap vs game teardown) and skipping either leaks listeners into stale game instances on hot reload + repeated menu‚Üígame‚Üímenu loops. Same `events.once` pattern that the fog overlay would benefit from once we add a "back to menu" path.
- Notes: Twenty-seventh autonomous-run cycle. First task in STORY-16 (unit interaction in GameScene) ‚Äî opens up TASK-031 (click-to-move) + TASK-032 (rumour-tile entity) which both depend on TASK-030's selection event. Streak=1 since PR #39 review checkpoint.

### Run [2026-04-21 17:17]
- Task: TASK-015 ‚Äî Audio manager with SFX + BGM buses
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/41 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: web=152 (was 137 ‚Äî +15 in `audio-state.test.ts`: createAudioState defaults/clamping/new-object-on-mutation, withPrimed idempotence, withMuted/withVolume same-ref identity when value matches, withCurrentBgm tracks key + nulls, effectiveVolume returns 0 when not-primed / muted / else per-bus, canPlay reflection, planBgmTransition start/noop/switch/stop/null-noop across full 2√ó2 matrix), content=37 (was 29 ‚Äî +8 in `audio.test.ts`: AUDIO_STEMS has sfx+bgm, unique-keys invariant, positive-duration invariant, bgm stems default loop=true, isAudioStemKey narrowing, getAudioStem lookup + unknown-key throw, audioStemUrl composition), core=179, shared=2, server=8
- Files changed: apps/web/src/game/audio-state.ts (new), apps/web/src/game/audio-state.test.ts (new), apps/web/src/game/audio-manager.ts (new), apps/web/src/game/boot-scene.ts, apps/web/src/game/create-game.ts, apps/web/src/game/index.ts, packages/content/src/audio.ts (new), packages/content/src/audio.test.ts (new), packages/content/src/index.ts, packages/content/scripts/generate-placeholder-audio.mjs (new), packages/content/package.json, apps/web/scripts/prepare-assets.mjs, .gitignore, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (web 137 ‚Üí 152, content 29 ‚Üí 37; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=2 since PR #39 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:87a26af82bdc64234c89d88bc51f398e03b210e73d5aff7a698dde6de4d58786, config sha256:427f1a49f97314f019b488b82e771ffd4bcf7e69117dc8a34bdbe8898d3b348f). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":5.422}`). `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî new audio manifest + generator ship in the existing `tsc -b` + `node scripts/prepare-assets.mjs` build steps; silent WAVs are generated inside the builder stage and copied into `apps/web/dist` by Vite's static-assets copy.
- Lessons learned:
  - Third canonical pure-sibling / Phaser-wrapper split lands: `audio-state.ts` (tested, no Phaser in closure) owns the decision logic and `audio-manager.ts` (untested) does the Phaser.Sound wiring. Joins `camera-controls`/`game-scene`, `tile-atlas`/`game-scene`, `fog-overlay-state`/`fog-overlay`, `unit-visuals+unit-input`/`game-scene` ‚Äî pattern is now the unambiguous default for new Phaser code, not an exception. The state module exposes transition planners (`planBgmTransition` emitting `noop` / `start` / `stop` / `switch`) rather than raw `playBgm` logic, so the wrapper becomes "apply the transition to the sound manager" ‚Äî one `switch` with no hidden conditions. Tests pin every transition quadrant (5 cases: null‚Üínull, null‚Üíkey, key‚Üísame, key‚Üídifferent, key‚Üínull) independently of any Phaser mock.
  - iOS audio priming rides on Phaser's own `WebAudioSoundManager.unlock()` rather than a bespoke `document.addEventListener('touchstart', ‚Ä¶, {once:true})` bridge from React. Phaser already attaches unlock listeners to `document.body` for `touchstart/touchend/click/keydown` inside its sound-manager constructor; AudioManager just does `sound.once('unlocked', ‚Ä¶)` to flip its own `primed` flag and kick off any BGM that was queued before the unlock. Considered adding a React-side primer in `App.tsx` on the "New Game" click, but that would duplicate Phaser's listener + force a bridge (window global / zustand slice leaking Phaser types / bus event) for zero correctness gain ‚Äî Phaser's listener fires for every body-level gesture, including the React button clicks. Same-lifecycle trick: the `defer BGM until primed` queue means the call site (MainMenuScene etc.) doesn't need to know whether audio is locked; it just calls `playBgm(key)` and the manager handles the gate. `currentBgm` is tracked in the pure state even when `bgmInstance` is null so the state model stays queue-aware without leaking Phaser types.
  - Source/packed/served triad extended from the atlas pipeline to audio: `packages/content/src/audio.ts` is the TS manifest (source of truth for runtime consumers), `packages/content/scripts/generate-placeholder-audio.mjs` renders 8-bit mono 8kHz silent WAVs into `packages/content/audio-out/` (gitignored), and `apps/web/scripts/prepare-assets.mjs` copies them to `apps/web/public/audio/` (gitignored) where Vite serves them at `/audio/*`. The generator uses a minimal 44-byte PCM WAV header (computed in pure Node `Buffer` ‚Äî no ffmpeg/web-audio dep) and a mid-scale byte `0x80` fill so the file is a valid silent audio payload every browser decoder accepts. Chose WAV over OGG/MP3 for the placeholder because every decoder supports PCM, the files are tiny at low sample rates (ui-click.wav = 684 bytes at 80ms 8kHz, bgm-menu.wav = 16044 bytes at 2s), and the generator is deterministic (no codec library to pin across CI runs). Swap-point later is `generate-placeholder-audio.mjs` ‚Üí a real asset packer when the music epic lands; the runtime consumer code doesn't change.
  - The audio-manager module flipped to `import type Phaser from 'phaser'` ‚Äî every Phaser reference in the file is a type (BaseSoundManager, BaseSound, LoaderPlugin), no runtime. ESLint's `consistent-type-imports` flagged it; accepting the flag keeps Phaser out of the module's runtime graph, which matters because even with dynamic-import isolation in `GameCanvas.tsx`, a non-type `import Phaser` in audio-manager.ts would pull the whole library into any future module that statically re-exports from `./game/index.ts` (the barrel already re-exports AudioManager). The canvas mount guard + pure-sibling pattern are the only reliable Phaser-in-jsdom protection ‚Äî this makes audio-manager.ts itself a legitimate non-Phaser-runtime module, while still being the one place that ties bound Phaser runtime values (the actual `game.sound` instance) to the state machine.
  - `AudioManager` is attached to the Phaser.Game via `game.registry.set(AUDIO_REGISTRY_KEY, audio)` rather than being returned from `createGame()` as a tuple. The registry is already the canonical cross-scene DataManager Phaser provides, so any scene reaches the manager via `this.registry.get(AUDIO_REGISTRY_KEY)` without a fresh constructor arg per scene; the tuple approach would either couple `GameCanvas.tsx` (the only external caller) to an interface it has no use for, or require threading the manager through `scene.init(data)` calls. Destruction rides on Phaser's `Phaser.Core.Events.DESTROY` event via `game.events.once(...)` so the AudioManager's queued BGM is stopped synchronously with the game teardown ‚Äî no leaked `Phaser.Sound.BaseSound` instances on hot reload.
  - `canPlay` / `effectiveVolume` treat "not primed" as volume=0 even when the user's configured volume is > 0. Meaning: a pre-unlock `play(key)` call is a silent no-op (returns without calling `sound.play`) rather than a queued-for-later play. Rationale: SFX are transient gestures (UI click, weapon fire) ‚Äî once the moment has passed, replaying the click 3 seconds later when the unlock finally fires is more jarring than simply dropping it. BGM is different: the `currentBgm` field in the state explicitly queues the track identity so the `unlocked` listener can start playback when ready. The asymmetric policy (drop SFX, queue BGM) is encoded once in `applyBgm` (start/switch only emit startBgmNow if primed) and the `play()` method's early return. If a future use case needs queued SFX, it becomes a new state field, not a wrapper-level change.
- Notes: Twenty-eighth autonomous-run cycle. First task in STORY-08 ("Audio hooks" ‚Äî Phaser audio manager through SFX/BGM buses + iOS prime tap + mood-driven BGM stems). Manager exists but no call sites consume it yet; follow-up tasks add per-scene BGM wiring and SFX on specific actions (unit select, end turn, combat). Streak=2 since PR #39 review checkpoint.

### Run [2026-04-21 18:23]
- Task: TASK-031 ‚Äî Click-to-move with path preview + animation
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/42 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: web=177 (was 152 ‚Äî +9 `path-preview.test.ts` covering full-path affordability, step-by-step budget truncation, origin-only output when budget=0, impassable-step short-circuit, RedTide-immunity flag passthrough, empty/single-tile input edge cases, and findPath‚Üítruncate end-to-end; +9 `move-intent.test.ts` covering first-click select, switch-selection, re-click-selected ‚Üí cancel-proposal (with or without pending), empty-water-no-selection ‚Üí none, empty-water-with-selection ‚Üí propose, re-propose on different tile, commit on same tile as proposal goal, re-propose when stale proposal belongs to a different unit; +7 `store/game.test.ts` covering `proposedMove` initial-null, set/clear, cleared on selection-change-to-different-unit, preserved on same-unit re-select, `commitMove` updates position+movement and clears proposal, `commitMove` clamps movement to zero (never negative), `reset` drops `proposedMove`), core=179, content=37, shared=2, server=8
- Files changed: apps/web/src/game/game-scene.ts, apps/web/src/game/move-intent.ts (new), apps/web/src/game/move-intent.test.ts (new), apps/web/src/game/path-preview.ts (new), apps/web/src/game/path-preview.test.ts (new), apps/web/src/store/game.ts, apps/web/src/store/game.test.ts, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (web 152 ‚Üí 177; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=3 since PR #39 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~32.1s, manifest list sha256:10719014c463f2839dea4b31af381a57670ce9e1cf7f625f45b0283e8695997b, config sha256:237cff37c5ee8b09cee5e19d5020bce6837d59cd0e96e8abd4a0ae986c385cb7). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":5.979}`). Web bundle sizes steady (main 162.83 kB + phaser 1,503.13 kB). `colonize:previous` tag preserved (sha256:87a26af82bdc64234c89d88bc51f398e03b210e73d5aff7a698dde6de4d58786) for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî new path-preview + move-intent modules + GameScene + store additions ship in `apps/web/dist` via the existing Vite build step.
- Lessons learned:
  - Two new pure-sibling modules land this cycle ‚Äî `path-preview.ts` (budget-aware path truncation) and `move-intent.ts` (click ‚Üí intent state machine) ‚Äî joining the lineage `camera-controls`, `tile-atlas`, `fog-overlay-state`, `unit-visuals`/`unit-input`, and `audio-state`. The split keeps game-scene.ts (untested per CLAUDE.md's pure-sibling rule) thin and lets every branching decision in the click-to-move flow have a vitest assertion under jsdom without mounting Phaser. The click intent is modelled as a discriminated union (`select` / `cancel-proposal` / `propose` / `commit` / `none`) so GameScene's `handleMapClick` is a single `switch` dispatcher ‚Äî no nested `if` chains, no hidden fallthrough. Same readability win as `planBgmTransition` in TASK-015's audio-state.ts.
  - `ProposedMove` stores the *full* pathfinder path plus a `reachable: number` index into it (rather than just the affordable prefix). This lets the preview layer render beyond-reach tiles as faded dots ‚Äî giving the player a read on the route's total length even when most of it lies past this turn's movement budget ‚Äî without a second pathfinder run at commit time. The commit path is a simple `path.slice(0, reachable + 1)` and the cost field stores only the affordable-prefix cost (what `commitMove` actually deducts), matching TASK-026's `Unit.spendMovement` semantics. Considered storing just the truncated path + a separate "stretch goal" slice, but the single-array-plus-index form is one fewer field and survives serialization cleanly when a future task saves proposals across reload.
  - Click-to-move semantics changed the "click empty water" branch from TASK-030. Previously (with no move system) clicking empty water when a unit was selected cleared the selection; that turned into a bug for move UX (the intuitive gesture has to become "propose path"). New semantics: click unit A = select A (clears any proposal); click selected A = cancel-proposal (no-op when none pending, so clicking an already-selected unit twice is idempotent); click empty water with no selection = none; click empty water with selection and no proposal = propose; click empty water with selection and proposal-points-elsewhere = re-propose; click empty water with selection and proposal-points-here = commit. No test regression because no existing test asserted the old "click water to deselect" behavior ‚Äî all selection tests drove the store directly. Deselect is now implicit via "select a different unit", which matches the 4X convention and would have been the intended UX anyway.
  - Store-level invariant: `setSelectedUnit` clears `proposedMove` whenever the selection changes to a *different* unitId, but preserves it when the same id is re-set. Keeps the state machine tight: every path-preview the player sees belongs to the currently-selected unit, and clicking the same unit again doesn't destroy an in-flight plan. The action inspects the prior selectedUnitId inside the `set((state) => ‚Ä¶)` callback so the invariant is enforced atomically with the selection change ‚Äî no race window where a listener could observe the new selection with the old proposal still attached. Same shape as `commitMove` which also clears `proposedMove` atomically with the unit update.
  - Sprite tween uses recursive per-step `this.tweens.add({ targets: container, x, y, duration: MOVE_STEP_MS, onComplete: tweenNext(i+1) })` rather than a Phaser tween *timeline* or *chain*. Reasons: (a) the chain API shape has shifted between Phaser 3.60 and 3.88 ‚Äî `tweens.chain()` + `tweens.timeline()` deprecations have burned upgrade cycles before; (b) the recursive form is 10 LOC and passes the commit semantics test (tween completes ‚Üí store updates ‚Üí camera follows) without special-casing the first/last waypoint; (c) waypoint count is bounded by max Sloop baseMovement (= 4), so the recursion depth is trivially small. An `isMoving` scene-level flag gates further map clicks during flight so rapid double-confirm clicks can't stack moves on a mid-tween sprite (which would race the store commit that lands at tween end). Selection ring hides during flight because it's drawn at an absolute world position (not a child of the moving container) ‚Äî redrawing it per frame via tween `onUpdate` would add a graphics-clear-plus-strokeCircle on every frame; the existing `state.units` subscription redraws it once at the endpoint, which is the cheap right answer.
  - Camera follow on commit calls `setCameraFocus(final.x, final.y)` only after the tween completes ‚Äî not during. Earlier drafts threaded the camera into the per-waypoint `onUpdate`, but Phaser's `startFollow` is itself smoothing (`lerp=0.1`) and layering two independent smoothers creates a sluggish, laggy feel. The simpler "snap the follow target to the destination at tween end" gives one smooth glide that arrives a beat after the sprite ‚Äî which reads as the camera *tracking* the unit rather than racing ahead. Works for both on-screen and off-screen destinations; no bounds check needed because `setCameraFocus` already clamps to map bounds.
  - Unit-movement flags (PathfindFlags) are passed as `{}` at call sites for TASK-031 ‚Äî the Unit class doesn't yet own the `redTideImmunity` trait and this task's scope is path preview + motion, not unit-trait modelling. `truncatePathToBudget` and `proposeMove` both accept a `flags` parameter though (and the truncator threads it into `tileCost` calls), so when the OTK Kraken Talisman / RedTide-immunity trait lands on Unit (per lore ¬ß9), wiring it through is a one-field edit at the scene's `findPath` + `truncatePathResult` call sites. Avoids rework when that trait gets added ‚Äî the seam is already in place.
  - `pickUnitIdAtTile` in `unit-input.ts` is now unused by GameScene (move-intent.ts defines its own `pickUnitAtTile` that returns the full UnitJSON so the intent decision can read `clickedUnit.id` + later attributes in a single lookup). Left the TASK-030 helper in place with its tests rather than churning ‚Äî the two functions serve different return shapes and a follow-up task that needs the id-only form (e.g. a right-click ‚Üí hover tooltip that never reads unit stats) can call it directly. CLAUDE.md's "Only implement exactly what is requested" rule pushes away from over-eager cleanup; both helpers are tested, both stay.
- Notes: Twenty-ninth autonomous-run cycle. Second task in STORY-16 (unit interaction in GameScene). TASK-031 closes the "propose + commit + animate" loop that TASK-030 opened with click-to-select; the next natural TASK-032 (rumour-tile entity) unblocks once this lands. Streak=3 since PR #39 review checkpoint.
