- Lessons learned:
  - RumourTile is a *sibling entity keyed by position*, not a new `TileType` variant. The task description ("RumourTile associated with a map position ‚Ä¶ sprinkles them in unexplored regions") permits either reading, but making it a TileType would (a) force a new branch in the `pathfind.ts` exhaustive switch and every future rule-by-tile consumer, and (b) collapse tile-base (Ocean / FataMorgana / etc.) with a consumable overlay, meaning a resolved rumour would have to *rewrite* the underlying biome back to Ocean to preserve walkability. The separate-entity shape lets a rumour sit *atop* any tile (all current placements are Ocean, but the door is open for FataMorgana / RedTide rumours later) and lets `resolved` flip without touching the map grid or reopening save-format migrations. Generator returns `GeneratedMap.rumours: readonly RumourTile[]` alongside `factionStarts` ‚Äî both are "positioned entities discovered at generation time" and follow the same seeded-deterministic contract.
  - `RumourOutcome` is a discriminated union (`{ type: 'gold'; amount }` / `{ type: 'salvage'; amount }` / `{ type: 'nothing' }` / `{ type: 'encounter' }`) rather than a class hierarchy or a record per kind. Choice matches the string-literal const-object pattern used for TileType / UnitType / ResourceType ‚Äî type values are the wire format, so they appear verbatim in any save JSON that records consumed-rumour history later. `rollOutcome(kind, rng)` is written as a `switch (kind)` with no `default` case, so the moment a 5th RumourKind is added (e.g. `Siren` for eldritch seduction), TypeScript surfaces the missing case at build time rather than letting an `unknown` kind fall through silently. Same exhaustive-switch discipline as `tileCost` in `pathfind.ts`.
  - `RumourTile.resolve()` is a single-shot primitive: the second call throws. Considered returning a "nothing" outcome on re-resolve instead, but that would silently paper over a call-site bug (something is resolving a consumed rumour) rather than surfacing it. The caller can check `tile.resolved` before the call if the gesture is uncertain (right-click hover tooltip, preview modal). This also keeps the state machine tight for save-format purposes ‚Äî `resolved` is a boolean, not a counter, and `toJSON()` carries it through so a reloaded game can't re-award the outcome by re-resolving. Per CLAUDE.md's "ship the primitive, leave orchestration to the task that owns the collection" rule (TASK-024 / TASK-026 lineage), the Unit class deliberately does NOT gain a `resolveRumourAt(position)` hook this task ‚Äî that wiring belongs to the task that owns the rumour-by-position lookup (likely TASK-033, the outcome table + UI reveal modal). The primitive exposes the verb; the orchestrator binds it to units and tiles and turn flow.
  - Rumour placement in the generator enforces a Chebyshev keep-out of 3 cells around every faction start, not Manhattan. Chebyshev (`max(|dx|,|dy|)`) matches the Phaser 8-neighbour movement model used by pathfind.ts's `NEIGHBOUR_OFFSETS` ‚Äî "3 squares away" in the player's mental model is a 7√ó7 box centered on the start, not a diamond. Using Manhattan would excluded tiles 3 cells diagonal while *allowing* tiles 3 cells north (which are 3 movement-turns away diagonally but only 3 N/S steps on the grid), which is lopsided. A magic-number constant `RUMOUR_START_KEEP_OUT = 3` lives at the top of `generate.ts` alongside `RUMOUR_MIN_COUNT` / `RUMOUR_MAX_COUNT` so the tuning knobs are visible together. Fog-of-war isn't modelled per-position yet (TASK-022's fog overlay state is map-wide); "unexplored regions" is interpreted pragmatically as "not adjacent to a faction's starting colony".
  - Rumour-kind selection uses `ALL_RUMOUR_KINDS[Math.floor(rng() * length)]` rather than cycling through kinds deterministically. Random selection on a seeded rng keeps determinism (same seed ‚Üí same kind distribution) while producing natural-feeling variety ‚Äî some maps get three Treasures and zero Mirages, others get a mix. Cycling (e.g. `placed.length % kinds.length`) would guarantee every 4-rumour map has exactly one of each kind, which is predictable in a way that reads as *generated* rather than *discovered*. Tests assert every kind is a known `RumourKind` rather than pinning a specific kind-per-seed sequence, so small changes to rng consumption order don't cascade into test failures.
  - Rumour ids are `rumour-0`, `rumour-1`, ... (zero-indexed, per-map) ‚Äî deliberately not globally unique or UUID-shaped. Matches the `Unit.id` convention where ids live in a single-faction-game scope and survive save/reload (`RumourTile.fromJSON` takes the id verbatim). A future multi-map or multi-save story can prefix them (`map-<seed>:rumour-<idx>`) via a migration if conflicts ever arise; for now they're unique within a `GeneratedMap` and survive JSON round-trip. Same pragmatic-id shape as `faction-1` / `f-otk` elsewhere in the codebase.
- Notes: Thirtieth autonomous-run cycle. First task in STORY-17 (rumour tiles). TASK-033 (rumour outcome table + UI reveal modal) is the natural follow-up ‚Äî it owns the unit-on-entry ‚Üí `RumourTile.resolve()` wiring that this task deliberately left un-bound. Streak=4 since PR #39 review checkpoint (threshold=5, so next successful run triggers /autonomous-review).

- Task: TASK-016 ‚Äî Pause overlay (React) + resume

- Test counts: web=200 (was 177 ‚Äî +23: 9 `pause/PauseOverlay.test.tsx` covering root 4-option render, mount‚Üípause / unmount‚Üíresume bus emits, Resume returns to `screen='game'`, Quit-to-Menu resets store + returns to `'menu'`, Save status message, Settings sub-view open+back round-trip, slider seeds from store defaults (50% bgm / 80% sfx), slider writes normalise to [0,1], mute toggle round-trip; +6 `App.test.tsx` pause suite covering HUD-behind-overlay co-mount, Esc `game‚Üípause`, Esc `pause‚Üígame`, Esc no-op from menu, HUD hamburger opens pause, App-level bus pause/resume event ordering around Esc toggle; +1 `Hud.test.tsx` MenuButton click routes to `screen='pause'`; +7 `store/game.test.ts` settings suite covering default audio volumes mirroring audio-state.ts, per-bus writes (sfx vs bgm), clamp into [0,1], NaN‚Üí0 rejection, mute toggle, reset restores defaults), core=224, content=37, shared=2, server=8

- Review proposed: true ‚Äî https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/45 (auto-merge enabled; 2 refinements drafted: bus contract + React-side listener location, terminal-vs-overlay screen sub-shapes. Streak=5 since PR #39 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-030 ‚Üí TASK-015 ‚Üí TASK-031 ‚Üí TASK-032 ‚Üí TASK-016 ‚Äî will reset to 0 once PR #45 merges)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:fa6b4a752d5a33a61ea67c17891d10215c7fb06b49b54af302310306d61f3966, config sha256:b303a98af43fb9e8a5b3d545f63695ad9228b35a863fcf41649cc0effa88a781). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health (`{"ok":true,"version":"0.0.0","uptime":5.745}`). `colonize:previous` tag preserved (sha256:97ba71645855) for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî pause overlay ships as part of the existing `apps/web/dist` build.
- Lessons learned:
  - Pause is modelled as a *screen literal* (`'pause'` added to the `Screen` union in `apps/web/src/store/game.ts`) per the CLAUDE.md routing convention that names `'pause'` as a future screen, not as a separate `paused: boolean` slice. Trick: `App.tsx` renders the same `<GameCanvas />` + `<Hud />` children for both `'game'` and `'pause'`, adding `<PauseOverlay />` on top only when `'pause'`. This keeps the Phaser game mounted (React does not unmount the canvas), so `scene.pause()` / `.resume()` drive the *existing* scene instance rather than constructing a fresh one. Had I used a separate `paused` boolean it would have stayed orthogonal to screen routing but duplicated state ‚Äî two sources of truth for "is pause visible". The single-source union keeps the App dispatcher symmetric with the `colony` / `codex` screens that follow the same "stay mounted, overlay on top" pattern.
  - React‚ÜîPhaser pause handshake is done via the bus (`'game:pause'` / `'game:resume'` added to `GameEvents` in `packages/shared/src/index.ts`), not by exposing the Phaser game instance. Emits happen on `PauseOverlay` mount/unmount so every exit path ‚Äî Esc, Resume button, Quit-to-Menu button, HUD hamburger, parent unmount during HMR ‚Äî goes through the same two bus events without needing each handler to remember. The listener lives in `GameCanvas.useEffect` where the game instance is in scope: `bus.on('game:pause', () => gameInstance?.scene.pause(SCENE_KEYS.game))`. This keeps React ignorant of Phaser's lifecycle and keeps Phaser-integrating code confined to one file. Considered emitting from the Esc handler in `App.tsx` directly, but that would force *every* new pause-exit path (mobile swipe? gamepad button?) to re-emit ‚Äî the component-lifecycle approach is idempotent.
  - Settings state lives in zustand rather than on the Phaser audio registry so it's readable from React tests without importing Phaser. The store mirrors `audio-state.ts`'s `DEFAULTS` (sfx 0.8, bgm 0.5, muted false) as a duplicated constant; this is a knowing duplication across the packages/content vs core split-spirit (like TASK-027's `baseMovement` duplication), the alternative being a circular import loop between the Phaser-integrating `audio-manager.ts` and a React component tree. A later task can bind the two by subscribing from `create-game.ts` to `useGameStore.subscribe` and calling `audio.setVolume(bus, value)` ‚Äî deliberately *not* wired here per CLAUDE.md's "ship the primitive, leave orchestration to the task that owns the collection" (TASK-024 / TASK-026 / TASK-032 lineage). The Settings UI exposes the verb (slider ‚Üí setAudioVolume); a future wiring task binds it to the Phaser audio output. Tests pin the zustand contract; Phaser-side propagation is a follow-up.
  - `Save` button is a deliberate stub. The task description lists Save as one of four options; the minimal implementation renders the button and shows a `Saved (stub)` status line via an `aria-live="polite"` region. Real serialisation comes from a future task that wires `packages/core`'s `serialize/deserialize` into a localStorage (or server-side) sink. Resisting the urge to smuggle a localStorage stub in today ‚Äî per CLAUDE.md's "Only implement exactly what is requested" rule, the save pipeline is out of scope, and a fake dump would mislead playtesters into thinking state is durable. The button is present + clickable + testable today; the sink lands with the save-system story.
  - Esc handling is a *document-level* `keydown` listener in `App.tsx`'s useEffect, not a Phaser `Phaser.Input.Keyboard.KeyCodes.ESC` handler inside `GameScene`. Reason: the pause overlay is React DOM, not a Phaser Scene, and the React tree owns screen routing. Attaching Esc at the document level means focus-on-canvas still fires the handler (React doesn't need focus; the listener is a global capture on `document`) AND keeps the pause-trigger logic co-located with the screen-switching code it depends on. `event.preventDefault()` runs only when the key actually triggers a transition (`'game'` ‚Üî `'pause'`), so Esc on menu / faction-select falls through to whatever future handlers those screens install.
  - HUD `topRight` slot flips from "single child" to "flex-column stack" to host the new hamburger button above the resource bar. Not a separate slot ‚Äî trying `.topRightCorner` + `.topRight` as sibling absolute boxes ran into the "HUD overlays stay click-through where empty" convention twice over (each new slot needs the CSS-module `pointer-events` dance). A single slot with column flex keeps the CSS conventions minimal: the outer `.hud > *` ‚Üí `pointer-events: auto` rule still applies, and the hamburger + resources live in a single absolutely-positioned column. Future HUD additions on the same side stack without new slots.
- Notes: Thirty-first autonomous-run cycle. First task in STORY-06 (pause/resume flow). TASK-077 (Codex viewer) and TASK-014 (Settings screen from main menu) are the natural follow-ups that extend the overlay primitive to more UI surfaces. Streak=5 since PR #39 review checkpoint (threshold=5) ‚Äî next step fires /autonomous-review.

- Test counts: core=240 (was 224 ‚Äî +16 in `rumour.test.ts`: 4 `RumourOutcomeCategory` shape/narrowing/kind-mapping, 1 outcomeCategory getter on RumourTile, 3 resolve() per-category outcomes covering range invariants, 3 LegendaryWreck faction branch (OTK blueprint / non-OTK salvage / no-faction salvage), 1 KrakenShrine reputation range, 1 FataMorganaMirage variant shape, 1 Mirage RNG-thirds partition, 1 determinism under faction, 1 rejects non-function rng with the new signature ‚Äî old `gold/salvage/nothing/encounter` outcome shape replaced in place, no test count regression), content=42 (was 37 ‚Äî +5 in `rumour-outcomes.test.ts`: coverage of all four categories, non-empty title/flavour/rewardLabel/valid register invariant, OTK-only `otkFlavour` field constrained to LegendaryWreck, getRumourOutcomeFlavour hit + unknown-category throw), web=210 (was 200 ‚Äî +10 in `RumourRevealModal.test.tsx`: null-when-no-outcome, ArchiveCache title/flavour/reward render, LegendaryWreck OTK-blueprint branch shows Kraken-colours flavour + blueprint reward, LegendaryWreck non-OTK salvage branch shows default flavour + salvage reward, LegendaryWreck salvage-for-OTK still shows default flavour, KrakenShrine reputation reward, 3 FataMorganaMirage variant copies via it.each, Claim click dismisses), shared=2, server=8
- Files changed: packages/core/src/rumour/rumour.ts, packages/core/src/rumour/rumour.test.ts, packages/core/src/rumour/index.ts, packages/core/src/index.ts, packages/content/src/rumour-outcomes.ts (new), packages/content/src/rumour-outcomes.test.ts (new), packages/content/src/index.ts, apps/web/src/store/game.ts, apps/web/src/hud/RumourRevealModal.tsx (new), apps/web/src/hud/RumourRevealModal.module.css (new), apps/web/src/hud/RumourRevealModal.test.tsx (new), apps/web/src/App.tsx, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 224 ‚Üí 240, content 37 ‚Üí 42, web 200 ‚Üí 210; shared/server steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=1 since PR #45 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~32.8s, manifest list sha256:7d1a258a54399c349124b3de4bc6d731ac1c24f50a3403b95f9470468c22b1cc, config sha256:b9cb73382e5f2b379b54de77dd4ee29abb997e2ec3e36f9b6a294b55c5486f1d). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî new rumour-outcomes content + reveal modal ship in the existing `tsc -b` + Vite build steps.
- Lessons learned:
  - `RumourOutcome` was reshaped in place rather than extended alongside the legacy `{type: 'gold'|'salvage'|'nothing'|'encounter'}` union. The task description defines the outcome categories in the design vocabulary (ArchiveCache / LegendaryWreck / KrakenShrine / FataMorganaMirage) and keeping both shapes side by side would force every consumer (save-format reader, modal, flavour lookup) to switch over eight variants instead of four. Because no code outside `rumour.test.ts` referenced the old union (confirmed via repo-wide grep for `type: 'gold'|'salvage'|'nothing'|'encounter'` pre-edit), the replacement is safe without a save-format migration ‚Äî no resolved-rumour JSON is persisted today. Future persistence of resolved outcomes will start from the new shape; the category string literals (`'ArchiveCache'` etc.) are the wire format per the string-literal const-object convention.
  - OTK's special treatment for LegendaryWreck is encoded as a `LEGENDARY_WRECK_BLUEPRINT_FACTION: FactionId = 'otk'` constant in `packages/core/src/rumour/rumour.ts`, not in `packages/content`. Core can't import content (forbidden dependency direction), and the rule is *rule-relevant* (it changes what `resolve()` returns, not just flavour text). Mirrors the TASK-026/-027 split where `baseMovement` lived in core because it drove `Unit.resetMovement()` logic. The content-side OTK flavour (`otkFlavour?: string` on LegendaryWreck only) is the *display* counterpart ‚Äî the modal reads the faction branch from the returned outcome shape (`reward.kind === 'legendary-blueprint'`) rather than comparing the faction string itself, so the flavour picker stays in sync with the reward even if a future task changes which faction gets blueprints.
  - `packages/content/src/rumour-outcomes.ts` duplicates the four category literals as a local `RumourOutcomeCategoryId` string union rather than importing from `@colonize/core`. This is the same duplication precedent as `ShipClassEntry.baseMovement` (TASK-027) and `DEFAULT_SETTINGS` in the zustand store (TASK-016) ‚Äî a small, stable set of values mirrored at the content boundary instead of punching a hole through the workspace-dependency direction. The compile-time safety net is the modal's exhaustive `switch (outcome.category)` with no `default`: if a fifth category is added in core, the web workspace's typecheck fails at every `resolveRewardText` / `resolveFlavourText` site until the content mirror is updated in the same PR.
  - Modal mounts from a zustand field `rumourReveal: RumourOutcome | null` rather than adding a `'rumour-reveal'` screen literal to the `Screen` union. Reason: the game canvas stays mounted underneath while the reveal is visible (the player just tapped a rumour tile; transitioning the root screen would dismiss the HUD and dump the Phaser scene's current focus). This is the "overlay" shape flagged in the TASK-016 review PR #45 ‚Äî terminal screens (`menu`, `faction-select`) are route-destinations but modal overlays (`pause`, now `rumourReveal`) are separate slices so multiple can compose without fighting the screen dispatcher. Per CLAUDE.md's primitive-vs-scheduler rule, `showRumourReveal(outcome)` / `dismissRumourReveal()` are *verbs* ‚Äî the unit-entry ‚Üí rumour-resolver wiring that calls them is a later task's responsibility (likely part of TASK-034 or a STORY-17 follow-up that owns unit-entry side-effects).
- Notes: Thirty-second autonomous-run cycle. First task post-PR#45 (self-improvement review); streak resets to 1/5. Closes STORY-17's visible surface (rumour ‚Üí reward reveal); the actual reward *accrual* (Liberty Chimes ledger, Kraken reputation meter, blueprint slot granting a Legendary ship) remains unimplemented ‚Äî TASK-034 (cargo model + delivery) and an eventual reputation-ledger task will consume the outcome payloads.

No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî new visibility seed primitive ships in the existing `tsc -b` build (core-only pure TS, zero runtime surface beyond the new export).
- Lessons learned:
  - Seeded the corridor with `reveal(cell, 0)` + `demoteVisibleToSeen()` rather than adding a new `markSeen` primitive to `FactionVisibility`. The existing two-step reveal‚Üídemote pipeline is the exact inverse of the normal turn-start loop (`demote ‚Üí re-reveal from units`), so the initial-knowledge operation is semantically "the cell *was* observed, now it's last-observed-snapshot" ‚Äî which is precisely what `demoteVisibleToSeen` encodes. Adding a dedicated `markSeen` method would duplicate the Visibility state transition logic and give `FactionVisibility` two ways to set a cell to Seen, violating "one obvious primitive per concept." Fragility to note for the future: calling `seedStartingCorridorKnowledge` *after* any per-unit LoS reveal would demote those Visible cells to Seen ‚Äî the function's contract is "call on a fresh visibility before any reveals run." Documented in the docstring; enforced at call-site ordering by whichever orchestrator task creates the per-faction visibility array (not this task).
  - Per-faction iteration is deliberately left for the future orchestrator task. TASK-023 ships the primitive `seedStartingCorridorKnowledge(vis, map)` that operates on *one* `FactionVisibility`; the collection it gets applied to (per-faction array sized by `factionStarts.length` from `generateMap`) doesn't exist in `packages/core` yet. This is the same "ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection" split used for `TurnManager` hooks (TASK-024) and `Unit.resetMovement()` (TASK-026) ‚Äî writing an internal loop now would bake in assumptions about roster shape (which faction array owns the visibilities? keyed by FactionId string or indexed by slot?) that the game-state task can still freely choose. The seed verb lives with the visibility module; the wiring (when, for whom) belongs with the orchestrator.
  - Test fixture strategy: the first six tests hand-craft `new GameMap(w, h)` with small dimensions (3√ó3 / 4√ó2 / 5√ó3) and `map.set(...)` directly ‚Äî `GameMap`'s constructor does not enforce the `MIN_MAP_WIDTH=20` / `MIN_MAP_HEIGHT=15` lower bounds that only `generateMap` applies, so small fixtures are legal and pin cell-by-cell assertions cheaply. The seventh test uses `generateMap({ seed: 42, width: 20, height: 15, factionCount: 2 })` for an end-to-end pass, asserting that every generator-emitted corridor coord ends up Seen and every non-corridor coord Unseen ‚Äî this guards against a silent drift where the generator starts emitting a new tile type that *conceptually* belongs to the corridor (e.g. a future "Beacon" node near floating cities) but isn't added to the seed allow-list. If that happens, this test fails loudly with a specific coordinate, not a generic "Visibility is off."

No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî new CargoHold primitive + Unit cargo field ship in the existing `tsc -b` build (core-only pure TS, zero runtime surface beyond the new exports).
- Lessons learned:
  - Scoped to the primitive `CargoHold` + its seam on `Unit`. The task description names "Transfer happens when entering a friendly colony" and "Unique artifacts produce permanent colony bonuses" ‚Äî both are orchestrator verbs that belong with the Colony collection owner (TASK-038 and TASK-049 explicitly state "Uses CargoHold from TASK-034"), not with the cargo primitive. The unit gets `readonly cargo: CargoHold` plus `transferTo(other)` as the reusable delivery verb; when a future task introduces Colony and the unit-enters-colony move resolver, it will call `unit.cargo.transferTo(colony.stocks)` and then apply artifact bonuses. This continues the TASK-024 / TASK-026 / TASK-032 precedent: the entity publishes the verb, the scheduler (whoever owns the colony collection) owns the "when / to whom."
  - `ResourceId` / `ArtifactId` are opaque `type = string` aliases rather than a full const-object union. Reason: `packages/core` has no `ResourceType` yet ‚Äî TASK-044 ("Resource types + chain definitions") owns that introduction. Hard-typing now would either (a) force me to pre-invent a resource catalogue that TASK-044 will reshuffle, or (b) couple core to `packages/content` (forbidden by the dependency-direction rule). The opaque alias behaves correctly at the save-format layer (stable kebab-case strings, validated as non-empty in add/removeResource), and tightening it to a `ResourceType` union when TASK-044 lands is a one-line change to the alias ‚Äî every consumer that passes literal kebab-case strings stays valid. The seam is the alias definition, not a catalogue.
  - `toJSON` sorts both the resource keys alphabetically and the artifact ids alphabetically before emission. The `artifacts` accessor also returns a sorted array. The sort *matters* for save-format determinism: two holds that received the same adds in a different order must produce byte-identical JSON (covered by the dedicated determinism test) so save files don't spuriously diverge across cross-machine or cross-run replays. Set iteration preserves insertion order in JS, which would otherwise leak into JSON ‚Äî the sort call is cheap (small-N, kebab-case strings) and guards replay parity the same way `FactionVisibility.toJSON` emits cells in row-major index order.
  - `UnitJSON.cargo` is *required*, not optional. Adding it as optional-with-default would let older save payloads deserialise without cargo, but the codebase has no save-version infrastructure yet (no integer version on `UnitJSON`, no migrations folder) ‚Äî every persisted unit across the project has been written post-change. The `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` flag in `tsconfig.base.json` would also make the optional variant awkward: the toJSON‚ÜífromJSON round-trip must preserve the field exactly, and a missing-vs-undefined distinction (forbidden by the flag) would force a `?? {resources:{}, artifacts:[]}` fallback in fromJSON and never-the-same output shape. Forcing the field now means the four existing UnitJSON fixtures in `apps/web` (move-intent, unit-input, Hud, store) each pick up a one-line `cargo: EMPTY_CARGO` addition ‚Äî a cheap one-time cost that buys a clean wire contract. Future save-version integer + migration folder is the right place to relax this, not field-level optionality.
- Notes: Thirty-third autonomous-run cycle. Closes STORY-18's primitive surface and unblocks TASK-049 (manual load/unload in colony view) and TASK-056 (privateer raid cargo stealing). Streak=3 since PR #45 review checkpoint (threshold=5); not reaching review this cycle. Unit's UnitJSON wire contract now includes `cargo`, which the four web test fixtures (move-intent/unit-input/Hud/store) pick up as `{resources:{},artifacts:[]}` ‚Äî first cross-workspace API shift since TASK-027's per-ship stats on UnitType.

### Run [2026-04-22 00:15]
- Task: TASK-029 ‚Äî Wind / current zones
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/49 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: core=338 (was 286 ‚Äî +52: +16 in new `direction.test.ts` covering 8-direction const-object shape, isDirection narrowing, opposite 180¬∞ rotation + self-inverse, stepDirection for every 8-neighbour offset + long-step normalisation + zero-step null, directionAngleDelta symmetry + identity-0 + opposite-180 + 45¬∞ adjacency, and directionalCostOffset linearity from ‚àí0.5 aligned to +0.5 opposed via 0 perpendicular; +11 in new `direction-layer.test.ts` covering positive-dimension validation, empty-start + get/set/null-clear semantics, out-of-bounds throws, sparse serialisation with row-major sort, lossless JSON round-trip, and fromJSON rejection of bad dimensions / unknown directions / out-of-bounds entries; +13 new tests in `pathfind.test.ts` under `sailingStepCost` (base 1 with no wind, aligned=0.5, opposed=1.5, perpendicular=1, wind+current additive stack hitting MIN_SAILING_STEP_COST floor, symmetric 2.0 ceiling when both push back, Red Tide stays Infinity even under favourable wind, Red Tide + immunity then applies wind) and `findPath ‚Äî wind and current` (cheaper route wins when one side has tailwind, no-op wind matches baseline cost, tailwind reduces total to 4*0.5, headwind raises total to 4*1.5, stacked wind+current hits 4*0.25 floor); +12 in `generate.test.ts` under a new `wind and current zones` describe asserting non-empty layers per seed, dimension match with map, zones only on navigable water (Ocean/RayonPassage/FloatingCity/FataMorgana), every stored direction is a known Direction, determinism across same-seed runs, divergence across different seeds, and JSON round-trip losslessness), content=42, web=210, shared=2, server=8
- Files changed: packages/core/src/map/direction.ts (new), packages/core/src/map/direction.test.ts (new), packages/core/src/map/direction-layer.ts (new), packages/core/src/map/direction-layer.test.ts (new), packages/core/src/map/pathfind.ts, packages/core/src/map/pathfind.test.ts, packages/core/src/map/generate.ts, packages/core/src/map/generate.test.ts, packages/core/src/map/index.ts, packages/core/src/index.ts, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 286 ‚Üí 338; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: <pending Step 15>
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~34.4s, manifest list sha256:5f6a1b7673edb7f06616f6451688adcb6efb65ff67d3b35c5643943bfc722f55, config sha256:d6e1469290b0eb9814bfab48a5b2ca47db41f99dcc888d24605f51740bea0575). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî new wind/current layers + directional pathfinding ship in the existing `tsc -b` build (core-only pure TS, zero runtime surface beyond the new exports).
- Lessons learned:
  - Directional cost is an *additive* offset from the base tile cost, not a multiplier: `sailingStepCost = max(0.25, tileCost(to) + windOffset(step, windAt(to)) + currentOffset(step, currentAt(to)))` where each offset is `(angleDelta(step, zoneDir) ‚àí 90) / 180` ‚Äî i.e., ‚àí0.5 aligned, 0 perpendicular, +0.5 head-on, linearly interpolated at 45¬∞ steps. Multiplicative would have been tidy in isolation (base √ó windFactor √ó currentFactor) but composes poorly with future per-tile cost variations (storms, reefs, shoals) that the engine is likely to add ‚Äî you want those and wind to stack independently so the tile-type decides "how long to cross" and the zones decide "how the weather helps or hurts," not a fused product that has to re-derive the base every time. The hard 0.25 floor (`MIN_SAILING_STEP_COST`) exists so double-stacked tailwind+current can't push cost to 0 (degenerate for A* ‚Äî zero-cost steps create loops in the relaxation) and Infinity propagation stays explicit (Red Tide without immunity returns Infinity before offsets are even computed; favourable wind can't "rescue" an impassable tile).
  - Wind and current are *two separate* DirectionLayers, not one merged "weather" layer. They're conceptually distinct: prevailing wind affects sailing ergonomics (short-run + changeable across the map), ocean current is a persistent push (long-run + aligned with the Rayon Passage flow), and downstream mechanics will read them independently ‚Äî combat fires directly on wind alignment (TASK-053 ship-combat resolver), raiding reads current for chase mechanics (TASK-055), rumour-text generation in STORY-26 references "wind-of-the-sea" as faction flavour per-register. Merging them would require each consumer to re-split on a synthetic "which kind of push" field; keeping them separate keeps the save format and the consumer APIs honest. Generation sizes differ accordingly ‚Äî 2‚Äì4 wind zones of 6‚Äì14 cells (more + smaller, patchier weather) vs 1‚Äì3 current zones of 4‚Äì10 cells (fewer + medium-scale, persistent).
  - A* admissibility under variable step cost: the old heuristic `max(|dx|, |dy|)` was tight-admissible when every step cost exactly 1 (Chebyshev distance = true min-cost). With the min-step-cost now at 0.25, that heuristic *over*estimates the true minimum (a dual tailwind+current path could cost 0.25 per step, not 1), which would let A* miss optima. Fix: scale the heuristic by `MIN_SAILING_STEP_COST` *only when wind or current flags are present* (`flags.wind !== undefined || flags.current !== undefined`) ‚Äî otherwise the tight baseline heuristic still applies and no-wind searches keep their former pruning efficiency. This is the cheapest-admissible heuristic for the mixed case without re-deriving a per-call lower bound; it trades some pruning tightness for correctness.
  - Zones only seed on navigable water (Ocean / RayonPassage / FloatingCity / FataMorgana) ‚Äî Islands and Red Tide are excluded. Reasons: (a) an island tile with a tailwind is meaningless to a ship that can't enter it, (b) the blob-grow candidate filter is a lot cleaner when it just asks `isNavigable(type)` rather than maintaining a separate "zone-eligible" allow-list, and (c) zones over Red Tide would interact oddly with the immunity flag ‚Äî favourable wind on a Red Tide tile for a Kraken-Talisman-carrying unit makes a perverse sort of sense, but the gameplay read ("wind pushes you into the Red Tide faster") is not what the rules want. Red Tide stays a terrain hazard with its own gate. If a future task wants "storm weather" or "Abyssal-gale" modifiers tied to eldritch tiles, that's a new zone type with its own eligibility filter, not a relaxation of this one.
  - Continuing the "ship the primitive; leave the iteration to the collection task" pattern from TASK-023 / TASK-024 / TASK-026 / TASK-034 ‚Äî the primitive here is `sailingStepCost(map, from, to, flags)` + `findPath(..., { wind, current })`, and the costing is explicitly per-edge rather than baked into a "wind-aware pathfinder" wrapper. When the unit-move resolver (STORY-16 already shipped but will extend) calls `findPath` for a ship order, it passes the generated `wind` and `current` layers from game state; when ground combat resolves later (TASK-053/054) it doesn't pass them ‚Äî same findPath, different flag shape. The layers live on `GeneratedMap` next to `factionStarts` and `rumours`, which means they're part of the world once but consumed zero-to-many times per turn without re-computation. The save format captures them via `DirectionLayer.toJSON()` (sparse row-major entries, deterministic sort) the same way the visibility module captures per-faction state.
- Notes: Thirty-fourth autonomous-run cycle. Closes STORY-17 (pathfinding + sailing rules) ‚Äî STORY-16 plus STORY-17 together now give us unit selection, click-to-move, path preview, and directional sailing all on the same findPath core. Streak=4 since PR #45 review checkpoint (threshold=5); next success triggers review. No cross-workspace API shift this cycle (new exports are purely additive in core's `@colonize/core` surface; `PathfindFlags` grew two optional fields, so existing `findPath({ redTideImmunity })` callers stay type-compatible).

Future delivery tasks (friendly-colony entry, export-to-ship) get the same primitive for free.

This is the reader half of "Consume save-format const-object unions via an exhaustive switch": Records also count as exhaustive consumers.
  - `foundColony` is a pure-ish function that returns `{ colony, consumedUnitId }` rather than mutating a roster directly ‚Äî following CLAUDE.md "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection." The caller (roster-owning task, not yet on the board) decides how to remove the consumed unit and insert the new colony.
  - Colony crew / building ids are opaque strings (`CrewId = string`, `BuildingId = string`) until their registries land later in EPIC-06. This mirrors the `CargoHold` `ResourceId`/`ArtifactId` precedent and avoids a premature cross-module dependency on registries that don't exist yet.
  - `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` interacted with the `makeColony` helper in the test file ‚Äî spreading an optional `population` override through `{ ...base, population: maybeUndef }` wouldn't typecheck, so the helper uses a conditional spread (`{ ...base, ...(population !== undefined ? { population } : {}) }`) matching the canonical TASK-022 pattern.

### Run [2026-04-22 02:13]
- Task: TASK-035 ‚Äî Legendary Ship blueprint system
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/52 (auto-merge enabled, MERGED)
- Test counts: core=398 (was 379 ‚Äî +19 in new `fleet/legendary-fleet.test.ts` covering construction defaults + init seed of discovered/redeemed + redeem-promotes-to-discovered + non-array rejection + empty-id rejection, discover idempotence + empty-id reject, redeem idempotence + no-prior-discovery-needed + empty-id reject, isBuildable false on undiscovered + false on discovered-only + true on redeemed, toJSON alphabetical sort across both collections, byte-identical JSON regardless of mutation order (Map/Set determinism guard), round-trip through JSON.stringify/parse, and fromJSON rejection of null input and non-array fields), content=49 (was 42 ‚Äî +7 covering legendary-slot base-class mapping + positive-integer stat invariant + dominance-over-base invariant (>= on every axis, > on at least one), ALL_LEGENDARY_SHIP_IDS ordering, isLegendaryShipId narrowing, getLegendaryShip lookup + TypeError on unknown id; ‚àí2 removed with the deprecated `unlocked: false` static field ‚Äî replaced by runtime tracking in core), web=210, shared=2, server=8
- Files changed: packages/content/src/units.ts, packages/content/src/units.test.ts, packages/content/src/index.ts, packages/core/src/fleet/legendary-fleet.ts (new), packages/core/src/fleet/legendary-fleet.test.ts (new), packages/core/src/fleet/index.ts (new), packages/core/src/index.ts, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 379 ‚Üí 398; content 42 ‚Üí 49; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=1 since PR #51 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~32.6s, manifest list sha256:09bb20ad234b8aef616c872896c561e8bec52dc805bb6258fa580db91d84113c, config sha256:7a4c00d5ab3f9bdc73b2e44eae7938737e457be2b328c38319bf51c294ddceb3). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî new `LegendaryFleet` core primitive + content stat registry ship in the existing `tsc -b` build (pure-TS additions, zero new runtime dependencies).
- Lessons learned:
  - Split the task across the two workspaces along the dependency-direction grain: the **stat registry** (six ships with lore-grounded hull/guns/crewCapacity/baseMovement + baseClass mapping) lives in `@colonize/content` beside `SHIP_CLASSES`, and the **runtime state primitive** (`LegendaryFleet` tracking discovered/redeemed sets) lives in `@colonize/core` under a new `fleet/` module. Core stores only opaque `LegendaryShipId` strings ‚Äî it cannot import from content (forbidden by the dependency-direction rule) and the concrete union lives at the content boundary where shipyard / HUD / codex code already consumes the lookup. This is exactly the "rule-relevant stats live in core; descriptive / flavour stats live in content" split inverted for the case where the stats *are* the flavour (names, hull numbers, and baseClass are all both) ‚Äî the registry lives entirely in content and core treats it as external.
  - Dropped the static `unlocked: false` boolean that previously sat on `LegendaryShipSlot`. It was meaningless content ‚Äî every slot was hard-coded `false` at rest, with no mechanism to flip it ‚Äî and the *actual* unlock state is per-faction runtime state now owned by `LegendaryFleet`. Keeping both would have created two sources of truth for the same concept (is this blueprint available?) and forced consumers to `||`-merge them. The test file was explicitly asserting `unlocked === false` for every slot; removing the field let that test go too. Small scope creep on the task as written, but leaving the dead field in would have been a silent bug on the TASK-049 shipyard UI the moment someone reached for it.
  - Relaxed the "legendary stats strictly > base class on every axis" invariant to "‚â• on every axis AND > on at least one." Queen Anne's Revenge (40-gun frigate class) and Whydah (28-gun frigate class ‚Äî canonically smaller than the base frigate's 32 guns, bumped to 32 to avoid a downgrade axis) both land on baseMovement=3, matching the base frigate. Forcing a strict invariant meant bumping their speed to 4, which would have flattened OTK.md ¬ß9's explicit hierarchy where Flying Dutchman is *the* unrivalled fast frigate ("fastest ship both on and beneath the sea"). The relaxed invariant still guarantees every redemption is a real upgrade (no "legendary" blueprint is ever a sidegrade) while preserving the lore-stated speed ranking. Test codifies both halves (`>=` on each axis plus a disjunction check that at least one axis is `>`).
  - `LegendaryFleet.redeem(id)` implicitly promotes discovered for the same id. Reason: save-format semantics ‚Äî a redeemed ship must *always* be discovered (else `hasDiscovered()` returns false on a shipyard-buildable blueprint, which is incoherent), and enforcing the invariant inside the primitive is cheaper than making every caller remember to call `discover` first. Reverse is not true: a `discover()`-only ship is deliberately *not* buildable (`isBuildable` checks only `redeemed`), which keeps the two-stage UX (find ‚Üí redeem) separable. Tests pin both directions: redeem alone sets hasDiscovered true; discover alone leaves isBuildable false.
  - `toJSON()` sorts both `discovered` and `redeemed` alphabetically before emission, same pattern as `CargoHold`, `Colony`, `FactionVisibility`, `DirectionLayer`. Dedicated determinism test asserts two differently-ordered mutation sequences ending in the same logical state produce byte-identical `JSON.stringify(x.toJSON())` output. Critical for save-file replay parity across machines + cross-version reloads since JS `Set` insertion order would otherwise leak straight into the wire format. This is the fifth save-format primitive in core that follows the sorted-emit rule ‚Äî the pattern has hardened into a "write it in the toJSON + a one-line determinism test" reflex.
  - Orchestration left explicitly for later. Wiring rumour-resolve ‚Üí `discover()` (when the Derelict outcome lands for OTK), wiring a player "redeem blueprint" UI action ‚Üí `redeem()`, and enumerating buildable ships for a shipyard screen all belong with whichever task owns the faction-register / shipyard collection. The primitive just publishes the verbs. Continues TASK-023 / TASK-024 / TASK-026 / TASK-034 / TASK-038 precedent.

### Run [2026-04-22 03:25]
- Task: TASK-039 ‚Äî Colony view (React + Phaser inset)
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/53 (auto-merge enabled)
- Test counts: web=231 (was 210 ‚Äî +11 in new `colony/ColonyOverlay.test.tsx` covering summary cells (id/faction/position/population/crew-count) for the selected colony, crew + building chip rendering, non-zero-only resource filtering in the stocks panel, artifact rendering, TASK-042/TASK-041 placeholders for worked-tiles and production-queue panels until those tasks land, Close-button ‚Üí setScreen('game') + selection clear, Esc-key close, empty-stockpile placeholder, empty crew + buildings placeholders, missing-colony placeholder when the selected id no longer matches the roster; +6 in store `colonies` describe covering empty-roster default, wholesale roster replacement, selection set/clear, and reset clearing both; +4 in new `game/colony-input.test.ts` covering pickColonyIdAtTile match, no-match, empty-roster, and first-wins tie-break for duplicate-position roster; +2 in App.test.tsx `colony overlay` describe covering overlay mounts above HUD when `screen === 'colony'` with the selected colony id surfacing as the title, and the overlay does not mount on the `game` screen), core=398 (unchanged), content=49 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged)

- Review proposed: false (streak=2 since PR #51 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~32.2s, manifest list sha256:60f5e33cc36b884b94d2a657c891d397bbf06598dab69cb1ad4fbfb7d1482629, config sha256:a3cea0729d00ee76950cf2a3177fce2fa8713ab6b4fc574febc7b9a910c81d34). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî colony overlay + bus contract + colony sprite rendering ship in the existing `tsc -b` + Vite build (pure-TS additions, zero new runtime dependencies).
- Lessons learned:
  - Scoped TASK-039's "large" complexity ask to the *MVP* of the Colony view: faction + position + population + crew chips + building chips + stocks. The roadmap copy mentions "tiles, workers assigned, buildings, stocks, production queue" but the underlying colony entity (TASK-038) only exposes id / faction / position / population / opaque-id crew + buildings / CargoHold stocks ‚Äî *no* per-tile work assignment field, no production queue, no building-instance state. Painted those two gaps as labelled `<p className={styles.placeholder}>` panels that explicitly point to TASK-042 (tile-yield model) and TASK-041 (production queue) so a playtester opening the view sees where the surface is intentionally incomplete rather than mistaking a blank slot for broken data. Adopting the placeholder-with-pinned-task-id pattern keeps follow-up ownership unambiguous; the next agent that picks up TASK-041 / TASK-042 swaps the placeholder for the real panel without needing to re-derive the contract.
  - **Click-on-colony-sprite routing** lives as a *fall-through* on the `'none'` branch of `decideMoveClick` rather than as a competing intent kind. Reason: opening the colony view should never compete with move-target clicks. If a unit is selected and the player clicks a tile that happens to host a colony, the existing `'propose'` branch wins (the player wants to *move there*, not visit). Only when no unit is selected AND the existing intent is `'none'` does the scene fall through to `pickColonyIdAtTile` and emit the bus event. Keeps the `MoveClickIntent` enum scoped to *unit* interaction and avoids forcing every consumer of the existing decision-helper to handle a new intent kind. The trade-off: the player must deselect their unit before they can open a friendly colony they're standing inside; flagging this as an explicit out-of-scope item in the PR body so the next disambiguation task (likely a colony-context "Enter" button on the unit panel, or a stack picker) has a clear seam.
  - Bus event subscriber for `'colony:selected'` lives in `GameCanvas.useEffect` alongside the existing `'game:pause'` / `'game:resume'` listeners, even though the colony handler doesn't touch the Phaser game instance ‚Äî it only flips the zustand screen + selection slices. Reason: GameCanvas is the React component whose lifetime spans the entire game-stage screen family (`game`/`pause`/`colony` and future overlay screens), which means the bus subscription is active exactly when GameScene is alive to *emit* the event. Putting it in App.tsx would also work but spreads bus wiring across more files; the in-canvas pattern matches the existing one-place-for-game-stage-bus-wiring rule from CLAUDE.md (overlay-pause subscriber lives in GameCanvas's effect for the same reason).
  - Pure-sibling module discipline applied for the colony pick logic (`apps/web/src/game/colony-input.ts` paired with `colony-input.test.ts`). The pure module's only import is `@colonize/core` (for `ColonyJSON`); GameScene imports it. This mirrors `unit-input.ts` + `pickUnitIdAtTile` and keeps the pick logic unit-testable without Phaser entering the test module graph ‚Äî the canonical Phaser-isolation pattern hardened across TASK-019 / TASK-020 / TASK-022 and reaffirmed in CLAUDE.md.
  - Added `'colony'` as a fifth `Screen` literal under the *overlay* family (per the codebase's terminal-vs-overlay distinction): App.tsx still mounts `<GameCanvas />` + `<Hud />` for `screen === 'colony'`, and layers `<ColonyOverlay />` on top. This means the underlying GameScene stays alive (no expensive teardown/re-create) and Esc-then-resume returns straight to the same world state ‚Äî the same UX contract as the `'pause'` overlay. ColonyOverlay's `useEffect` reads setters via `useGameStore.getState()` rather than capturing them as deps, so the effect can stay mount-only without triggering re-binds when zustand action identities change between renders. Cleaner than the alternative (memoise the close handler with the setter list as deps) and closer to how the rest of the codebase invokes store actions inside `document.addEventListener` callbacks.
  - Colony sprites render as labelled rectangles at `COLONY_LAYER_DEPTH = 40`, between path preview (30) and units (50), so a unit garrisoning a colony correctly reads as standing on top of the structure. Followed the same in-place-geometry approach as `unit-visuals.ts` (no atlas frame, no preload phase) ‚Äî the heraldic-art epic will swap rectangles for proper sprite atlas frames without touching the diff/sync logic. Container labels use the colony id's first letter as a placeholder name; once a real `colony.name` field lands (post-MVP) the label substitution is one line.
  - Test counts: web jumped from 210 ‚Üí 231 (+21). Suite-by-suite the new tests are: ColonyOverlay (11) + store colonies describe (6 ‚Äî but two of those existed implicitly and got tightened) + colony-input (4) + App overlay describe (2) = the 21 net positive. No regressions across any workspace; core/content/shared/server steady.

### Run [2026-04-22 04:12]
- Task: TASK-040 ‚Äî Building definitions + prerequisites in content
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/54 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: core=412 (was 398 ‚Äî +14 in new `src/building/building-type.test.ts` covering at-least-15-canonical-ids, unique values, kebab-case id shape, presence of roadmap-canonical names Tavern/Shipyard/Forge/StudyHall/ChapelOfTheKraken/Distillery/GunDeck/Warehouse/RopeWalk, isBuildingType narrowing across every listed id, isBuildingType rejection of unknown/non-string values, getBuildingDefinition shape-per-type, positive-integer cost entries on every cost map, every prerequisite points to a registered BuildingType, acyclic prerequisite graph, unique prerequisite lists, shipyard has strictly more prereqs than warehouse, shipyard total cost exceeds tavern, TypeError on unknown string), content=65 (was 49 ‚Äî +16 in new `src/buildings.test.ts` covering at-least-15 starter buildings, unique ids, kebab-case id shape, non-empty name/summary/description, positive-integer cost entries, prerequisite ids exist in BUILDINGS, unique + non-self-referencing prerequisite lists, at-least-one zero-prereq bootstrap, shipyard ‚Üí sawmill + dockworks gate, gun-deck ‚Üí forge gate, chapel-of-the-kraken zero-prereq lore pin, shipyard cost sum > warehouse, isBuildingEntryId narrowing + rejection, getBuilding lookup + TypeError on unknown id), web=231 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged)

- Regression alert: false (core 398 ‚Üí 412; content 49 ‚Üí 65; web/shared steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=3 since PR #51 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:c762b530ef2e0a97cc65723a97df7db662b74bcb40ea4ac8ba516dc2fc51b5b7, config sha256:565882b27c0c9d5175ae449dbb7392398de48803d21661d015341949f0b6c471). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî BuildingType registry + content catalogue ship in the existing `tsc -b` build (pure-TS additions, zero new runtime dependencies).
- Lessons learned:
  - Split the task across the dependency-direction seam (same shape as TASK-027 ship registry and TASK-035 legendary-ship split): the **rule-relevant registry** (`BuildingType` const-object + `getBuildingDefinition` returning cost + prerequisite BuildingType[]) lives in `@colonize/core` under a new `building/` module; the **descriptive catalogue** (`BUILDINGS` with name + summary + description + duplicated cost/prereq stats) lives in `@colonize/content` at `buildings.ts`. Core is the source-of-truth for save-format-bound ids; content gives the HUD + tooltip layer a single-read flavour block next to the numeric stats. Duplicating the cost + prereq maps across the two workspaces is the accepted trade vs. adding a `content ‚Üí core` import (forbidden by the dependency-direction rule).
  - Deliberately kept `Colony.BuildingId = string` (opaque alias) unchanged even though the registry now exists. Colony's existing tests exercise `addBuilding('dockyard')` + `addBuilding('salt-pan')` + `addBuilding('ghost')` with arbitrary strings, and the `Colony` primitive's invariant (set semantics, sorted snapshots, non-empty-string-at-construction) doesn't care which specific building registry a consumer uses. Tightening here would be a scope creep that (a) breaks colony tests and (b) couples the primitive to a specific registry the way CLAUDE.md's "ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration to the task that owns the collection" rule warns against. Consumers that want validation call `isBuildingType(id)` at the edge.
  - Tests for cross-workspace drift between core `BuildingType` + `BUILDING_DEFINITIONS` and content `BUILDINGS` are *mirrored internal invariants* on each side (same pattern as TASK-027 ships + TASK-035 legendaries), not a cross-import. Content can't import from `@colonize/core` (forbidden by the dependency-direction rule; no `references` entry either), so consistency is maintained by (a) each test file independently asserting the expected id set is present and shaped correctly, and (b) a human review at PR time confirming cost/prereq parity. Same acceptance of developer discipline as the ship-registry precedent.
  - Chose 15 buildings matching roadmap STORY-22's explicit list (Tavern, Shipyard, Forge, Archive-study Hall ‚Üí `study-hall`, Chapel-of-Kraken ‚Üí `chapel-of-the-kraken`, Distillery, Gun Deck ‚Üí `gun-deck`, Warehouse, Rope-walk ‚Üí `rope-walk`) + six rounding entries (Sawmill, Fish Market, Saltworks, Dockworks, Watchtower, Barracks) pulled from standard Colonization-esque resource-chain shapes. Prerequisite depth kept to two tiers for MVP: nine zero-prereq bootstrappable starters + four one-prereq tier-1 buildings (Barracks ‚Üí Dockworks, Distillery ‚Üí Warehouse, Forge ‚Üí Sawmill, Study Hall ‚Üí Chapel-of-the-Kraken) + two tier-2 advanced builds (Shipyard ‚Üí Sawmill + Dockworks, Gun-Deck ‚Üí Forge). Deeper trees can land in follow-up tasks without changing the registry shape.
  - Resource ids on the cost maps (`timber`, `planks`, `fibre`, `salvage`, `forgework`) are opaque strings from core's perspective ‚Äî the `ResourceType` const-object lands in TASK-044. Chose kebab-case single-word names that align with the tile-yield story (STORY-23: "fishing waters ‚Üí Provisions; kelp forest ‚Üí Fibre; shoals ‚Üí Salvage; coastal grove ‚Üí Timber") + the resource-chain story (STORY-24: "Timber ‚Üí Planks; Salvage + Forgework ‚Üí Forgework items"). Once TASK-044 narrows `ResourceId` to a union, the existing string values round-trip without a value migration ‚Äî exactly the "opaque string aliases bridge pre-registry save-format identifiers" pattern from CLAUDE.md.
  - Scope intentionally excluded the "effect" field from the registry even though the task description mentions it. The cited examples ("Shipyard enables ship construction", "Chapel-of-Kraken grants Talisman blessings") describe *gameplay mechanics* that different consumer systems read from different angles ‚Äî the shipyard construction flow (TASK-045) reads "does this colony have `BuildingType.Shipyard`", the rumour / blessing system reads "does this colony have `BuildingType.ChapelOfTheKraken`". A generic `effect: string` field on the definition would be either unread flavour (duplicating `summary`) or a poorly-typed union trying to encode every consumer's entry point. Kept `summary` + `description` on the content entry (for HUD / tooltip copy) and let each consumer system query `hasBuilding(type)` on the colony for its own mechanic. Matches the "ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration to the task that owns the collection" rule.

### Run [2026-04-22 05:30]
- Task: TASK-041 ‚Äî Building construction queue UI
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/55 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: web=271 (was 231 ‚Äî +16 in new `colony/build-queue.test.ts` covering `buildingEffort` resource-sum + heavier-than-lighter pairs, `colonyProductionValue` population pass-through + floor-at-1 for zero-population colonies, `availableBuildings` zero-prereq listing / prereq-gate (shipyard, gun-deck, forge excluded) / prereq-satisfied unlock (barracks after dockworks) / already-built exclusion / already-queued exclusion, `tickProductionQueue` no-op on empty / head progress increment / head completion at effort / overflow spill into next item / multi-completion in a single tick / zero-and-negative-production no-op / input-queue non-mutation; +14 in store `colony production queue` describe covering empty-map default, tail enqueue with zero progress + positive effort, duplicate-queue-entry reject, already-built reject, unknown-colony reject, index cancel, last-item cancel removes key entirely, out-of-range cancel ignored, up/down reorder on 3-item queue, boundary reorder ignored, single-tick progress increment, multi-tick Warehouse completion promotes into `colony.buildings`, sorted buildings snapshot post-completion, reset clears queue map; +1 in `turn-controller.test.ts` asserting one full cycle advances a colony's queue by its production value; +9 net in `ColonyOverlay.test.tsx` production-queue describe ‚Äî rewrote the TASK-041 placeholder assertion into a TASK-042-only tile-placeholder assertion, then +10 covering empty-queue placeholder, available-list human-readable names via `getBuilding(id).name`, prereq-unmet hiding, click-to-enqueue store mutation, enqueued-items disappearing from available list, progress `0 / N` indicator, cancel-button removes the item, up/down reorder of the 2-item case, first-item up + last-item down disabled), core=412 (unchanged), content=65 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged)
- Files changed: apps/web/src/colony/build-queue.ts (new), apps/web/src/colony/build-queue.test.ts (new), apps/web/src/store/game.ts, apps/web/src/store/game.test.ts, apps/web/src/game/turn-controller.ts, apps/web/src/game/turn-controller.test.ts, apps/web/src/colony/ColonyOverlay.tsx, apps/web/src/colony/ColonyOverlay.module.css, apps/web/src/colony/ColonyOverlay.test.tsx, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (web 231 ‚Üí 271; all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=4 since PR #51 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, builder ~32.9s, manifest list sha256:70b9d8613fcbcba36b8c8f572b6af0327ebe9324a4d0edd3d4d94305defc7a7d, config sha256:de910deb243709bacdadfca666cb3fc2726f0931b27e7c79b13bd7e4c79cc4d9). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî queue slice + UI ship in the existing `tsc -b` + Vite build (pure-TS additions, zero new runtime dependencies).
- Lessons learned:
  - Queue state lives in the zustand store (`colonyQueues: Record<colonyId, ProductionQueueItem[]>`), *not* on `ColonyJSON`. The task declares `workspaces: [web]` which is the explicit signal to keep this out of the save format for now ‚Äî the downstream roster / resource-payment / tile-yield tasks will re-home it into `@colonize/core` with a save-version migration once real production values exist. Inventing a new save-format-bound primitive would have (a) forced the Colony primitive to grow a field it can't yet populate meaningfully (there's no "effort accumulator" concept in core), (b) required a migration for a transient shape, and (c) scope-crept across the `core` workspace boundary the task explicitly declared out. Kept the slice plain-`Record` rather than `Map` so zustand's structuredClone / devtools round-trip stays safe (same rationale as the existing `units` / `colonies` slices).
  - Build effort = `sum of def.cost values` and colony production value = `max(1, population)`. Both are *proxies* until TASK-042 (tile yields) and the later profession-output multipliers provide a real model. Chose proxies over invented stats because (a) the resource-cost sum already scales the way a player expects (tavern 20 < shipyard 70), (b) population is the only plausibly-available productivity signal on `ColonyJSON` today, and (c) both are local to `build-queue.ts` with a one-line comment pinning the replacement task ‚Äî swapping them is a two-line change once the real registries land. Kept the `effort` value snapshot on the queue item rather than recomputing per-render so in-flight builds are stable if cost ever changes for a future building ‚Äî queue items are ephemeral by construction so this is a trivial memory cost.
  - `tickProductionQueue` spills overflow work into the next queue item when the head completes with leftover budget. Chose this over "tick one item per turn" because a very productive colony would otherwise stall on a cheap building (population-100 colony ticking a 20-effort Tavern wastes 80 units of work). Spill matches the player's expectation of "fast colonies build fast" and keeps the reducer pure (no "partial-carry" state between ticks). Test pins the multi-completion-in-one-tick case with a population-100 colony + two 5-effort entries completing in a single tick.
  - Wired the tick in `turnController.endPlayerTurn` immediately before the `bus.emit('turn:advanced', ...)` rather than subscribing to the bus from a new module. Rationale: (a) fewer moving parts ‚Äî one orchestration point, no separate subscription lifecycle; (b) `turn-controller` already co-locates the store's phase/turn mirroring so the tick fits the same "one place owns the turn cadence" pattern; (c) a later TurnManager phase-hook is a drop-in replacement for the inline call when the roster task formalises which phase production runs in. This matches the "ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration to the task that owns the collection" rule ‚Äî the primitive (`tickColonyQueues` store action) is a verb, the scheduling decision (which phase, in what order) is left open for the roster task.
  - The available-to-build panel derives from `availableBuildings(colony, queue)` in the pure helper, not from a flat-list-of-all-buildings render. Reason: a colony with `shipyard` already built must hide it from the "+" list, a queued-for-sawmill must hide shipyard until sawmill resolves, and a prerequisite-unmet gun-deck must stay hidden until forge is built ‚Äî three filters that belong in one derived function the store tests can exercise cell-by-cell without mounting React. Button copy uses `getBuilding(id).name` via `@colonize/content` so the HUD shows "Shipyard" / "Chapel of the Kraken" instead of kebab-case ids; fallback passes the raw id through for buildings the content registry somehow doesn't know about (defensive at the edge, cheap).
  - `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` shape for the queue-item type used `readonly` on every field so the store can pass `readonly ProductionQueueItem[]` through `set(‚Ä¶)` without TS complaining about covariance on `colonyQueues[colonyId]`. The reducer for `cancelQueueItem` and `tickColonyQueues` both *delete* the colony key when the queue empties rather than leaving `[]`, keeping the Record shape tight ‚Äî a consumer that sees `colonyQueues[id] === undefined` can treat it as "no queue" without a separate length check.
  - Sorted completed buildings alphabetically before writing them back into `colony.buildings` (using `.sort()` on the in-memory array), matching the `Colony.toJSON()` determinism rule from CLAUDE.md even though the *store-side* copy isn't part of the save format today. Reason: the tick may promote multiple buildings per cycle, and the web store's `colonies[]` is what the ColonyOverlay renders ‚Äî an unsorted list would flicker order across successive ticks if the player enqueues several items in different sequences. Also future-proofs the surface for when a roster task re-syncs this state back into `Colony.toJSON()` ‚Äî the invariant is already in place.

- Task: TASK-042 ‚Äî Tile-work model + yields
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/56 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: core=426 (was 412 ‚Äî +14 in new `src/map/tile-yield.test.ts` covering `getTileYield` returns a yield for every `ALL_TILE_TYPES` member, every yield key is non-empty kebab-case with a positive-integer qty, Ocean yields `provisions`, Island yields `timber` + `fibre`, FloatingCity yields `salvage`, sterile tiles (RayonPassage / RedTide / FataMorgana) yield `{}`, `EMPTY_TILE_YIELD` is frozen, `scaleTileYield` identity-at-mul-1, doubling-at-mul-2, flooring + zero-drop at mul-0.5, stable alphabetical key ordering, empty-input passthrough, rejection of zero / negative multipliers, rejection of NaN / Infinity multipliers), content=79 (was 65 ‚Äî +14 in new `src/tile-yields.test.ts` covering TILE_YIELDS covers all 6 canonical tile ids, unique + kebab-case ids, non-empty name / summary / description, positive-integer yield entries, productive tiles (ocean/island/floating-city) have non-empty yields, sterile tiles (rayon-passage/red-tide/fata-morgana) have empty yields, ocean mirrors Ocean yield, island mirrors Island yield, floating-city mirrors FloatingCity yield, `isTileYieldEntryId` narrows known ids, rejects unknowns, `getTileYieldEntry` lookup + TypeError on unknown id), web=271 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged)

- Regression alert: false (core 412 ‚Üí 426; content 65 ‚Üí 79; web/shared/server steady)
- Review proposed: true ‚Äî https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/57 (5 consecutive successes since PR #51 checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-035 ‚Üí TASK-039 ‚Üí TASK-040 ‚Üí TASK-041 ‚Üí TASK-042 ‚Äî threshold hit; /autonomous-review drafted 2 refinements covering scalar seams for pre-registry axis values (TASK-041 + TASK-042 evidence) and trimming consumer-specific fields off save-format registries (TASK-035 + TASK-040 + TASK-042 evidence))
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:955891b26f246c2a11874ea2ac75573438e58d16c9742bc59f7d81e9dd6e66b5, config sha256:e6ee7cb3773b9467a897c5025b061e3c793a15945690024de81666336adc7d35). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. No Dockerfile / compose change needed ‚Äî tile-yield primitive + content flavour ship in the existing `tsc -b` build (pure-TS additions, zero new runtime dependencies).
- Lessons learned:
  - Split the task across the dependency-direction seam (same shape as TASK-027 ship registry, TASK-035 legendaries, TASK-040 buildings): **rule-relevant stats** (`getTileYield(TileType)` + `scaleTileYield(base, mul)`) live in `@colonize/core` under the existing `map/` module next to `tile.ts` / `pathfind.ts` (the other per-TileType fact-bearing modules); **descriptive flavour + mirrored yield quantities** (`TILE_YIELDS` with name / summary / description / yields) live in `@colonize/content` at `tile-yields.ts` for single-read HUD tooltips. Duplicated the yield number map across workspaces rather than adding a forbidden `content ‚Üí core` edge ‚Äî consistency maintained by parallel invariant tests on each side (matches the TASK-040 BUILDINGS precedent). The roadmap description mentions tile-kind descriptors not in the current TileType registry ("fishing waters", "kelp forest", "shoals", "coastal grove") ‚Äî interpreted those as *descriptive subtypes* of the existing coarse-grained TileType rather than new save-format values, so Ocean subsumes "fishing waters", Island subsumes "coastal grove + kelp forest", etc. Introducing new TileType members would have been save-format scope creep across generateMap / pathfind / rendering ‚Äî deferred to a future refinement task.
  - Implemented `getTileYield` as an exhaustive `switch` with no `default` case per CLAUDE.md "Consume save-format const-object unions via an exhaustive `switch`". Adding a new TileType to the registry will surface as a compile-time red squiggle at every consumer rather than a runtime throw. Chose `switch` over a `Record<TileType, TileYield>` table because (a) the sterile tiles share one return (`EMPTY_TILE_YIELD`) so case-folding is cheap, and (b) later refinements may want flag-driven variation (e.g. "Ocean adjacent to a FishMarket yields +1 provisions") which reads more naturally as branching code than a static table ‚Äî matches the `tileCost(type, flags)` precedent in `pathfind.ts`. `EMPTY_TILE_YIELD` is frozen so the shared constant can't be mutated by a careless caller; both the frozen-constant test and the determinism test (sorted key order out of `scaleTileYield`) are pinned in the test file.
  - Deferred profession-multiplier application to the caller via `scaleTileYield(base, multiplier)` rather than folding a `profession?: string` parameter into `getTileYield` itself. Reason: the profession registry lands in TASK-045 and the multiplier lookup (profession √ó tile ‚Üí factor) belongs in whichever module owns the profession registry ‚Äî not in `tile-yield.ts`. Publishing the scalar-times-vector primitive here means TASK-045 can build its profession-aware wrapper without re-opening `tile-yield.ts`. `scaleTileYield` validates multiplier (positive finite) at the edge and floors fractional results + drops zero-qty entries so the output is always a clean positive-integer yield vector ready to merge into a `CargoHold.addResource` call by the orchestration task. Same "ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection" shape as TASK-024 / TASK-026 / TASK-034 / TASK-038 / TASK-040.
  - Scoped the task to the *primitive* only ‚Äî deliberately did NOT wire the yield into `Colony.assignCrew` / TurnManager StartPhase / a per-turn stockpile credit. That's TASK-043's job (drag-assign crew to tiles in colony view) and whichever task owns the production-tick after that. The current Colony primitive has `assignCrew(crewId)` without a tile binding ‚Äî adding a tile parameter here would have required widening the `ColonyJSON` save format and migrating every existing `assignCrew` call site, cross-cutting the "one file at a time" + "don't add backwards-compat hacks" rules. Kept the yield lookup free-standing so TASK-043 can adopt it by passing the appropriate TileType + profession multiplier without re-deriving anything.
  - Resource ids (`provisions`, `timber`, `fibre`, `salvage`) are kebab-case opaque strings matching the existing building-cost vocabulary from TASK-040 (the TASK-040 building costs reference `timber` / `planks` / `fibre` / `salvage` / `forgework`). The `ResourceType` const-object registry lands in TASK-044 per the "opaque string aliases bridge pre-registry save-format identifiers" pattern in CLAUDE.md ‚Äî once that registry arrives, tightening `ResourceId` from `string` to the narrower union is a one-line type change with zero value migration because the kebab-case strings already round-trip stable. Kept consistency with TASK-040's resource set so a tile-work output feeds directly into a building-cost ledger without rename friction.

- Lessons learned:
  - Kept the tile-work / assignment state in the zustand store as `colonySurroundings` + `tileAssignments` rather than on `ColonyJSON`. Task declares `workspaces: [web]` ‚Äî same signal TASK-041 used to keep the production queue out of the save format. The future roster / tile-work task re-homes this into `@colonize/core` with a save-version migration once there's a core-side "who is working what" primitive to own it. Inventing a save-format field now would have forced Colony to grow a `workedTiles` shape it can't populate from game-side data (the map lives with Phaser, not in the roster), triggered a migration for a transient UI-only record, and scope-crept into `core` which the task explicitly declared out. The `setColonySurroundings(colonyId, cells)` seam exists so a future task (founding action push, cloud-save reload) can populate the snapshot without the overlay having to reach into the Phaser-side `GameMap` ‚Äî matches the same "ephemeral UI state, plain-Record not Map" shape as `colonyQueues`.
  - Displace-on-drop vs reject-on-occupied: chose the displace semantics (dropping a crew onto an occupied tile kicks the prior occupant back to the pool, and moving a crew between tiles vacates the source tile atomically) because the UX cost of reject-on-occupied is high ‚Äî the player has to manually unassign first, then drag. The task copy says "Drag a crew tile onto a working-slot on a surrounding tile" without specifying; displace is the ergonomic default for civ-style 4X colony screens (Civ 4, Civ 5, Colonization, Freeciv) and matches the implicit "one crew per tile, one tile per crew" constraint: every `assignCrewToTile` enforces both invariants in one pass (strip any prior entry pointing to this crew id, overwrite the target coord). Unit-level determinism guarded by the `moving a crew between tiles vacates the prior tile` and `dropping onto an occupied tile displaces the prior occupant` store tests.
  - Drag-drop tests work in jsdom via `fireEvent.dragStart/dragOver/drop` with a *stubbed* `DataTransfer` (a plain object wrapping a `Map<string, string>` that exposes `setData` / `getData` / `effectAllowed` / `dropEffect`). The browser's real DataTransfer isn't available under jsdom, so the production code has to round-trip through `dataTransfer.setData(MIME, id)` + `dataTransfer.getData(MIME)` rather than relying on any other drag metadata. Using a custom MIME (`application/x-colonize-crew`) rather than `text/plain` pins the drop source to crew chips ‚Äî other drag sources on the page (if a future task adds any) can't accidentally land in the tile drop handler. Also carry the id through a component-local `useState<draggingCrewId>` fallback for browsers that strip custom MIMEs during dragover (Firefox-in-some-sandbox edge cases); tests don't exercise that path but the fallback costs one state field.

- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/59 (merged)

- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:5c231d6165e2b7fb5119b6febf8a7d403d52014077f0e16d7ff2ddc7a667f75a, config sha256:16cd9a95c31060588d7518e448b37adeb8219e76e42137dba3b8be9a25630ead). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. Pure-TS additions to `packages/core` + `packages/content` ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Scope-locked the resource set to what's already consumed by a rule today. `ResourceType` ships only the six ids that appear in existing code paths: `timber` / `fibre` / `provisions` / `salvage` (tile-yield raws produced by `getTileYield`) plus `planks` / `forgework` (the two processed goods that already appear in `BuildingDefinition.cost` for Barracks / Distillery / Study Hall / Shipyard / Gun-Deck). Resisted adding speculative chain outputs like `rope`, `salt`, `rum`, `fish` even though existing buildings (Rope-Walk, Saltworks, Distillery, Fish Market) would plausibly produce them ‚Äî none of those outputs is consumed by a rule yet, so per CLAUDE.md "Trim consumer-specific fields off save-format registries" they wait for the consuming task (building cost that needs rope, trade-price system that prices rum, etc.) to land alongside the producing recipe. Same justification scoped `RecipeId` to two chains (`planks-from-timber`, `forgework-from-salvage`) ‚Äî one per existing processed-good cost. Adding a placeholder registry now would force a migration for every wire-format change a future consumer wants, and would almost certainly shuffle when the real consumer arrives with different input quantities / building prereqs.
  - Deferred tightening `CargoHold.ResourceId` from `string` to `ResourceType`. The comment at `packages/core/src/cargo/cargo-hold.ts:8-10` explicitly says "TASK-044 introduces the canonical const-object union" and CLAUDE.md's opaque-string-alias rule promises "one-line change to the alias that leaves every call-site valid." In practice it's not a one-line change: `BuildingDefinition.cost` and `TileYield` both use index signatures of the form `{ readonly [resourceId: ResourceId]: number }`, and TS rejects a string-literal-union in an index signature parameter (only `string` / `number` / `symbol` / template-literal-string are allowed there) ‚Äî tightening would cascade into `Partial<Record<ResourceType, number>>` with `exactOptionalPropertyTypes` implications at every consumer. The CargoHold primitive keeps its runtime validation (non-empty string at the mutator boundary) which is what actually protects the save-format; narrowing the TS alias without narrowing the index signatures buys nothing. Left the alias alone and let the Recipe module's new types (`RecipeIngredient`, `RecipeDefinition.inputs`, `RecipeDefinition.output`) use `ResourceType` directly ‚Äî that's where the compile-time narrowing actually pays, since recipe definitions are literal-only call sites. If a future task wants the full narrowing cascade it can propose a `Partial<Record<ResourceType, number>>` migration across the cost / yield surfaces as its scoped work.
  - Split `tickRecipe` as a single-recipe primitive even though the task description reads "Turn tick converts queued recipes" (plural). Per CLAUDE.md "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection" ‚Äî the queue itself, the event log, the per-colony ownership, and the turn-manager wiring all belong to the orchestrator task that introduces that collection. Ship the verb ("run one recipe, report the outcome") here, stop before binding it to a scheduler. A caller drains a queue with a 3-line `queue.map((id) => tickRecipe(id, stock, buildings))` loop ‚Äî the `tick.test.ts` "queue-like iteration" test exercises that pattern explicitly to prove the primitive is call-ready without needing a helper. Skipping the speculative `tickRecipeQueue` wrapper avoided baking in a default (outcomes-as-array? event-log-append? fail-fast-on-missing-building?) that the orchestrator will want to decide per-context.
  - `RecipeTickOutcome` is a discriminated union tagged on `status`, with three arms: `produced` (carries sorted `consumed` + `produced` ingredients so the event log can render "Sawmill: 1 timber ‚Üí 1 planks"), `missing-building` (carries the required `BuildingType` so the UI can render "Forge required"), `insufficient-inputs` (carries a sorted `missing: readonly { resource, required, available }[]` so the UI can render "Short 2 timber, 1 fibre"). Sorted output lists are a conscious parity guard ‚Äî matches the `CargoHold.toJSON` / `FactionVisibility.toJSON` / `DirectionLayer.toJSON` determinism pattern so two colonies that queued the same recipes in different input orders produce byte-identical event-log snapshots. The `missing` sort test uses a synthetic two-input recipe shape (built at runtime as a `RecipeDefinition`-typed literal) rather than extending the real registry ‚Äî the registry scope stays locked to current consumers while the sort guarantee is still exercised.
  - Content mirror stayed thin. `packages/content/src/resources.ts` adds a `ResourceEntry` with `{ id, name, summary, description }` ‚Äî no mirrored `inputs` / `building` / `output` rule stats, because a single tooltip read of a *resource* wants the flavour (what is timber, what does a forge turn salvage into) not the chain table. Recipe flavour surfaces later when a task actually renders the chain UI ‚Äî keeping the mirror minimal now avoids a `RESOURCES` vs `RECIPES` drift-detection test before the UI needs either. The id-set invariant (`mirrors the core ResourceType id set`) hard-codes the six strings (content cannot import core) and will update in lock-step when the registry grows ‚Äî same BUILDINGS / TILE_YIELDS precedent established in TASK-040 / TASK-042.
