- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/61 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: core=474 (was 448 ‚Äî +26 new in `src/profession/profession-type.test.ts` covering: registry membership for the seven STORY-25 ids, uniqueness, kebab-case invariant, `isProfessionType` accept + reject; `getProfessionYieldMultiplier` Deckhand-baseline-1.0-for-every-resource, Quartermaster‚Üíprovisions only, Cartographer‚Üísalvage only, Shipwright‚Üíplanks, Gunner‚Üíforgework, unknown-resource fallback to 1, finite-and-‚â•1 invariant across every (profession √ó resource) pair; `getProfessionBuildingMultiplier` Deckhand-baseline-1.0-for-every-building, Shipwright‚Üíshipyard 1.25 + sawmill 1.15 + tavern 1.0, Gunner‚Üígun-deck 1.25 + forge 1.15, Scholar‚Üístudy-hall, Loremaster‚Üíchapel-of-the-kraken, Quartermaster‚Üíwarehouse + fish-market, finite-and-‚â•1 invariant across every (profession √ó building) pair; `applyProfessionBonusToYield` Deckhand-pass-through on Island, Quartermaster scales `provisions: 4 ‚Üí 5`, Quartermaster does not scale `timber` on a mixed tile, Cartographer scales floating-city salvage, drops floor-to-zero entries (1 √ó 1.25 floors to 1, kept), stable alphabetical key order for save-format determinism, empty-input pass-through), content=94 (was 86 ‚Äî +8 new `professions.test.ts` covering: registry exposes seven entries, unique kebab-case ids, non-empty name/summary/description with description-longer-than-summary, hard-coded id-set mirror matching core's ProfessionType, `isProfessionEntryId` accept + reject, `getProfession` hit + TypeError path), web=290 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged)

- Review proposed: pending (Step 15 ‚Äî will fire after deploy if streak ‚â• 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:32431556cd126e2087923e4199708120e1216c7e0dca4be3ae41d4fef38c4cc7, config sha256:d58e3df36db9007a87b4bbc17dd416715db530b2d903d097582d67cb96147079). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. Pure-TS additions to `packages/core` + `packages/content` ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Scope-locked the registry to two scalar lookups + one composed primitive. `ProfessionType` ships the seven STORY-25 ids plus three exports: `getProfessionYieldMultiplier(profession, resourceId): number` (per-resource scalar, defaulting to 1.0), `getProfessionBuildingMultiplier(profession, buildingType): number` (per-building scalar, defaulting to 1.0), and `applyProfessionBonusToYield(base, profession): TileYield` (the composed primitive that walks a base-yield vector and applies per-resource bonuses with floor-and-drop semantics matching `scaleTileYield`). Resisted introducing a Crew entity that owns `profession` + `training-in-progress` even though the task description names both ‚Äî per CLAUDE.md "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection," Crew ownership belongs to a future crew-roster task that will hold the actual collection (Colony.crew is `Set<CrewId>` opaque-string today). The scalar lookups + composed primitive are the verbs; "for each crew on a tile, scale its yield contribution" is the orchestration verb that lives with the iterator.
  - Did NOT generalise `scaleTileYield` to accept per-resource multipliers. The existing `scaleTileYield(base, scalarMultiplier)` signature in `tile-yield.ts` (TASK-042) takes one scalar that scales every entry uniformly ‚Äî appropriate for whole-tile multipliers (a future weather modifier, a colony-wide bonus). Profession bonuses are per-resource (Quartermaster +25% to provisions only) so a uniform-scalar wrapper would mis-model the rule. Added `applyProfessionBonusToYield` as a sibling primitive instead: same floor-and-drop arithmetic, same alphabetical key sort for save-format determinism, but each entry is scaled by its own per-resource multiplier. Composing the two later (apply profession bonus, then scale by weather) is just function composition. This avoids hidden behaviour change in `scaleTileYield` callers (TASK-042 added it expecting whole-vector semantics).
  - Used the `Partial<Record<BuildingType, number>>` shape for the per-building bonus table. The yield bonus table is `Readonly<Record<string, number>>` because resource ids are still opaque strings (`ResourceId = string`, the registry-tightening cascade was deferred in TASK-044 for index-signature reasons). The building bonus table can use the narrowed type because `BuildingType` is a const-object string-literal union with no index-signature consumers in the bonus path. Mixed shapes are fine ‚Äî the consumer-facing API is two `getProfession*Multiplier(...)` lookups that both return `number`, so the internal table shape is implementation detail.
  - Content mirror stayed thin and parallel to RESOURCES / BUILDINGS / TILE_YIELDS. `packages/content/src/professions.ts` adds `ProfessionEntry` with `{ id, name, summary, description }` only ‚Äî no mirrored multiplier values. The numeric stats live in core where the rule reads them; the flavour copy lives in content where the HUD reads it. Per CLAUDE.md "Rule-relevant stats live in `@colonize/core`; descriptive / flavour stats live in `@colonize/content`." Decided NOT to duplicate the multiplier table on the content side even though TASK-027 / ship-class duplicates `baseMovement` between core + content for tooltip-stat rendering ‚Äî the ship-class duplication is justified because tooltip rendering wants the full stat block, but the profession tooltip only wants the *name of the bonused resource / building* ("Boosts provisions yield"), not the multiplier value, and that name is already in the `summary` string. If a future tooltip wants "+25%" rendered explicitly it can call into core's `getProfessionYieldMultiplier` from the consumer side (web ‚Üí core is a valid edge per the dependency-direction rule); content doesn't need to mirror the number until that demand exists.
  - Exhaustive `switch` with no `default` in both multiplier lookups ‚Äî caught one drift case during scaffolding when I first listed only six profession arms. TS pinned the missing case at compile time (per CLAUDE.md "Consume save-format const-object unions via an exhaustive `switch`"). The internal table assertion (`Readonly<Record<ProfessionType, ...>>`) catches the same drift symmetrically ‚Äî adding a new ProfessionType requires both a table entry and a switch case, and either omission fails the build.

### Run [2026-04-22 10:14]
- Task: TASK-047 ‚Äî HomePort entity + price model
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/62 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: core=512 (was 474 ‚Äî +38 new in `src/homeport/homeport.test.ts` covering: construction (id / faction / sorted `tradedResources` / `trades` membership / zero-default `netVolume` / explicit-seed-with-zero-drop / 7-arm `it.each` rejection matrix for empty id, empty faction, empty basePrices, fractional price, price below `MIN_MID_PRICE`, price above `MAX_MID_PRICE`, empty resource id, plus untraded-netVolume and fractional-netVolume rejection); price queries (basePrice, midPrice = base when zero volume, sellPrice = mid + SPREAD, buyBackPrice = mid - SPREAD, untraded-resource throws on every query); price ‚Üî volume coupling (sale drops mid by 1 every `PRICE_VOLUME_STEP` units, purchase raises by same step, sub-step volume does not yet shift, sale + offsetting purchase clears netVolume to zero, mid clamped at `MIN_MID_PRICE` floor under massive sale + at `MAX_MID_PRICE` ceiling under massive purchase, `buyBack < sell` and `sell - buyBack === 2 * SPREAD` invariant tested across ¬±50, ¬±7, ¬±1, 0, 1000); mutator validation (zero / negative / fractional qty rejected on both record* methods, untraded resource rejected on both); toJSON / fromJSON (round-trip with non-zero netVolume preserves derived midPrice, sorted-keys determinism across reordered seeds and reordered mutations, JSON-text-lossless, `fromJSON` rejects non-object / null basePrices / null netVolume, revived port is independent of source ‚Äî large mutation on source does not affect revived), content=99 (was 94 ‚Äî +5 new in `src/homeport-prices.test.ts` covering: every-faction-pricing-every-resource invariant via id-set comparison against `FACTIONS` and `RESOURCES`, `MIN_MID_PRICE`-to-`MAX_MID_PRICE` integer-bounds invariant across every (faction √ó resource) pair, `getHomePortStartingPrices` happy-path returning a populated table, `getHomePortStartingPrices` throws on unknown faction id), web=290 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged)
- Files changed: packages/core/src/homeport/{homeport,index}.ts + homeport.test.ts, packages/core/src/index.ts (re-exports), packages/content/src/homeport-prices.ts + test, packages/content/src/index.ts (re-export), roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 474 ‚Üí 512, content 94 ‚Üí 99, all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: pending (Step 15 ‚Äî will fire after deploy if streak ‚â• 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:3bc521836c14c4b6a24230919f6282459e99135a68ac120ac483c40e35deda5d, config sha256:86d90a49cb25123c8d0e45606d72ac136177c14900a4ebff48e16e2c278ee14b). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. `colonize:previous` tag preserved for rollback. Pure-TS additions to `packages/core` + `packages/content` ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Modeled the volume-coupled price as a *signed net-volume integer per good* + a single integer-divide derivation, rather than tracking sell/buy histories or float-elastic curves. The state surface is just `Map<ResourceId, number>` (sales positive, purchases negative) and `midPrice = clamp(basePrice - floor(netVolume / PRICE_VOLUME_STEP), MIN_MID_PRICE, MAX_MID_PRICE)`. Integer arithmetic everywhere is a deliberate save-format-parity guard ‚Äî float multipliers would risk byte-divergence across 64-bit / 32-bit FPUs (TASK-022 fog overlay hit a similar issue with float alphas, fixed by integer fixed-point). The `floor` + `step` pair gives a discrete "shifts mid by 1 every `PRICE_VOLUME_STEP` units traded" feel without needing a `Math.round` tiebreak, and it composes cleanly with the spread (`sell = mid + SPREAD`, `buyBack = mid - SPREAD`) so `buyBack < sell` is a structural invariant, not a runtime check. Considered the alternative shape ‚Äî separate `sellPrice` / `buyBackPrice` per-good as independent stored fields ‚Äî but rejected: that would let drift accumulate (sell ‚â• buyBack could fail after enough mutations) and the spread-as-derived form is what naturally enforces the task description's "Buy-back prices < sell prices (spread)" requirement.
  - Used opaque-string `ResourceId` rather than tightening to `ResourceType` in the HomePort signatures, matching the deferred-tightening lesson from TASK-044 / CargoHold. The `_basePrices` and `_netVolume` maps are keyed by `ResourceId` (= `string`); the runtime guards (`assertNonEmptyString` on every mutator, `_basePrices.has(resourceId)` membership check) are what actually protect the save format. Tightening the alias to `ResourceType` would cascade into `Record<ResourceType, number>` index-signature traps and force a content-side type change in `homeport-prices.ts` that doesn't currently exist (content can't import core). The wire-level kebab-case strings round-trip identically either way.
  - Shipped `HomePort` as the entity primitive only; deferred *every* orchestration verb. Per CLAUDE.md "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection," the primitive exposes `recordPlayerSale` / `recordPlayerPurchase` (volume mutators) plus `sellPrice` / `buyBackPrice` / `midPrice` / `netVolume` (queries) ‚Äî no `executeTrade(cargoHold, resourceId, qty)`, no `tickToEquilibrium()`, no per-turn-decay, no per-faction iteration. The trade-screen task (TASK-048) will compose these primitives ("read sellPrice, debit player gold, transferTo CargoHold, recordPlayerPurchase") in whatever ordering its orchestrator wants. Resisted adding `executeBuy` / `executeSell` convenience methods even though they're 4-line wrappers ‚Äî coupling the primitive to gold (which doesn't exist as a core concept yet) or to a `CargoHold` source argument would bake in cross-system assumptions the orchestrator should own. The "no equilibrium tick" decision in particular is conscious: the task description says "moves inversely to volume sold" but says nothing about whether prices drift back when trade pauses, so that's an orchestration choice (per-turn `floor(netVolume * 0.95)`? linear -1 toward zero? no decay at all?) the trade task or a future market-tick task can pick. The primitive just records the volume.
  - Per-faction starting prices live in `packages/content/src/homeport-prices.ts` as `Readonly<Record<PlayableFactionId, Readonly<Record<ResourceEntryId, number>>>>` plus a `getHomePortStartingPrices(factionId)` lookup. Numbers reflect each faction's economic profile (OTK premium for sacred salvage + cheap kelp-derived fibre, Ironclad cheap forgework + pricey provisions, Phantom cheap raid-loot salvage + scarce provisions, Bloodborne cheap shipyard planks + pricey timber consumption) ‚Äî content can be re-tuned without touching core's price-model arithmetic. Mirrored the resources / buildings / tile-yields / professions content pattern: invariant test asserts every playable faction prices every `ResourceEntryId` and every value falls in core's `[MIN_MID_PRICE, MAX_MID_PRICE]` range. The faction-id √ó resource-id mirror is hard-coded (content can't import core) and updates in lock-step when either registry grows ‚Äî same lock-step drift-detection precedent as `resources.test.ts` mirroring `ResourceType`.
  - Validation guard `assertBasePrice` is a *primitive-private* helper (defined at the bottom of `homeport.ts` alongside `assertNonEmptyString` and `assertPositiveQty`), not a shared utility. Mirrors the local-helper pattern Colony / CargoHold / LegendaryFleet established. Decided NOT to extract a shared `packages/core/src/util/assert.ts` even though three primitives now have near-identical `assertNonEmptyString` ‚Äî the duplication is six lines per module and extracting would create a transitive dependency that complicates the import graph (and the `packages/core/src/util/` directory doesn't exist yet, so creating it would establish a precedent the next primitive would have to follow). Per CLAUDE.md Tier 1 "Three similar lines is better than a premature abstraction" ‚Äî six is still fine.

- Outcome: success

- Files changed: apps/web/src/trade/{trade-math,trade-math.test,TradeScreen,TradeScreen.test}.ts{,x} + TradeScreen.module.css, apps/web/src/store/game.ts + game.test.ts, apps/web/src/colony/ColonyOverlay.tsx + ColonyOverlay.test.tsx, apps/web/src/App.tsx + App.test.tsx, packages/core/src/index.ts (re-exports), roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md

- Review proposed: pending (Step 15 ‚Äî will fire after deploy if streak ‚â• 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:0d6242f1f5a39ff249990c690036fc580515644e3f56f112ce06e091dcc4a30a, config sha256:365371098aac1a794cf5d1b793c4ec6bde548ade8f4a9f4f51812653f1fff610). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Pure-web change in apps/web + opaque store-slice additions ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Scope-locked to the UI surface only ‚Äî deliberately did NOT bootstrap the HomePort roster from `HOMEPORT_STARTING_PRICES`, did NOT introduce a ship-at-colony detector in core, and did NOT add a coin ledger. Per CLAUDE.md "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection," HomePort instances are seeded by the spawning flow (a later task) ‚Äî tests pump the store via `setHomePort(factionId, port)` directly. The "ship at colony tile" check is a 6-line loop in `ColonyOverlay.tsx#findTradableShip` that filters the existing `units` roster by faction + type + `position.{x,y}` equality ‚Äî no core-level roster-iterator primitive invented. Running profit is a *preview* figure (live recompute from slider state), not a cumulative session P&L requiring a coin column in the store; no coin ledger gets introduced speculatively.
  - `'trade'` is a *terminal* screen in the zustand screen-literal union (not an overlay on top of `'colony'`). Per CLAUDE.md the terminal-vs-overlay split hinges on "does Phaser state need to survive?" ‚Äî the trade screen pauses player actions anyway, the colony overlay underneath is already a modal that swallows input, and the Phaser `GameScene` keeps running in the background (not paused). So mounting trade as its own `App.tsx` dispatch case + unmounting the ColonyOverlay root is the cleaner shape; closing routes the screen back to `'colony'` (not `'game'`), giving the player the Esc-colony ‚Üí Esc-game ‚Üí return-to-map muscle memory the pause overlay already trained.
  - Pure-sibling `trade-math.ts` even though the pure-sibling rule is narrowly about Phaser. React tests don't suffer Phaser's module-load probes, so `TradeScreen.test.tsx` could freely import the component. But the arithmetic (unit-price selection per qty sign, line totals, net-coin aggregation) deserves isolated tests ‚Äî they read clearer with plain HomePort instances than with slider-fires-events-and-we-assert-rendered-text. Same two-module shape as `camera-controls.ts` + `game-scene.ts` / `fog-overlay-state.ts` + `fog-overlay.ts`, just motivated by testing ergonomics rather than the jsdom/Phaser boundary.
  - `commitTrade` is atomic at the zustand-set boundary ‚Äî it reads the HomePort JSON + ship JSON, runs every line through `port.recordPlayerSale` / `recordPlayerPurchase` + cargo delta in-process, then produces one `set(...)` call with both new slices. Mid-trade a `homePort.netVolume(resource)` can go backwards (a sell then a buy in the same cart), but external observers never see a "ship lost 3 timber but netVolume still 0" race because the snapshot writes together. Resisted splitting into two actions (update port, update cargo) ‚Äî split writes would race if a re-render interleaved.
  - Silent-ignore on sell-exceeds-hold rather than throw. The slider max is already `min=-shipQty`, so an exceeding-sell should be unreachable through the UI ‚Äî the guard is defensive against a future caller (hotkey, AI, save-reload) that doesn't respect the slider bound. Per CLAUDE.md "trust internal code and framework guarantees" we normally wouldn't validate, but `commitTrade` straddles the store boundary (user-ish input path: slider values feed the store) so a cheap clamp-and-skip is reasonable. Chose skip-the-line over throw-the-batch to keep a partial trade valid when just one line is malformed.
  - Running profit is shown per-*cart*, not session-cumulative. Read the task description's "running profit" as "what would I net if I confirmed this cart right now" ‚Äî matches the slider UX where dragging sliders updates the figure live. A session-cumulative view would need a separate `sessionProfit: number` store slice that resets on `openTradeSession` / `closeTradeSession`, plus an `appendProfit(delta)` action called from `commitTrade`. Decided that's orchestration (whoever owns the trade-session lifecycle) rather than primitive, and the single live-cart figure is what the sliders visually support. If a future task wants the cumulative version it's a 3-line store addition.

- Files changed: apps/web/src/transfer/{transfer-math,transfer-math.test}.ts + {CargoTransferScreen,CargoTransferScreen.test}.tsx + CargoTransferScreen.module.css, apps/web/src/store/game.ts + game.test.ts, apps/web/src/colony/ColonyOverlay.tsx + ColonyOverlay.test.tsx, apps/web/src/App.tsx + App.test.tsx, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (web 327 ‚Üí 366, all other counts steady)
- Review proposed: pending (Step 15 ‚Äî will fire after deploy if streak ‚â• 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:d756a314031a655fd589e3a1f9654f3a2a9c0d7748ba74e08773648eb0ef47da, config sha256:6425398a95d2340deff288297a6c58d68158f36ad261ae8e21f75bdddde7d06d). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Pure-web change in apps/web ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Scope-locked to the minimum primitives needed for player-facing load/unload ‚Äî deliberately did NOT touch `@colonize/core` even though the task lists `[web, core]`. Cargo and colony stocks are both `CargoHoldJSON` already, the screen + store action work with those JSON shapes directly, and adding a `Colony.deliverFrom(unit, line)` core method would have invented an orchestration verb that lives more naturally with the roster owner (a future task that mediates ship-at-colony entry events). Per CLAUDE.md "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection" ‚Äî `CargoHold.transferTo(other)` from TASK-034 is the cargo-side primitive, but it transfers *all* contents in one go, while manual load/unload is a per-resource per-quantity verb owned by the UI task. The atomic store-set boundary is sufficient for the consistency guarantee a single screen needs.
  - `'transfer'` is a *terminal* screen in the zustand screen-literal union, parallel to `'trade'` rather than overlay-on-`'colony'`. Same reasoning as TASK-048's trade-screen choice: closing the colony overlay would unmount the work-tile drag-and-drop state, but transferring cargo doesn't need the colony tile grid in the background, and the round-trip Esc-transfer ‚Üí Esc-colony ‚Üí Esc-game muscle memory is what the player already has from trade. Mounting transfer as its own dispatch case in `App.tsx` keeps the routing literal-union pattern uniform ‚Äî every player-action screen owns its own root component.
  - Renamed `findTradableShip` ‚Üí `findFriendlyShipAt` in ColonyOverlay because the predicate (faction match + ship type + colony-tile position) is now used by both the trade panel and the transfer panel. The "tradable" qualifier was always misleading ‚Äî every ship can dock; the eligibility check is purely about location and ownership. Resisted extracting the helper to a shared util module ‚Äî it's ten lines, single-call-site-per-panel, and lives next to its only consumers. Per CLAUDE.md Tier 1 "Three similar lines is better than a premature abstraction" ‚Äî and renaming-in-place keeps the dependency graph flat.
  - Pure-sibling `transfer-math.ts` for the row-generation step even though the React tree could test it inline. Mirror of TASK-048's `trade-math.ts` decision: small pure functions are easier to read and faster to fail when extracted, and the alphabetical-sort + key-union arithmetic deserves its own micro-tests independent of slider rendering. The pure-sibling rule is narrowly about Phaser isolation, but the same shape pays off whenever there's non-trivial pure logic adjacent to a stateful component.
  - Clamp-loads-and-unloads in `commitCargoTransfer` rather than throw or no-op the whole batch. Sliders enforce the bounds (`min=-shipQty`, `max=+colonyQty`) but a hotkey, AI orchestrator, or save-reload could pass an out-of-range qty later. Same defensive posture as `commitTrade`'s `if (sellQty > have) continue` ‚Äî clip to the available source and proceed with the rest of the cart, so one malformed line doesn't drop ten valid ones. Per-line clamping also lets us composite a partial transfer cleanly: "load 99 timber" silently becomes "load all available timber" rather than a runtime error.
  - Resources only ‚Äî artifacts deferred to a future task. CargoHold.artifacts is a Set of opaque ids representing unique items (Kraken Totem, Salt Charm); they don't have a quantity to slide and they couple to colony bonuses (per TASK-034 lesson "Unique artifacts produce permanent colony bonuses"). The transfer UI for an artifact is fundamentally different ‚Äî checkbox per artifact, with the colony's bonus state visible ‚Äî and its logic depends on the artifact-bonus task that hasn't shipped. Including it speculatively would either (a) ship a checkbox UI that doesn't yet trigger any bonus, masking the future feature, or (b) hard-code a bonus path that the real task would have to reshape. Better to ship the resources-only scope cleanly and add an artifacts row when the bonus orchestration task lands ‚Äî the screen's row-per-resource-id structure trivially extends to a row-per-artifact-id sister panel.
  - Made the transfer panel visible at *every* colony, regardless of home-port status. The trade panel correctly hides without a home-port (because there are no prices), but cargo transfer doesn't need a price model ‚Äî it's a free move between two storage spots the player owns. A player should be able to ferry timber from a producing colony to a building one even if neither is a home-port. This decouples the load/unload feature (TASK-049 STORY-27 inter-colony hauling) from the trade-economy feature (TASK-048 STORY-26 home-port trade) so they remain orthogonal ‚Äî the player can build a hauling chain across new colonies without first earning a home-port.

### Run [2026-04-22 13:14]
- Task: TASK-053 ‚Äî Combat resolver in packages/core
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/65 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: web=366 (unchanged), core=543 (was 512 ‚Äî +31 new in `src/combat/resolve.test.ts` covering: input validation (6 ‚Äî hull-zero attacker/defender rejected, non-function rng rejected, negative-hull combatant rejected, hull-exceeds-max rejected, empty id rejected); broadside (7 ‚Äî opening volley + return fire shape, DefenderSunk skips return fire, AttackerSunk on lethal return volley, Inconclusive when both survive, hull never goes negative, zero-gun attacker still triggers return volley, deterministic outcome for fixed RNG sequence); boarding (6 ‚Äî boarding-round events emitted per round, DefenderCaptured when defender crew zeros first, AttackerCaptured when attacker crew zeros first, Inconclusive at the round cap with non-breaking crews, crew counts never go negative, hull preserved during boarding); ramming (5 ‚Äî single ram-impact event, DefenderSunk when only defender zeroes, AttackerSunk when only attacker zeroes, MutualSunk when both zero, Inconclusive on glancing hit); fleeing (6 ‚Äî AttackerFled on speed-favoured low roll, Inconclusive on speed-favoured high roll, AttackerSunk if parting volley wipes the fleer, single flee-attempt event, defender hull preserved, zero-pursuer-movement does not divide by zero); replay determinism (1 ‚Äî identical RNG sequence yields equal CombatOutcome across all four actions)), content=99 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged)
- Files changed: packages/core/src/combat/{combat-action,combat-event,combat-result,combatant,resolve,index,resolve.test}.ts (new module), packages/core/src/index.ts (re-exports for `CombatActionType` / `CombatResult` / `Combatant` / `CombatContext` / `CombatOutcome` / `CombatEvent` / `CombatSide` / `assertValidCombatant` / `resolveCombat` / arrays / guards), roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 512 ‚Üí 543, every other count steady)
- Review proposed: true ‚Äî https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/66 (5 consecutive successes since PR #57 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-045 ‚Üí TASK-047 ‚Üí TASK-048 ‚Üí TASK-049 ‚Üí TASK-053 ‚Äî threshold hit; /autonomous-review drafted 3 refinements covering pure-sibling extension to non-trivial React component logic, multi-slice zustand mutations atomic in single set(), and clamp-and-skip on out-of-range qty at the zustand store boundary)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:be0cb65cef37e1023cc26f5d058dcb0b767921dd148120a6cc1e4c22fec3757e, config sha256:69aca3806d56e989d6828e23c80a383e68425effe5d7ac7999371e3c6c477c73). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Pure-core change in `packages/core/src/combat/` ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Scope-locked to the *primitive* per the "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection" rule. The combat resolver exposes `resolveCombat(attacker, defender, context)` and stops there ‚Äî it does NOT mutate `Unit` state, does NOT register a TurnManager phase hook, does NOT iterate a fleet roster, does NOT write encounter outcomes back to a save-format encounter log. Every one of those is a wiring decision owned by the orchestrator that introduces the encounter-detection collection (likely the EPIC-08 ground-combat or encounter-event task). A na√Øve implementation would have grown a `Unit.takeDamage(amount)` method and a `combat:resolved` bus event; both would couple the resolver to whichever roster shape today's task happens to need and would force a rewrite when the encounter task lands with its own ideas about turn-interleaving and side-by-side fleets.
  - Scalar-seam pattern for combatant stats. The resolver does NOT look up `getShipClass(id)` from `packages/content` ‚Äî `Combatant` carries hull/guns/crew/movement (and their maxes) directly, supplied by the caller. Three reasons: (a) `packages/core` is forbidden from importing `@colonize/content` by the dependency-direction rule, (b) the legendary-ship roster (`OTK_LEGENDARY_SHIP_SLOTS`) is a *parallel* registry whose redeemed instances should slot into combat with the same shape as a regular ship class ‚Äî the scalar-seam consumes either source uniformly, and (c) intermediate combat states (mid-skirmish, between rounds) can't be represented by a registry id alone, so passing an immutable snapshot of *current* numbers is what the resolver actually needs. This mirrors `scaleTileYield(base, multiplier)` (TASK-042) and `buildingEffort = sum(def.cost values)` (TASK-041).
  - Seeded RNG passed in as a closure (`rng: () => number`), not a numeric seed. Same pattern `RumourTile.resolve(rng, options)` (TASK-031) and `generateMap` (TASK-019) already use ‚Äî `mulberry32(seed)` lives at the orchestrator boundary, the called primitive only knows it has a function returning [0,1). This keeps the resolver agnostic to the PRNG family (mulberry today, splitmix or xoshiro tomorrow) and lets tests inject deterministic sequences without re-implementing `mulberry32` per test file. `rngFromSequence([...])` in the test file is the canonical fixture and explicitly throws when the resolver consumes more rolls than the test seeded ‚Äî so adding a roll to the resolver without updating tests fails loudly.
  - Typed event log per outcome (`CombatEvent` discriminated union: broadside-volley / boarding-round / ram-impact / flee-attempt). Two consumers benefit: (a) the cinematic UI (TASK-054) animates the events without re-implementing the math, (b) replay-determinism tests (and the eventual save-format replay system) can assert event sequences cell-by-cell rather than just final-state equality. Resisted shipping a "narrative tag" string per event ‚Äî the cinematic owns its own copy / surface, and a free-form string would invite the resolver to encode UI-specific subtypes ("graze" vs "broadside-hit") that consumers would then parse. The structured event payload pins the *what happened* without prescribing the *how it should be drawn*.
  - MutualSunk-via-boarding deliberately unreachable. With the asymmetric initiator factor (0.12 attacker √ó 0.10 defender), whichever crew reaches zero first reaches it *strictly* first ‚Äî no single-round mutual zeroing math holds at any realistic crew size. The branch is kept in the result-classifier for cleanliness (degenerate inputs with both crews already zero classify cleanly) and a code comment names the reason. Ram is the realistic MutualSunk path and is well-covered by tests; boarding's character-of-engagement is "one side breaks, the other captures" ‚Äî Inconclusive is the natural draw outcome when both crews stay non-empty at the round cap.
  - Const-object enums (`CombatActionType`, `CombatResult`) follow the save-format-bound string-literal pattern even though combat outcomes are not (yet) part of the wire format. The CombatOutcome shape is consumed by the cinematic UI today and by the eventual encounter-replay log tomorrow ‚Äî having the same identifiers as the wire format from day one means no rename-via-migration when replay lands. Switch-on-action in `resolveCombat` has no `default` case so adding a new `CombatActionType` (boarding-with-grappling-hooks, parley, fire-ship) fails the build until every per-action sub-resolver picks behaviour. Same writer-half/reader-half split that `tileCost` (TASK-028) uses for `TileType`.

### Run [2026-04-22 14:23]
- Task: TASK-054 ‚Äî Combat UI: cinematic resolver + log
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/67 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: web=402 (was 366 ‚Äî +36 new across four surfaces: +18 in `src/combat/cinematic-state.test.ts` covering empty timelines / sequential layout with 200ms gap / per-kind descriptions + focus for broadside-volley(attacker|defender), boarding-round, ram-impact, flee-attempt(success|fail) / activeBeat null-before-zero + first-at-zero + previous-during-gap + switch-at-startMs + last-past-end + empty / revealedBeats accumulation / describeResult per CombatResult member; +12 in `src/combat/CombatOverlay.test.tsx` covering null-when-no-outcome, mount on outcome, Skip‚ÜîContinue toggle, log reveal on Skip, result line on Skip, beat-label hidden on finish, attacker-focus active during attacker broadside, focus-clear on finish, dismiss-on-Continue, zero-event outcome ‚Üí finished controls, time-advance reveals successive log entries (`vi.useFakeTimers`), restart playback when a new outcome opens; +4 in `src/store/game.test.ts` combat-outcome slice subsuite (starts null, showCombatOutcome stores, dismissCombatOutcome clears, reset clears); +2 in `src/App.test.tsx` combat-overlay dispatch subsuite (mount when an outcome is set, not mounted otherwise)), core=543 (unchanged), content=99 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged)

- Regression alert: false (web 366 ‚Üí 402, every other count steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=1 since PR #66 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:0f2efd4746007063ad9f677e81bdc9c0582d8d4e789320274567de97ba9aacc7, config sha256:af3a1c5356a793d64504e58987f09152b8cab0bb960013b4088683b121089c23). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Pure-web change in apps/web ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Self-mounting overlay (RumourRevealModal pattern) NOT a new screen literal in the zustand `Screen` union. Considered adding `'combat'` parallel to `'pause'` / `'colony'` / `'trade'` / `'transfer'`, but combat happens *during* a turn while the player is on whatever screen they were on ‚Äî hard-binding it to a `screen === 'combat'` dispatch case would force the orchestrator to remember the previous screen and route back to it on dismiss. The `combatOutcome !== null` slice in the store is the single source of truth; CombatOverlay self-mounts and the underlying screen (game, colony, trade) stays untouched. This matches the rumour-reveal modal which has the same "happens-during-an-action" semantics. The trade-off vs PauseOverlay's `screen === 'pause'` shape: pause needs to suspend every other interaction (so a screen flip is the right granularity), combat needs to overlay the current view without disrupting the underlying screen state. Different problem, different shape.
  - Pure-sibling `cinematic-state.ts` even though we're not in Phaser. The pure-sibling rule (CLAUDE.md `apps/web/src/game/`) is narrowly framed around Phaser's module-load probes, but the *shape* ‚Äî non-trivial branching logic + state lives in a pure module the React component imports ‚Äî pays off whenever the React tree has timing logic worth testing in isolation. The component test exercises Skip/Continue/dismiss with synchronous fireEvent; the timeline derivation (per-kind durations, active-beat-during-gap, revealed-beats accumulation) is exercised independently with plain values. Mirror of the precedent set by TASK-048's `trade-math.ts` and TASK-049's `transfer-math.ts` ‚Äî not Phaser-driven, just testing-ergonomics-driven.
  - Scope-locked the wire from `resolveCombat` to the overlay to a *single* store action (`showCombatOutcome(outcome)`). Considered (a) adding a `'combat:engagement'` bus event in `@colonize/shared`'s `GameEvents` interface, (b) routing through GameCanvas.useEffect like the colony-selected handler. Both rejected for now ‚Äî `GameEvents` payloads are deliberately primitive (turn numbers, ids, empty objects) and importing `CombatOutcome` from `@colonize/core` into `@colonize/shared` would establish a forbidden cross-package edge (per the dependency-direction rule, `shared` is a peer of `core`, not a dependent). Adding a structurally-equivalent shape inline in `GameEvents` is duplication that the orchestrator task can introduce once it's clear what *exactly* needs the bus seam (the orchestrator might prefer a direct store call). The scoped task ships the *primitive* ‚Äî store action + overlay ‚Äî and leaves the orchestrator wiring (where the engagement is detected, how the resolved outcome flows back to the UI) to the task that introduces encounter detection. Same "ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection" rule.
  - 50ms `setInterval` ticker driven by `Date.now() - startMs`, NOT requestAnimationFrame. Two reasons: (a) `vi.useFakeTimers()` mocks both `setInterval` and `Date.now` cleanly, so the time-advance test can `vi.advanceTimersByTime(1100)` and assert the second log entry materialised ‚Äî would have to fake `requestAnimationFrame` separately and the cadence would still depend on jsdom's frame scheduling, (b) frame-cadence smoothness doesn't matter for an overlay whose only animation is sprite-flash + log-entry-reveal at ~200ms-1000ms granularities. Saving the `Date.now() - elapsed` baseline in a ref instead of recalculating ensures the elapsed counter stays stable across React re-renders (a useState-only approach drifts when a parent re-render forces the effect to re-run mid-cinematic).
  - Per-event-kind playback duration table (`BEAT_DURATION_MS`) keyed by `CombatEvent['kind']`. Three reasons over a single uniform 800ms: (a) ram is visually heavier (impact recoil) so wants 1000ms, (b) boarding rounds are quick exchanges and should snap (600ms), (c) flee is a single-shot animation (700ms is the parting-shot beat). The 200ms inter-beat gap leaves space for the active-side highlight to release before the next side flares ‚Äî without it the cinematic looks like one continuous flash. Table-not-switch because durations are flat constants the consumer reads, not per-case branching logic ‚Äî same shape as the `BEAT_DURATION_MS` precedent could later use to feed a sound-effects orchestrator (per-kind sfx asset id) when audio lands.
  - Inline-divs-not-Phaser-sprites for the cinematic visual. Per CLAUDE.md "Heraldic / crest visuals are inline SVG until the art epic ships" ‚Äî the same logic applies to the combat cinematic. Pre-art-epic, two coloured rectangles with `transform` + `box-shadow` for the active-side flash is enough to communicate "attacker shoots ‚Üí defender hit"; switching to Phaser sprites later is a localized swap inside `CombatOverlay.tsx` (or a render-target migration into `GameScene` if combat goes inline-on-the-map) without touching the cinematic-state primitives, the store action, or the test surface. Adding sprite assets now would force a tile-atlas regeneration for assets that are placeholder-quality and would trigger a packed-output diff every cycle.
  - Roadmap-housekeeping commit before the implementation commit cleaned up TASK-049's two-line YAML duplicate-key residue (lines 1067-1068: `last_attempted: null` + `attempt_count: 0` overrode the successful PR-64 attempt's `"2026-04-22T12:00:00Z"` + `1`). The validator's `roadmap/yaml-lite.mjs` parser silently last-wins on duplicate keys so the corruption was invisible to CI but breaks any standard parser (js-yaml threw on it during selection). Bundled with the task because both touch `roadmap.yml` and the cleanup is two lines ‚Äî a separate housekeeping PR would have been disproportionate ceremony. Called out as a separate commit + in the PR body so the diff is reviewable.

+27 in `src/combat/ground-resolve.test.ts` covering input validation (hp-zero attacker/defender, non-function rng, negative-hp, hp-exceeds-max, non-ground UnitType), RPS (marines‚Üípikemen + dragoons‚Üímarines + pikemen‚Üídragoons advantage, reverse-of-cycle disadvantage, same-type neutral), engage outcomes (attacker-volley + defender-counter shape, DefenderSunk skips counter, AttackerSunk on lethal counter, Inconclusive when both survive, hp never goes negative, zero-attack still triggers counter), terrain modifiers (per-terrain modifier exposed on outcome, FloatingCity 1.5 < RedTide 0.75 damage ordering via shared rng seed, getTerrainDefenderModifier returns 1.0 for Ocean/RayonPassage/FataMorgana), flee (AttackerFled on speed-favoured low-roll, Inconclusive on high-roll, AttackerSunk when parting volley wipes fleer, single flee-attempt event, defender-hp preserved), replay determinism across both actions; - CI note: initial push failed typecheck because `ground-resolve.test.ts` imported `GROUND_CLASSES` from `@colonize/content` ‚Äî a forbidden cross-workspace edge (packages/core must not depend on packages/content per the dependency-direction rule). Locally the symlinks + prior `tsc -b` output masked the error; CI ran clean and surfaced it. Fix commit `fc6244e` dropped the import + the single cross-workspace consistency test (each side still has its own ordering invariants); core count 596 ‚Üí 595.
- Deploy: success (rolling strategy, healthcheck 200 OK on attempt 2, URL colonize.blacksail.dev)
- Lessons learned:
  - Separate `GroundCombatant` struct + `GroundCombatActionType` + `GroundCombatEvent` union rather than widening the existing `Combatant` / `CombatActionType` / `CombatEvent` in `resolve.ts`. Two reasons over extension: (a) naval combat's `hull` / `guns` / `crew` / `maxCrew` / `movement` / `maxMovement` stat axes are semantically different from ground combat's `hp` / `attack` / `defense` ‚Äî squeezing them into one struct forces consumers to branch on `kind` to read the right fields and makes `assertValidCombatant` either too-loose (allow both stat-sets) or too-strict (reject-on-missing for the other mode). (b) TypeScript exhaustiveness on `CombatEvent['kind']` is the contract cinematics + audit logs depend on (TASK-054's `BEAT_DURATION_MS` + `describeEvent` table are keyed by `kind`) ‚Äî adding `'ground-volley'` / `'ground-flee-attempt'` to the naval union would silently weaken those consumers' compile errors (a forgotten case falls through to a no-op instead of a red squiggle). Cost of the separation: two parallel resolvers. Benefit: cleaner typing on both sides, cinematic layer can decide *explicitly* whether ground events join the same timeline or get their own CombatOverlay variant when the ground-combat UI task lands.
  - Combatant carries `type: UnitType` but the resolver owns the RPS matrix internally (not the caller). Per the scalar-seam pattern, the caller supplies stats (`attack`, `defense`, `hp`) but the *rule* that marines-beat-pikemen is rule-relevant tuning ‚Äî it belongs in core, not in whichever content-driven multiplier passes through. This contrasts with `resolveCombat` where `guns` / `crew` / `hull` are all caller-supplied and there is no intrinsic RPS layer to maintain. New ground types would live on the `UnitType` registry + `GROUND_UNIT_TYPES` list + the `beats()` switch in `ground-resolve.ts` ‚Äî three touch-points, one PR, compile errors if any is forgotten.
  - Exhaustive switch on `TileType` in `getTerrainDefenderModifier` ‚Äî modulo the `Ocean`/`RayonPassage` case-stack that share a return value ‚Äî follows the CLAUDE.md "consume save-format const-object unions via an exhaustive switch with no `default`" rule even though only a subset of tiles (Island + FloatingCity) ever host live ground combat in the current model. Reason: when a future `TileType` member lands (sky / deep / new island subtype) the author must pick a ground-combat modifier for it, even if the obvious pick is 1.0 ‚Äî silencing the compile error is a decision, not a default. Adding a `default: return 1.0` would hide the decision and defeat the whole point.
  - Embark/disembark shipped as *pure predicates* ‚Äî `canEmbark` / `canDisembark` return `{ok: true} | {ok: false; reason}` but do not mutate anything. Three reasons for predicate-not-mutator: (a) the roster task (which owns `Map<shipId, passengers[]>`) has not yet landed; adding a `Unit.embark(shipId)` method now would force a save-format migration for `UnitJSON` (new nullable `carrier` field) that breaks existing saves for a feature no caller can exercise end-to-end yet. (b) the orchestrator needs to apply *paired* mutations (remove unit from roster + add id to ship's passengers list + spend movement) in one atomic pass so partial failures don't corrupt state ‚Äî splitting the mutation across two entity methods (`unit.embark()` + something on the ship) puts the atomicity burden back on every call site. (c) a pure predicate is exhaustively testable with plain struct literals (no Unit class construction, no map geometry). The primitive the roster task will consume is exactly this predicate; the mutator wraps the check and then commits the state change in one place.
  - `shipCapacity` + `currentPassengerCount` as scalar-seam arguments rather than reading from `SHIP_CLASSES`. The registry does not yet carry a `passengerCapacity` field; adding one speculatively ‚Äî per CLAUDE.md "Trim consumer-specific fields off save-format registries" ‚Äî would either duplicate `crewCapacity` (and force the author to pick a split no consumer has asked for) or be dead flavour until the roster task lands. Threading the scalar through the predicate signature keeps the orchestrator's options open ‚Äî it can source capacity from a new SHIP_CLASSES field, from a per-ship runtime counter, from a hull-damage modifier, without touching `canEmbark` again.

### Run [2026-04-22 16:18]
- Task: TASK-058 ‚Äî Diplomacy actions + relations matrix
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/69 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: core=680 (was 595 ‚Äî +85 across three new suites: +29 in `src/diplomacy/diplomacy-action.test.ts` covering `DiplomacyAction` kebab-case identifier shape + `ALL_DIPLOMACY_ACTIONS` member list + `isDiplomacyAction` narrow/reject matrix, `getDiplomacyActionEffect` per-member effect invariants (integer cooldownTurns > 0, hostile actions produce negative deltas, goodwill actions produce positive deltas, proposals carry a non-zero decline penalty + require acceptance, unilateral actions never require acceptance, alliance harder-to-earn-than-peace ordering on both delta + cooldownTurns), `aiShouldAccept` threshold rule per boundary (propose-peace accepts at score ‚â• -50, propose-alliance accepts at ‚â• 50, unilateral actions always true, rejects non-finite score); +37 in `src/diplomacy/relations-matrix.test.ts` covering constructor defaults + seeded entries + duplicate-pair-order rejection + malformed-seed rejection matrix (out-of-range score, self-pair, empty faction, non-integer, unknown-action cooldown, non-positive cooldown-expiry), `getScore` symmetry + same-faction/empty-id rejection, `shiftScore` symmetric update + clamp-to-max + clamp-to-min + return-value + delta-0-no-create + non-integer rejection, `setScore` out-of-range + exact-boundary accept, cooldown record/clear + active-window inequality (< not ‚â§) + symmetric read + idempotent clear + non-positive expiresOnTurn / unknown action / non-positive currentTurn rejections, `getEntry` null-for-untouched + canonical-pair + cooldowns-omitted-when-empty, serialization entry-sort + byte-identical across mutation orders + cooldown-key sort + round-trip + malformed-fromJSON rejection; +19 in `src/diplomacy/attempt.test.ts` covering unilateral accepted delta + cooldown lock (declare-war), gift always accepts regardless of score, propose-peace acceptance at exact -50 boundary + decline below + decline penalty applied, propose-alliance accept-at-50 + decline-at-49, cooldown locked on accept AND decline, repeat-within-cooldown blocked + score unchanged + cooldownUntil surfaced, retry-at-expiry accepted, orthogonal-action not blocked, cooldown symmetric across (proposer,target)/(target,proposer), same-faction rejected + no state change, invalid-params rejection matrix (non-RelationsMatrix, empty proposer/target, unknown action, non-integer/zero currentTurn, null params)), content=108 (unchanged), web=402 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged)
- Files changed: packages/core/src/diplomacy/{diplomacy-action,diplomacy-action.test,relations-matrix,relations-matrix.test,attempt,attempt.test,index}.ts (new module), packages/core/src/index.ts (re-exports for DiplomacyAction / ALL_DIPLOMACY_ACTIONS / isDiplomacyAction / getDiplomacyActionEffect / aiShouldAccept / DiplomacyActionEffect / RelationsMatrix + MIN/MAX/NEUTRAL_RELATIONS_SCORE / RelationsMatrixJSON / RelationsMatrixInit / RelationsEntryJSON / attemptDiplomacyAction + DiplomacyAttempt{Outcome,Success,Blocked,Invalid,Status,Params}), roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 595 ‚Üí 680, every other count steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=3 since PR #66 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:74e6cb7cb6f50c0d9791f16575dbb7b61bd284e87b2fd81edc1b2430e568da13, config sha256:ac26cd2a376c60f59cad10eefde4dbdf1705e7abd9c78428f2b6bd572a08d4e1). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Pure-core change in packages/core ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Three-file split inside `packages/core/src/diplomacy/` ‚Äî `diplomacy-action.ts` (const-object + effect table + aiShouldAccept), `relations-matrix.ts` (data primitive), `attempt.ts` (orchestrator) ‚Äî rather than one mega-module. Reason: the three files have independent change cadences. Adding a new action is a diplomacy-action.ts-only change (new literal + new switch case + new threshold case ‚Äî TypeScript exhaustiveness pins the three touch-points). Re-tuning a cooldown or threshold is a data edit in the same file. Adding a new *data shape* (say, per-pair event log, or opinion-modifier stack) is a relations-matrix.ts edit that leaves the action table untouched. Adding new attempt semantics (pre-conditions, emit a side-effect event) is attempt.ts-only. Monolith would have been ~600 lines of heterogeneous concerns; the split mirrors `combat/` (combat-action + combatant + resolve + event).
  - Symmetric pair semantics via a *canonical key* inside `RelationsMatrix` (`a < b ? "a|b" : "b|a"`) rather than storing two directional entries or exposing an ordered-pair API. Reasons over two-entries: halves the storage footprint, eliminates the "what if (a,b) and (b,a) drift" bug class, keeps toJSON output compact. Reasons over ordered-pair API: diplomacy actions are symmetric by the game's rules (declare-war affects both sides, cooldown applies to both), so exposing order at the signature level would either force every consumer to sort themselves or invite inconsistent call-site conventions. Pipe separator is safe because FactionId values are kebab-case identifiers ‚Äî TILESPAN-style escaping would be premature. Same canonical-key pattern as the `cells` key in `DirectionLayer` but applied to pair identity instead of grid index.
  - Cooldowns stored as *absolute expiry turn* (`expiresOnTurn`), not as a countdown. The matrix has no reference to the TurnManager ‚Äî consumers pass `currentTurn` on every `isOnCooldown` / `attemptDiplomacyAction` call. Reasons: (a) countdown state would need a per-turn decrement hook registered against the TurnManager, which ties this primitive to the turn scheduler ‚Äî exactly the coupling CLAUDE.md's "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection" rule guards against. (b) A save snapshot mid-turn is unambiguous: "cooldown expires on turn 14" reads the same whether you reload during turn 9's AI phase or turn 10's player phase; a countdown integer is interpretable only relative to a per-turn tick that the save format would have to carry. (c) Replay determinism is easier: the test asserts `isOnCooldown(..., currentTurn=10) === false` once `expiresOnTurn=10`, no "advance turn X times then check" wrapper.
  - Separated `shiftScore` (clamped delta) from `setScore` (absolute, bounds-validated). Gameplay code should only ever use `shiftScore` ‚Äî relations are earned or spent, not dictated. `setScore` exists for the save-load path (fromJSON reads the absolute number directly) and for deterministic test seeding. Keeping them as two surfaces makes the "only use shift in live game code" rule enforceable at code review: any `setScore` call outside `fromJSON` / tests is a red flag. Exposed both because a single method that accepted an "absolute or delta?" second arg would either be confusing or land on a magic convention (delta if `< 100 && > -100`?).
  - Attempt outcome as a *discriminated union* keyed by `status` ‚Äî `'accepted' | 'declined' | 'blocked-cooldown' | 'invalid-same-faction'` ‚Äî rather than a single shape with nullable fields. Reasons: `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` is enabled (CLAUDE.md) so mixing "has cooldownUntil when blocked / has scoreDelta when not blocked" into one shape means the type has to declare both as optional and every consumer branches on truthiness, which TypeScript doesn't narrow correctly across two conditional fields. Union discriminator narrows cleanly at every call site (`if (outcome.status === 'accepted') outcome.newScore ‚Ä¶`) and the invalid-same-faction variant carries *zero* mutation-state fields ‚Äî it cannot pretend to have a score delta the matrix didn't apply. Cost: four interface declarations instead of one. Benefit: no "did that run mutate or not?" ambiguity at the use site.
  - Action effect table via an exhaustive `switch(action)` with no `default` in `getDiplomacyActionEffect` rather than a `Record<DiplomacyAction, DiplomacyActionEffect>` object literal. The CLAUDE.md "consume save-format const-object unions via an exhaustive switch with no default" rule applies: adding a new `DiplomacyAction` literal causes `getDiplomacyActionEffect` and `aiShouldAccept` to both fail to compile until the author picks concrete numbers and a threshold for the new case. A `Record` would still give a compile error on the writer side (you must add the key) but not on the *reader* side if someone imported the table indirectly ‚Äî the switch makes every reader a build-time tripwire. Same precedent as `tileCost(TileType)` in `pathfind.ts`.
  - Matrix owns no knowledge of the action table ‚Äî `RelationsMatrix.shiftScore(a, b, delta)` accepts any integer delta; the attempt orchestrator reads the effect table and supplies the right delta. This mirrors the "scalar seam" pattern (CLAUDE.md): the data primitive doesn't look up policy, the orchestrator passes policy through. Benefits: re-tuning action numbers is a data edit in diplomacy-action.ts with zero matrix-test churn, an alternate policy layer (e.g. AI personality modifier that scales deltas by 0.8x) slots in at the orchestrator without the matrix knowing, and tests for `shiftScore` stay at the primitive level (delta clamping, determinism) while tests for action numbers stay at the action-table level.

### Run [2026-04-22 17:25]
- Task: TASK-059 ‚Äî Diplomacy screen (React)
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/70 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: web=431 (was 402 ‚Äî +29 across four surfaces: +13 in `src/diplomacy/diplomacy-math.test.ts` covering `stanceFromScore` per-threshold boundaries (hostile/tense/neutral/warm/allied at -100/-50/-49/-20/-19/0/19/20/49/50/100) + non-finite + out-of-range rejections, `describeOutcome` null-on-no-outcome + null-on-different-target + per-status format (accepted/declined/blocked-cooldown/invalid-same-faction) + ¬±0 zero-delta format, `computeDiplomacyPanels` excludes-proposer + default-score-0-neutral-no-cooldown + onCooldown-flag-set-when-locked + flag-clears-at-expiry + lastActionSummary-only-for-matching-target + stance-reflects-shifted-score + positive-integer-currentTurn rejection; +13 in `src/diplomacy/DiplomacyScreen.test.tsx` covering routing (openDiplomacy ‚Üí screen), card-per-peer (excluding player), default neutral ¬∑ 0 + "no recent action", button-per-action per card, cooldown disables button + surfaces turn-N note, confirmation modal opens on click + shows title/cost/flavour, cancel closes modal only, confirm commits attempt (updates matrix + last outcome + cooldown + closes modal), last-action summary updates on target card, declined-outcome path at score 0 for alliance, close button routes back to 'game', Esc closes modal first then screen, pre-shifted stance chip (allied ¬∑ 75 / hostile ¬∑ -75); +2 in `src/hud/Hud.test.tsx` covering hud-diplomacy-button presence + click-opens-diplomacy; +1 in `src/App.test.tsx` diplomacy-screen dispatch subsuite (mount when screen is diplomacy + not mounted otherwise)), content=114 (was 108 ‚Äî +6 in `src/diplomacy-flavour.test.ts` covering six-action membership + non-empty field invariants + valid tone register + getDiplomacyActionFlavour happy-path + unknown-action throw + isDiplomacyActionId narrow/reject), core=680 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged)
- Files changed: packages/content/src/{diplomacy-flavour,diplomacy-flavour.test,index}.ts (new module), apps/web/src/diplomacy/{DiplomacyScreen,DiplomacyScreen.test,DiplomacyScreen.module,diplomacy-math,diplomacy-math.test}.{ts,tsx,css} (new module), apps/web/src/store/game.ts (Screen +'diplomacy', relations + lastDiplomacyOutcome slices, setRelations/openDiplomacy/closeDiplomacy/attemptDiplomacy/dismissDiplomacyOutcome actions), apps/web/src/hud/Hud.{ts,tsx} + Hud.test.tsx (DiplomacyButton in topRight), apps/web/src/App.tsx + App.test.tsx (dispatch {screen === 'diplomacy' && <DiplomacyScreen />}), roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (web 402 ‚Üí 431, content 108 ‚Üí 114, every other count steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=4 since PR #66 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:e6ae02ca9ff7179cb53f350d21441d46601398c5ad7f3d1426279cefbe2329dc, config sha256:6ad7518207b354c79ecda3ac3b4c5a197282a74badeb187435847121298b6f12). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Web-only change in apps/web + content flavour in packages/content ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Pure-sibling `diplomacy-math.ts` mirrors the `trade-math` / `transfer-math` precedent ‚Äî not driven by Phaser's jsdom load-probe (diplomacy is pure-React) but by testing ergonomics. `stanceFromScore` + `describeOutcome` + `computeDiplomacyPanels` are plain functions over plain data, exercised 13 times without mounting a component, at the ~6ms test-run cost of the whole file. The component test then only has to verify *wiring* (what data flows where, what the click does), not arithmetic. If the stance-threshold set ever becomes faction-personality-specific ‚Äî "the Ironclad Syndicate forgives peace at score ‚â• -70, not -50" ‚Äî the rewrite is a sibling-module parameter change with all 13 assertions re-runnable against the new seam; the component stays untouched.
  - Relations snapshot lives in the zustand store as the plain `RelationsMatrixJSON`, not as a `RelationsMatrix` class instance. Rationale: zustand state needs to round-trip through `structuredClone` for devtools + time-travel (same precedent as `units` / `colonies` being `UnitJSON[]` / `ColonyJSON[]`, not class instances, per the game-state slice comments). Readers ‚Äî both the UI and the `attemptDiplomacy` action ‚Äî call `RelationsMatrix.fromJSON` to get a live instance when they need methods. This keeps the primitive's public API as "pure data" without forcing consumers to remember a serialise step before every write. The trade-off: every attempt re-parses the JSON (~O(pairs)) but the matrix is small (4-faction playable set, so at most 6 pairs) so the cost is a rounding error versus the slot-it-in wins on save-load parity.
  - `attemptDiplomacy(target, action)` returns the outcome, *and* writes both `relations` and `lastDiplomacyOutcome` slices in a single `set(...)` call ‚Äî the multi-slice atomic-set rule. Without the atomicity, a render could land between "relations updated, outcome not yet" and "outcome updated, relations not yet" ‚Äî the DiplomacyScreen subscribes to both slices via separate `useGameStore(s => ‚Ä¶)` calls, and a partial render would paint a stale score + an outcome for a score the matrix didn't yet hold. Same shape as `commitTrade` updating `units` + `homePorts`.
  - `currentTurn = Math.max(1, state.currentTurn)` inside `attemptDiplomacy`. The `attemptDiplomacyAction` primitive in `@colonize/core` asserts `currentTurn >= 1` (a positive integer, matching `TurnManager.turn`). The zustand store initialises `currentTurn: 0` until the first `advanceTurn` tick fires, so a freshly-loaded game where the player clicks Declare War before any turn boundary would otherwise throw. The clamp is defence-in-depth at the store boundary (same shape as the user-input `clamp-and-skip` rule in CLAUDE.md, applied to a derived time value rather than a slider qty). The cost is that a first-turn attempt records `cooldownUntil = 1 + cooldownTurns` which is still correct relative to the game's actual turn index ‚Äî the cooldown simply fires one turn earlier than it would from turn 1, with no mis-ordering. Future work: wire the turn manager to seed `currentTurn = 1` on new-game start so the clamp becomes redundant.
  - `'diplomacy'` is a *terminal* screen dispatch (like `'trade'` / `'transfer'` / `'colony'`), not an overlay on top of `'game'`. The distinction matters because terminal screens unmount the Phaser canvas' parent view, whereas overlays keep it mounted underneath. Diplomacy is launched from the HUD button, consumes the whole screen, and closes back to `'game'` ‚Äî no colony context needs to persist, no Phaser-side hover state is relevant, no player-turn interaction is dispatched behind the modal. If a future "negotiate from within a colony" entry-point lands (e.g. a colony overlay button that opens diplomacy then returns to colony), the store action takes a parameter for the return-screen ‚Äî exactly how `openTradeSession` / `closeTradeSession` route back to `'colony'`. Not added speculatively because the current entry point is HUD-only.
  - Cost labels live in content as *descriptive strings* ("Tribute of 10 cargo", "Requires warm relations", "‚Äî"), not as enforced resource deductions. Reason: the core `attemptDiplomacyAction` primitive does not yet read a coin / cargo ledger (no ledger exists), and fabricating one inside the store action would either require a companion task to land first or be a dead branch the orchestrator task rips out. Per the "trim consumer-specific fields off save-format registries" rule, flavour stays in content and the gameplay consequence (clamp to affordability, deduct on confirm) lands when the coin ledger task lands. The UI shows the label so the player sees the *intent* of the feature without the plumbing pretending to exist.
  - In-screen confirmation modal via `useState<{target, action} | null>` rather than a separate `'diplomacy-confirm'` screen literal or a global `pendingDiplomacyAction` store slice. Reason: the confirmation is a sub-interaction of the diplomacy screen ‚Äî the state only needs to survive between the action-click and the confirm/cancel click, and it's meaningless outside the DiplomacyScreen lifecycle. Local React state stays localised; navigating away from diplomacy via close/Esc implicitly discards the pending state (the component unmounts). A separate screen would need its own Esc handler + re-entry logic + store action to return-to-screen; a global slice would persist across unmount, which is the wrong semantics (pending an action, closing the screen, and re-opening it should *not* re-show the modal against stale target info).
  - Esc handler inside DiplomacyScreen handles modal-first-then-screen (two-Esc staircase) via `pending` dependency on the `useEffect`. Mirrors TradeScreen's single-level Esc handler but with an extra branch ‚Äî when `pending !== null`, Esc cancels the modal without closing the outer screen. Test verifies both: first Esc closes the modal + keeps `screen === 'diplomacy'`, second Esc closes the screen. `stopPropagation()` prevents the App-level Esc handler (which routes `'game' ‚Üî 'pause'`) from firing on top ‚Äî diplomacy's Esc is locally scoped even though the screen is opened via the HUD.
  - Stance thresholds align with `aiShouldAccept` thresholds from `@colonize/core`: `'allied'` at score ‚â• 50 matches the ProposeAlliance accept bar, `'hostile'` at score ‚â§ -50 matches the ProposePeace accept bar (below which peace gets declined). This avoids the UI claiming "allied" while the AI still refuses an alliance ‚Äî the label promises what the AI delivers. Derived in the pure sibling so the stance label and the AI's threshold stay couple-able; if the thresholds ever diverge (faction-personality-driven AI with one stance ‚Üí multiple AI bars), stanceFromScore expands to take a faction-id parameter without the UI having to branch.

- Task: TASK-063 ‚Äî Implement per-faction bonus hooks
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/71 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: core=714 (was 680 ‚Äî +34 new in `src/faction/faction-bonus.test.ts` covering `PlayableFactionId` registry (four-MVP membership + unique values + kebab-case invariant), `isPlayableFactionId` narrow/reject matrix, `FACTION_BONUSES` per-faction invariants (OTK owns Red Tide immunity + Legendary blueprint redemption exclusively; Ironclad owns +10% colony production + ‚àí20% shipyard cost multiplier exclusively; Phantom owns open-ocean stealth + 1.5√ó raid loot exclusively; Bloodborne owns 1.15√ó combat damage + free-soldier-per-colony-per-turn exclusively), per-faction multipliers are finite + positive, no faction carries more than two non-neutral fields (bonus-focus invariant), `getFactionBonus` returns the registry entry for every playable id, `factionPathfindFlags` adds/ORs `redTideImmunity` for OTK + passes through base + plugs into `tileCost(RedTide)` making the tile traversable for OTK but Infinity for the others, per-helper spot-checks for `factionColonyProductionMultiplier` / `factionBuildingCostMultiplier` (Ironclad √ó Shipyard only) / `factionCombatDamageMultiplier` / `factionRaidLootMultiplier` / `factionHasOpenOceanStealth` / `factionCanRedeemLegendaryBlueprint` / `factionGrantsFreeSoldierPerColonyPerTurn`, and a core-side drift guard pinning the canonical MVP set), content=114 (unchanged ‚Äî drift-guard prose comment added above the matching MVP-set assertion in `src/factions.test.ts`), web=431 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged)

- Regression alert: false (core 680 ‚Üí 714, every other count steady)
- Review proposed: true ‚Äî https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/72 (5 consecutive successes since PR #66 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-054 ‚Üí TASK-055 ‚Üí TASK-058 ‚Üí TASK-059 ‚Üí TASK-063 ‚Äî threshold hit; /autonomous-review drafted 1 refinement codifying slice-driven self-mounting overlays for "happens-during-an-action" events like CombatOverlay / RumourRevealModal; five other candidate patterns appeared in only one run in the window and were deferred per the ‚â• 2-entry bar)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:e4c277a08d7c47e1ceb0dd585fa748b6506fb311a7151bce1c3d47dec9fe3bc5, config sha256:fcb65527e9ac70ae82521ce74291653e70353d90c7fc828cc13ed6a4f34f5d9d). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Core-only change in packages/core + drift-guard prose in packages/content ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Registry-as-primitive interpretation of "implement per-faction bonus hooks." The task description enumerates the mechanical surfaces (economy, combat, map) but the concrete iteration points ‚Äî per-turn free-soldier grant, per-raid loot scale, per-shipyard-construction cost discount ‚Äî each live in consumers that don't yet exist (no turn-tick colony iterator, no raid action, no faction-aware shipyard-build pipeline). Shipping the full wiring would have either invented those orchestrators prematurely or left dead branches the real orchestrators rip out. Shipping only the registry + per-surface scalar/flag helpers leaves the wiring task for the consumer to own ‚Äî exactly CLAUDE.md's "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection" rule applied to per-faction modifiers. The helper signatures (return a scalar, return a flag, return a `PathfindFlags`) match the shape every existing scalar-seam consumer already expects, so wiring later is a single multiply / single flag pass at the call site, not a protocol shift.
  - Hook-point granularity decided by "does the existing code already accept this seam?" `PathfindFlags.redTideImmunity` already exists and is read by `tileCost(RedTide)` ‚Üí `factionPathfindFlags` is a zero-churn helper that produces the flags object. Colony production in `apps/web/src/colony/build-queue.ts` already accepts a scalar `colonyProductionValue` and there's no existing ceiling-scaled math ‚Üí `factionColonyProductionMultiplier` returns a scalar the future orchestrator multiplies through. Combat has `CombatContext` with no damage-multiplier field yet ‚Üí `factionCombatDamageMultiplier` returns a scalar the future orchestrator applies when it builds the `Combatant` (scale attacker.guns by the multiplier) or when it extends `CombatContext`. Bloodborne's free-soldier-per-colony-per-turn is a boolean flag the future turn-tick grant reads; it doesn't imply a soldier-count scalar until the grant task owns the policy. The rule: if a consumer already has a seam, the helper mirrors it; if no consumer exists, a flag or scalar is the cheapest future-extension shape ‚Äî not a pre-baked orchestrator.
  - `PlayableFactionId` duplicated between `@colonize/core/faction/faction-bonus.ts` (rule-relevant mechanical bonuses) and `@colonize/content/factions.ts` (descriptive flavour) because neither package may import the other per CLAUDE.md's dependency-direction rule. The drift risk is mitigated by sibling tests in each package that pin the canonical MVP set (sorted `['bloodborne', 'ironclad', 'otk', 'phantom']`). This mirrors the ship-class `baseMovement` precedent (core + content both carry the number, with a content-side ordering-invariant test guarding consistency). Same trade-off: two lines of duplication + two drift-guard tests, versus a new cross-package edge just to save the duplication. The rule wins.
  - `FACTION_BONUSES` uses a neutral-bonus base (`NEUTRAL_BONUS` constant with every field at the identity value) spread into each faction, with only the non-neutral fields overridden per-faction. Reasons over per-faction-literal-everything: (a) adding a new bonus field surfaces as a TypeScript error at *every* faction that hasn't set it only if the field is required on `FactionBonus` ‚Äî spreading from a neutral default means adding a new field requires updating the default only, with every faction still defaulting to neutral until intentionally customised; (b) the "no faction carries more than two non-neutral fields" invariant (asserted in tests) becomes visually obvious in the source ‚Äî only two overrides per entry; (c) the neutral-bonus constant is the implicit answer to "what's a non-playable faction's bonus?" ‚Äî a NPC faction would carry the same shape even if their bonuses aren't surfaced in the player-facing flavour. Cost: one extra top-level constant. Benefit: every field's identity value lives in one place, so "what counts as neutral?" is unambiguous.
  - `factionBuildingCostMultiplier(id, type)` branches on `type === BuildingType.Shipyard` rather than exposing a per-building multiplier map on `FactionBonus`. Reason: the MVP roster has exactly one per-building-type cost bonus (Ironclad √ó Shipyard at 0.8). Adding a full `Record<BuildingType, number>` to every faction would be ~15 √ó 4 = 60 extra cells of which 59 are 1.0 ‚Äî dead weight for the save format, dead weight for tests, and no future-proofing since any second per-building bonus would still slot into the bonus struct as a new field (`shipyardCostMultiplier`, `forgeCostMultiplier`, etc.). When / if the second bonus lands, the branch becomes an `if` chain and later a table; the table-first shape is premature abstraction. Canonical test invariant enforces this: every `(faction, building)` pair other than `(ironclad, shipyard)` returns 1.0, so adding a new per-building bonus surfaces as a test failure that forces intentional update.
