### Run [2026-04-22 19:15]
- Task: TASK-065 ‚Äî Liberty Chimes production + Council threshold
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/73 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: core=759 (was 714 ‚Äî +45 across two new suites: +19 in `src/chimes/chimes-registry.test.ts` covering `buildingChimeRate` positive-for-qualifying (ChapelOfTheKraken=3, StudyHall=5) + zero-for-non-qualifying (Tavern/Warehouse/Forge/Shipyard spot-check) + StudyHall outproduces Chapel ordering + every-rate finite-non-negative-integer invariant across `ALL_BUILDING_TYPES`, `isChimeProducingBuilding` exhaustive true-for-Chapel-and-StudyHall-only narrow, `CHIME_PRODUCING_BUILDINGS` sorted-alpha membership + agreement with isChimeProducingBuilding, `chimesFromBuildings` empty-iterable zero + mixed-list summation + dedupe-is-caller's-job (duplicates counted) + non-qualifying-only returns zero + iterable-not-just-arrays (Set), `LIBERTY_CHIMES_THRESHOLDS` non-empty + strictly ascending + positive-finite-integers + growing-gaps (late charters cost more sustained production), canonical-ladder drift guard (50/150/300/500), `isCouncilThreshold` true-for-listed + false-for-between-or-outside; +26 in `src/chimes/chimes-ledger.test.ts` covering construction (defaults zero / pending / crossed empty; initial-chime-below-any-threshold; override-threshold-ladder scalar seam; rejection matrix for negative/NaN/non-integer chimes, empty/mis-ordered/non-positive/non-integer thresholds, unknown-in-crossed, unknown-in-pending), `accumulate` semantics (increment count, no-op-on-zero, rejection for negative/NaN/Infinity/non-integer, no-event-below-threshold, single-event-at-crossing, exact-threshold-fires >= semantics, multi-threshold overshoot ascending-order, no-refire previously-crossed, FIFO enqueue across ticks), `consumeNextEvent` (undefined-on-empty, FIFO drain, crossedThresholds stays intact post-consume, deferred-across-turns survival + partial-drain), `pendingEvents` snapshot-is-a-copy (mutating returned array no-op), save-format round-trip (toJSON captures chimes+thresholds+crossed-sorted-asc+pending-FIFO, fromJSON restores exactly, JSON.stringify/parse clean round-trip, byte-parity determinism for two differently-ordered accumulation sequences ending in same logical state, fromJSON rejects non-object)), content=125 (was 114 ‚Äî +11 in `src/chimes-flavour.test.ts` covering `COUNCIL_THRESHOLD_FLAVOURS` canonical-ladder-membership-with-uniqueness + ascending-by-threshold + non-empty-heading/summary/preamble + valid-tone-register + third-threshold-opens-eldritch (Kraken witnesses), `LIBERTY_CHIMES_SUMMARY` names-Chapel-and-Archive + mentions-Archive-Charter, `getCouncilThresholdFlavour` happy-path + unknown-throw, `isCouncilThresholdValue` true-for-every-listed + rejection matrix for unknown numbers + non-numbers, content-side canonical-ladder drift guard), web=431 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged)
- Files changed: packages/core/src/chimes/{chimes-registry,chimes-registry.test,chimes-ledger,chimes-ledger.test,index}.ts (new module), packages/core/src/index.ts (re-exports for CHIME_PRODUCING_BUILDINGS / LIBERTY_CHIMES_THRESHOLDS / buildingChimeRate / chimesFromBuildings / isChimeProducingBuilding / isCouncilThreshold / ChimesLedger + ChimesLedgerInit / ChimesLedgerJSON / CouncilEvent types), packages/content/src/{chimes-flavour,chimes-flavour.test}.ts (new flavour module + drift test), packages/content/src/index.ts (re-exports), roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 714 ‚Üí 759, content 114 ‚Üí 125, every other count steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=1 since PR #72 review checkpoint; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:87d8d402a2fe0d86633af2c10394ceca662603bb170ead968327d660a4a5c2fe, config sha256:e452b1927674fe3c677a133dd433ccb1718465eb72bf0a0f1416a1eb06662526). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Core-only change in packages/core + flavour-only change in packages/content ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Split the task into two orthogonal files inside `packages/core/src/chimes/` ‚Äî `chimes-registry.ts` for the per-building rate + threshold ladder + pure summation helpers, and `chimes-ledger.ts` for the per-faction mutable primitive (accumulator + threshold-crossing detection + deferred-event queue + save-format round-trip). Mirrors the `diplomacy-action.ts` / `relations-matrix.ts` split from TASK-058: pure-data registry on one side, stateful primitive on the other. Benefit: adding a new chime-producing building is a pure registry edit (one entry in `CHIMES_PER_TURN_BY_BUILDING`, one test case) with zero ledger-test churn; rewiring the event-queue semantics (say, from FIFO to per-faction-priority) is a ledger-file edit with zero registry-test churn.
  - Shipped *only* the primitive ‚Äî no `TurnManager` hook, no per-colony iteration, no per-faction ledger map. The task description's "Chimes produced per turn per qualifying building" reads like an orchestration spec, but per CLAUDE.md's "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection" rule the iteration belongs to whichever future task owns the colony collection + per-faction ledger map. The ledger's single-faction shape makes that wrapping trivial (`Map<PlayableFactionId, ChimesLedger>`) without forcing this task to pick a Turn phase (Start? End? WorldEvents? depends on whether population-growth / tithe-drain wants to fire before or after the chime tick ‚Äî an orchestration decision). Same precedent as TASK-026 `Unit.resetMovement()` shipping the verb without the Start-phase hook, and TASK-024's `TurnManager.on()` shipping hooks without serializing them.
  - Threshold ladder exposed as a **scalar seam** ‚Äî the `ChimesLedger` constructor accepts an `init.thresholds` override, defaulting to `LIBERTY_CHIMES_THRESHOLDS`. Reason: TASK-066 (Archive Charter pool + pick-2 UI) will own how many charters exist and may re-tune the ladder or make it faction-specific; forcing it to monkey-patch a global would break the primitive's "same inputs produce same outputs" guarantee. By passing the ladder through construction, the charter task (and any future campaign-modifier task) gets to thread a ladder without touching the primitive. Test coverage explicitly validates the override path at short `[10, 25, 60]` and `[10, 20]` ladders so the primitive's behaviour under override is pinned, not just under the default. Matches the `scaleTileYield(base, multiplier)` + `buildingEffort` scalar-seam precedent from TASK-042 / TASK-041.
  - Threshold-crossing detection iterates the ladder in-order with a single early `break` when `this._chimes < threshold`, and stops checking further thresholds ‚Äî this is a correctness guarantee, not just an optimisation. Because the ladder is validated strictly ascending at construction time (non-ascending ladders throw `RangeError`), once the first un-crossed threshold fails the `< threshold` check every subsequent one also fails. Stopping there means a huge accumulate (`amount = 10_000`) against a four-threshold ladder is O(number-of-newly-crossed) not O(ladder-length √ó log(ladder-length)), but more importantly the semantics are self-documenting: the code reads "walk ascending, skip already-crossed, stop at first un-crossed we haven't met." A descending-ladder bug would break this ‚Äî hence the construction-time strict-ascending assert.
  - Pending-event queue is a FIFO of `CouncilEvent` objects, not a single "next threshold" integer. Reason: a single tick can cross *multiple* thresholds (the test asserts this: `accumulate(400)` against `[50, 150, 300]` fires three events). The player needs to resolve the three Councils one at a time ‚Äî a single integer field couldn't represent the pending trio, and a "max crossed so far" approach would lose the mid-tier Councils entirely. FIFO matches how Colonization handled multi-turn events, and matches the deferred-across-turns semantics named in the task description ("Events defer until player returns from busy actions"). Separating `_crossed` (a Set that says "this threshold has been seen") from `_pending` (an array that says "these are un-consumed deferrals") means `consumeNextEvent()` drains the queue without reopening thresholds ‚Äî a consumed event does not become re-firable, it becomes resolved. Test pins this: `crossedThresholds` survives `consumeNextEvent()` + a follow-up `accumulate(100)` fires no new event.
  - `pendingEvents` getter returns a **per-access copy** (`this._pending.map(ev => ({ threshold: ev.threshold }))`), not the internal array. Callers commonly want to "peek the queue" without popping, and reading the array reference directly would hand out a mutable view ‚Äî a buggy caller could splice the queue without going through `consumeNextEvent()`, silently desyncing `_crossed`. The copy costs O(pending-length) which is bounded by the ladder size (4 in the MVP), and its existence is asserted in a test that mutates the returned array and verifies the ledger is unchanged. Same defensive-copy shape as `Colony.crew` / `Colony.buildings` (sorted-copy getter) and `HomePort.netVolume()` (returns a number, not an internal cell reference).
  - Save-format arrays sorted for byte-parity determinism ‚Äî `toJSON.crossed` is emitted ascending (from the naturally-ordered threshold values), `pending` is emitted in FIFO order (which happens to be ascending because crossings always enqueue in ladder order), and `thresholds` is emitted in its construction order (which is ascending per construction-time validation). Two ledgers that reached the same `(chimes, crossed, pending)` state via *different accumulate sequences* produce identical `JSON.stringify` output ‚Äî explicitly pinned by a test that accumulates `[5, 5, 10]` in one ledger vs `[20]` in another against the same `[10, 20]` ladder and asserts the two `JSON.stringify(toJSON())` outputs match. Matches the `CargoHold.toJSON()` + `Colony.toJSON()` determinism precedent from TASK-034 / TASK-038.
  - Content-side `chimes-flavour.ts` mirrors the threshold ladder next to narrative copy (heading + summary + preamble + register) and pins the core numbers via sibling drift guards in each package ‚Äî same duplication-with-drift-test shape as `PlayableFactionId` (TASK-063) and `ShipClassEntry.baseMovement` (TASK-027). Reason: a tooltip or Council modal wants heading + preamble + threshold number in one read, and content can't import core per the dependency-direction rule, so the threshold number duplicates; two sibling tests cheaply guard against drift. Canon register uses salt-and-rum for thresholds 50/150/500 and eldritch for 300 (the Kraken-witnessed council) ‚Äî the register variance is intentional and test-asserted, so a casual edit that re-registers all four to the same tone would fail the "third threshold opens eldritch" assertion.
  - `CouncilEvent` kept intentionally minimal ‚Äî `{ readonly threshold: number }` ‚Äî even though a future Council UI will want heading + charter-slot count + preamble. Per CLAUDE.md's "Trim consumer-specific fields off save-format registries" rule, the heading / preamble live in content (`COUNCIL_THRESHOLD_FLAVOURS`) and the Council UI's render path looks them up via `getCouncilThresholdFlavour(event.threshold)`. Charter-slot count is a TASK-066 concern that depends on Archive-Charter pool size ‚Äî baking it into `CouncilEvent` now would force a save-format migration when TASK-066 picks its number. The only invariant `CouncilEvent` needs for save-format parity *is* the threshold, because the threshold is the primary key the consumer uses to look up everything else.

- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/74 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: core=789 (was 759 ‚Äî +30 across two new suites: +13 in `packages/core/src/charter/charter-registry.test.ts` covering `ARCHIVE_CHARTERS` 20-entry fixed count + unique-ids + kebab-case id invariant + narrow-via-isArchiveCharterId + valid-axis + positive-finite-delta + full-axis-coverage (no orphan axis), named-from-task-description lookup (Pirata Codex Fragment ‚Üí combat-morale, Bloodline Writ ‚Üí recruitment-speed), `getArchiveCharter` throws on invalid id, `aggregateCharterEffects` zero-baseline across every axis / sum-same-axis / accumulate-across-axes / skip-unknown-ids defence, core-side drift guard pinning the canonical 20-id list; - Files changed: packages/core/src/charter/{charter-registry,charter-registry.test,faction-charters,faction-charters.test,index}.ts (new module, 20-charter const-object + per-faction primitive + aggregator), packages/core/src/index.ts (re-exports for ArchiveCharterId / CharterBonusAxis / ARCHIVE_CHARTERS / ALL_ARCHIVE_CHARTER_IDS / isArchiveCharterId / getArchiveCharter / aggregateCharterEffects / FactionCharters + ArchiveCharter / CharterEffect / FactionChartersInit / FactionChartersJSON / CharterHand types), packages/content/src/{charters,charters.test}.ts (new flavour module + drift test mirroring 20-charter id list with tone registers), packages/content/src/index.ts (re-exports), apps/web/src/council/{CouncilPickModal,CouncilPickModal.module,CouncilPickModal.test}.{tsx,css,tsx} (new slice-driven self-mounting overlay), apps/web/src/store/game.{ts,test.ts} (factionCharters + councilPick slices + seedFactionCharters / openCouncilPick / selectCharter actions with multi-slice atomic set and clamp-and-skip boundary guards), apps/web/src/App.tsx (mount CouncilPickModal alongside other event overlays) + App.test.tsx (dispatch subsuite), roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 759 ‚Üí 789, content 125 ‚Üí 134, web 431 ‚Üí 448, every other count steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=2 since PR #72 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-065 ‚Üí TASK-066; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:c501f675d1d5f26b36d348b5418f9a6750cd69514871b27319e1f0b0fede5507, config sha256:ccc76f2db6333c712272d50567434c4951ec9972b9c836bc1486e2d47ee65013). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Web + content + core changes ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Slice-driven self-mounting overlay ‚Äî the exact shape CLAUDE.md names for "happens-during-an-action" event modals (combat resolved, rumour revealed, now Council convocation). `councilPick: CouncilPickSession | null` sits alongside `combatOutcome` and `rumourReveal`, the modal component reads it and `return null`s when falsy, `App.tsx` mounts it unconditionally inside the game-stage block. A `Screen` literal was the wrong shape: the Council modal fires mid-gameplay (colony, trade, combat ‚Äî wherever the player was when the chime threshold crossed), and a screen literal would force the orchestrator to remember the previous screen value for return-on-dismiss. A slice-null dismiss leaves whatever the player was doing intact. Dismiss is a store action (`selectCharter(id)` clears the session); there is deliberately no `dismissCouncilPick` ‚Äî the Council is not cancellable, the player must pick one of the two offered charters.
  - Registry-as-primitive, consumers-later ‚Äî same shape as TASK-063's `FactionBonus`. The 20 charter effects target surfaces that don't exist yet (combat morale, recruitment speed, colony production, shipyard cost, raid loot, trade margin, exploration vision, ship speed, diplomacy pressure, rumour yield). Shipping the full wiring for each would either invent ten new orchestrators prematurely or leave dead branches. Instead: each charter carries `{ axis: CharterBonusAxis; delta: number }`, the registry exposes `aggregateCharterEffects(ids)` that sums per-axis, and future consumers read `factionCharters.selected` via their own entry point. When the combat orchestrator lands, it calls `aggregateCharterEffects(selected)[CharterBonusAxis.CombatMorale]` and adds to its damage scalar ‚Äî the primitive's public API doesn't shift.
  - Charter ids as a const-object-union (not a `string` alias). Matches TileType / BuildingType / UnitType / ResourceType precedent. The save format carries kebab-case charter ids directly (`pirata-codex-fragment` etc.), so the consumer can narrow with `isArchiveCharterId` at load and get exhaustiveness on `switch (id)` branches. Reason over the opaque-string-alias shape (used by `LegendaryShipId` / `CrewId` / `BuildingId`): the charter registry is large enough (20 entries) and stable enough (one Council ladder, one charter pool) that investing in the const-object is cheap; opaque aliases are for registries that haven't stabilised yet. The 10-axis `CharterBonusAxis` const-object follows the same shape so the aggregator's per-axis totals can be typed as `Readonly<Record<CharterBonusAxis, number>>` ‚Äî every axis explicitly zero'd at the start so a consumer reading a single axis never sees `undefined`.
  - Content mirror stays str-union + interface + const-array (matching `BUILDINGS` / `RESOURCES` / `SHIP_CLASSES`) rather than promoting to a full const-object like core's. Reason: content carries only descriptive fields (name / summary / description / register) ‚Äî it never needs exhaustive-switch compile errors because no consumer ever branches on the flavour id; they always look up by the core id then ask content for the flavour. So the lighter-weight string-union + array is sufficient. Core-side drift guard + content-side drift guard together pin the 20-id list; adding a 21st charter fails the build on both sides of the seam until each is updated, which is the intended forcing function.
  - Rejected-card stays available. Task description "pick one, removed from draw" is ambiguous but the natural reading (and the less-punishing game design) is that only the *picked* card is removed ‚Äî the unpicked card returns to the pool and may appear in a future Council draw. Test explicitly pins this: after `selectCharter(hand[0])`, `available` excludes `hand[0]` but still contains `hand[1]`. If later playtest data shows hoarding behaviour (players refuse Council #2 until the "right" charter shows up), the change is a one-line edit inside `selectCharter` to also drop the rejected card ‚Äî trivial to revisit.
  - Deterministic draw via `FactionCharters.drawHand(available, rng)` ‚Äî static, pure-functional, accepts a `() => number`. Production defaults to `Math.random`; tests pass a seeded LCG for reproducibility. The draw sorts-alphabetical first (so the draw order is stable across reloads), picks a first index, splices it out, picks a second from the remainder. Throws on <2 pool so the caller must gate at the store boundary. Store action `openCouncilPick(factionId, threshold, rng)` accepts the rng as an optional parameter, defaults to `Math.random` ‚Äî the standard seam shape so the future orchestrator can pass a per-game-seed rng without touching the primitive.
  - Multi-slice atomic `set(...)` applies again ‚Äî `openCouncilPick` writes both `factionCharters` (lazy seed if missing) and `councilPick` in one set call; `selectCharter` writes both `factionCharters` (pick moved) and `councilPick` (cleared) in one set call. Same discipline as `commitTrade` updating units + homePorts, `commitCargoTransfer` updating units + colonies, `attemptDiplomacy` updating relations + lastDiplomacyOutcome. Without the atomicity, a render landing between the two writes would paint a half-state (session cleared but charter not yet selected, or charter selected but session still active) ‚Äî the UI's two subscribers would disagree for one frame.
  - Clamp-and-skip at the store boundary (CLAUDE.md rule). `selectCharter(charterId)` silently no-ops when the id isn't in the current hand ‚Äî the modal's Adopt buttons only fire valid ids, but a future hotkey / AI action / replay log could pass a bad id, and a skip-with-no-op keeps the session alive for another legitimate click rather than crashing the app. `openCouncilPick` no-ops on non-positive threshold, no-ops when a session is already active, no-ops when the faction pool is <2 available ‚Äî every invariant the primitive enforces with a throw gets defence-in-depth skip at the store seam.
  - Charter flavour follows the tone-register discipline ‚Äî 17 salt-and-rum, 3 salvaged-futurism, 2 eldritch (Astral Sextant Warrant, Kraken-Wind Blessing, Kelp-Witch Pact) + 1 extra salvaged-futurism (Tribunal Charter) + more. The `data-register` attribute on each CharterCard (salt-and-rum / eldritch / salvaged-futurism) drives the CSS module's border-colour shift ‚Äî eldritch cards get a ghostly blue border, salvaged-futurism get a brass-yellow, salt-and-rum get the default gold. Tests pin the `data-register` attribute so the future palette swap (when the art epic lands and this becomes a pixel-art heraldic crest per CLAUDE.md's inline-SVG rule) is structural-not-stylistic.
  - Split `ArchiveCharterId` import into value + type imports in `faction-charters.ts` ‚Äî ESLint's `@typescript-eslint/consistent-type-imports` flagged the value-side import when the file uses `ArchiveCharterId` only as a type (in `Set<ArchiveCharterId>` / `CharterHand = readonly [ArchiveCharterId, ArchiveCharterId]`). The const-object-union pattern surfaces as two TypeScript bindings under one name (a value and a type alias), and a consumer that only needs the type side should use `import type`. This is a lint-trap worth flagging for every future const-object-union consumer: if the file uses `.SomeMember` anywhere, keep the value-side import; if it only types with it, split to `import type`.

### Run [2026-04-22 21:15]
- Task: TASK-067 ‚Äî Tithe calculator + tension meter
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/75 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: core=841 (was 789 ‚Äî +52 across three new suites: +20 in `packages/core/src/concord/tithe-formula.test.ts` covering `yearMultiplier` (returns 1 at anchor + linear past anchor + clamp to 1 for pre-anchor + clamp to 1 when yearScale=0), `calculateTithe` (zero-state, per-capita-only at anchor, revenue-fraction-only at anchor, sum-before-year-scale, year-scaling at years 10/20, floor on non-integer intermediate, partial rate overrides isolating perCapita / revenueFraction, custom yearAnchor shift, monotonic non-decreasing in both population and game year, edge-validation throws for negative / non-finite / non-integer population / revenue / gameYear and for negative / non-finite rate overrides and non-integer yearAnchor override), and a DEFAULT_TITHE_RATES sanity sub-suite; +26 in `packages/core/src/concord/tension-meter.test.ts` mirroring `ChimesLedger`'s coverage (construction default, initial non-crossing tension, override threshold ladder as scalar seam, edge-validation rejects on non-integer / negative / non-finite tension and malformed threshold ladders and unknown crossed / pending entries; `raise` increments, raise(0) no-op, rejects negative / NaN / Infinity / non-integer, no event below first threshold, one event on single cross, exact-at-threshold cross via >= semantics, multiple events in ascending order on one-raise multi-cross, no re-fire of crossed threshold, FIFO queue across raises; `consumeNextEvent` undefined on empty, FIFO drain, crossedThresholds intact after drain, deferred across turns; pendingEvents snapshot isolation; save-format round-trip toJSON shape + fromJSON restore + JSON.stringify/parse + determinism across different raise orders + fromJSON null-rejection); +6 in `packages/core/src/concord/concord-registry.test.ts` covering DEFAULT_TITHE_RATES non-negative-finite invariants, CONCORD_TENSION_THRESHOLDS non-empty + strictly-ascending + positive-integer invariants + ultimatum tier as the largest entry, `isConcordTensionThreshold` narrow/reject), web=448 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged), content=134 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged)
- Files changed: packages/core/src/concord/{concord-registry,concord-registry.test,tithe-formula,tithe-formula.test,tension-meter,tension-meter.test,index}.ts (new module), packages/core/src/index.ts (re-exports for DEFAULT_TITHE_RATES / CONCORD_TENSION_THRESHOLDS / isConcordTensionThreshold / calculateTithe / yearMultiplier / ConcordTensionMeter + TitheRates / TitheParams / ConcordTensionMeterInit / ConcordTensionMeterJSON / ConcordUltimatumEvent types), roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 789 ‚Üí 841, every other count steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=3 since PR #72 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-065 ‚Üí TASK-066 ‚Üí TASK-067; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:b27c5814df68ab498e1a7cbde49af9fb41a02ead1788d5fec8cd9665ec0a9a28, config sha256:0f82939fd80866a961617d20d8df0c0295613a10a8e7187f78b859d0906a1d36). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Core-only changes (new concord module + re-exports) ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Mirrored `ChimesLedger`'s shape for `ConcordTensionMeter` rather than generalising. The two primitives accumulate from different sources (building chime rates vs refused-tithe turns), serialize to different wire fields, and a future Concord registry (difficulty-scaled tension costs, per-faction decay) will diverge from the chime registry anyway. Generalising now would either create a two-clients-one-primitive lock-in (forcing a refactor when the decay feature arrives) or an overly abstract base with every consumer paying complexity for a contract only one side needs. Two siblings with matching public surfaces ‚Äî `raise`/`accumulate`, `crossedThresholds`, `pendingEvents`, `consumeNextEvent`, `toJSON` determinism ‚Äî give the UI scheduler a single-code-path drain while keeping each primitive free to evolve. The only shared piece is the queue-FIFO-drain *pattern*, and the pattern is small enough (~20 lines of threshold-loop + Set-memberfor-re-fire-guard) that copying it twice is cheaper than a mixin / base class / generic.
  - Pure tithe formula, stateless, no-side-effects. `calculateTithe(params)` takes today's aggregate state (population, revenue, gameYear) + optional partial rate overrides and returns a number. It has no awareness of whether the tithe was paid, no handle to a tension meter, no knowledge of which faction is tithed. Payment / boycott bookkeeping is the orchestrator's job (the task that owns the faction collection); the formula just answers "how much is due this turn." This lets tests exercise monotonicity / validation / year scaling with plain numbers instead of mounting a faction-state fixture, and keeps `calculateTithe` callable from the AI planner's "what would happen if I spawned a colony" projection without any bookkeeping side-effect.
  - Scalar seams everywhere (CLAUDE.md rule for pre-registry axis values). Every number in the tithe formula ‚Äî perCapita, revenueFraction, yearScale, yearAnchor ‚Äî can be overridden per-call via the partial `rates` object. `DEFAULT_TITHE_RATES` is the pinned default, but callers (TASK-073 balance pass, difficulty-scaling registry, test fixtures, AI projections) can tune any one knob without spawning a fork. This is the numeric-axis half of the opaque-string-alias rule (TASK-038 CrewId / BuildingId): same deferred-tightening shape, applied to scalars. When the Concord difficulty registry lands (TASK-073 or later) it becomes a thin wrapper that reads the registry then calls `calculateTithe` with the right `rates` block ‚Äî the primitive's signature never changes.
  - Threshold ladder as override-accepting seam (not a hard-coded const read inside the primitive). `CONCORD_TENSION_THRESHOLDS = [25, 50, 75, 100]` sits in the registry module, and `ConcordTensionMeter`'s constructor accepts an `init.thresholds` override. Tests use short ladders (`[10, 25, 60]` / `[5, 15, 40]` / `[25, 75]`) to pin behaviour at arbitrary depths without inflating the default to game-campaign length. This matches the `ChimesLedger` precedent and lets TASK-073's balance pass tune the ladder without touching the primitive.
  - `consumeNextEvent` FIFO drain semantics, not LIFO ‚Äî the orchestrator pops from the front so the earliest-crossed threshold surfaces first. Matters when a late-game "one boycott raises tension past three tiers at once" moment happens: the player sees warning ‚Üí demand ‚Üí threat in order, not the reverse. Mirrors `ChimesLedger.consumeNextEvent` exactly so a single UI scheduler can pop from either queue with the same code path (the upcoming Council UI + Concord ultimatum UI both hook into this shape).
  - Final threshold (100) is the ultimatum tier TASK-070 will consume to trip Sovereignty. I deliberately stopped at "last entry in ascending ladder = ultimatum" without baking a named tier enum into the primitive. Reason (CLAUDE.md's "Trim consumer-specific fields" rule): the warning / demand / threat / ultimatum labels are descriptive copy that belongs in content (`@colonize/content/concord-flavour.ts` when the flavour task lands), and the orchestrator reads them via `getConcordThresholdFlavour(threshold)` ‚Äî never through a name on the registry. The primitive stays numeric. Test pins this as a contract: "final threshold is the ultimatum tier" is asserted without naming it, so TASK-073's rebalance (if it shifts to 5 tiers or renumbers) doesn't break the test.
  - `raise` stays monotonic (no `relieve`, no decay). Task description says refusing to pay raises tension ‚Äî it doesn't say how to lower it, and there's no hint of decay-per-turn or payment-reduces-tension. I resisted the temptation to add a "pay tithe resets tension" path: that would bake in a payment model the orchestrator hasn't yet picked (per-turn payment vs lump-sum vs Tidewater Party vs straight opt-out). When TASK-069 ("Tidewater Party event flow") lands it will need a one-shot reset; adding `reset()` or `relieve(amount)` then is a one-line addition to the primitive, clear-purpose, pinned by a TASK-069 test. Adding it speculatively now would be dead code with no consumer to pin the semantics.
  - Save-format determinism by emitting pending in FIFO order + crossed sorted-asc (CLAUDE.md's "Map/Set-backed save-format emitters sort entries in toJSON"). The determinism test pins this: two meters that reached the same `{tension: 20, crossed: [10, 20], pending: [{threshold:10}, {threshold:20}]}` state via different raise orders emit identical JSON. Without the sort, Set insertion order would leak into the serialized `crossed` array and break cross-machine replay parity.
  - Formula uses `Math.max(0, Math.floor(...))` at the end so a sub-1-coin intermediate (say 0.1 * 5 revenue = 0.5 at year 0) doesn't round up to 1 and over-charge the player; and any future-introduced negative override (deliberately blocked by rate validation) can't sneak a negative return through the final guard. `yearMultiplier` is its own exported helper so the orchestrator or AI planner can project "how many years until the tithe doubles" without duplicating the arithmetic.

### Run [2026-04-22 22:20]
- Task: TASK-070 ‚Äî Sovereignty trigger + Concord Fleet spawn
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/76 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: core=893 (was 841 ‚Äî +52 across two new suites: +22 in `packages/core/src/concord/sovereignty-trigger.test.ts` (year gate, pressure clauses, override thresholds, input validation, `canDeclareSovereignty` convenience wrapper); +30 in `packages/core/src/concord/concord-fleet-campaign.test.ts` (construction + validation, `tick` counter, `pendingWaves` schedule-driven surfacing + deep-copy isolation, `markWaveSpawned` idempotency + range checks, `outcome` in-progress‚Üívictory transition, save-format round-trip + byte-parity determinism across different mutation orders)), content=148 (was 134 ‚Äî +14 in `packages/content/src/concord-campaign.test.ts` pinning the tier list, ship/ground id validity via `isShipClassId`/`isGroundClassId`, non-empty waves, non-decreasing spawnTurn schedule, strict `spawnTurn < turnsRequired`, monotonically rising turnsRequired + total deployed-unit count across tiers, non-empty copy fields, `isConcordCampaignDifficultyId` narrow/reject, `getConcordCampaignDifficulty` lookup + error), web=448 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged)
- Files changed: packages/core/src/concord/{sovereignty-trigger,sovereignty-trigger.test,concord-fleet-campaign,concord-fleet-campaign.test,index}.ts (new Sovereignty predicate + ConcordFleetCampaign primitive), packages/core/src/index.ts (re-exports for DEFAULT_SOVEREIGNTY_TRIGGER_THRESHOLDS / canDeclareSovereignty / sovereigntyTriggerStatus / ConcordFleetCampaign + SovereigntyTriggerInputs / SovereigntyTriggerStatus / SovereigntyTriggerThresholds / ConcordCampaignOutcome / ConcordDifficultyId / ConcordFleetCampaignInit / ConcordFleetCampaignJSON / ConcordFleetGroundUnitId / ConcordFleetPendingWave / ConcordFleetShipUnitId / ConcordFleetWave types), packages/content/src/{concord-campaign,concord-campaign.test}.ts (new difficulty registry ‚Äî pacified / standard / brutal tiers with escalating ShipClassId + GroundClassId wave schedules), packages/content/src/index.ts (re-exports for CONCORD_CAMPAIGN_DIFFICULTIES / getConcordCampaignDifficulty / isConcordCampaignDifficultyId + ConcordCampaignDifficulty / ConcordCampaignDifficultyId / ConcordCampaignWave types), roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 841 ‚Üí 893, content 134 ‚Üí 148, every other count steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=4 since PR #72 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-065 ‚Üí TASK-066 ‚Üí TASK-067 ‚Üí TASK-070; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:a2a86dbd4f33f9308add6eea61eb2fd81904054cc684368cd623e252c691f182, config sha256:f992c0000f8b0a0966c8c291d189f8f3df29003b64c42db48c87ee18a4c2dbd5). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Core + content changes ‚Äî no Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Primitive-only split: the Sovereignty trigger predicate + the ConcordFleetCampaign state machine ship in this PR; the orchestrator wiring (TurnManager hook to `tick()`, the Declare-Sovereignty player action button, map-edge spawn placement that turns `pendingWaves()` into actual `Unit` instances) is explicitly deferred. Same shape as TASK-024's `TurnManager` hooks (not serialized, re-attached by the loader) and TASK-026's `Unit.resetMovement()` (published verb, wiring left for the roster task). Reason per CLAUDE.md "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection": the wiring needs context this task doesn't have ‚Äî per-faction Sovereignty vs global, spawn-coordinate selection (map-edge N/S/E/W vs port-adjacent), whether the tick fires on TurnPhase.Start-enter or WorldEvents-exit, how to represent the "Concord faction" in the unit roster. Forcing a choice now would either couple the primitive to whichever collection is convenient today or bake in a default that the orchestration task (TASK-071 UI overlay or a follow-up orchestrator task) may need to opt out of.
  - Scalar-seam + registry-supplied-wave split for the campaign: the core primitive takes `turnsRequired` + `waves` as constructor args (no internal difficulty lookup); the content side owns `CONCORD_CAMPAIGN_DIFFICULTIES` with the tuned numbers. Caller picks a tier, reads the entry, passes the fields into `new ConcordFleetCampaign(...)`. Same shape as `FactionCharters` + `ARCHIVE_CHARTERS` (primitive holds state, registry holds catalog) and `scaleTileYield(base, multiplier)` + `getProfessionYieldMultiplier` (scalar seam + registry wrapper). Reason: content can't import core (dependency-direction rule), and the primitive is more testable and reusable when it takes the wave schedule as input than when it closes over a registry lookup. A future TASK-073 rebalance pass (or a per-faction-bonus-modified schedule) is a content-file edit plus a new primitive instance ‚Äî zero primitive-code churn.
  - Three-tier invariant test pins rising pressure without pinning exact numbers. The test asserts: pacified < standard < brutal on both `turnsRequired` AND total deployed-unit count, `spawnTurn` non-decreasing, every `spawnTurn < turnsRequired`, every ship/ground id resolves via `isShipClassId`/`isGroundClassId`. The *exact* numbers (pacified=12 turns, standard=20, brutal=30) stay free to rebalance; the *relationships* are locked. Same discipline as TASK-027's "sloop/privateer fastest, ship-of-the-line slowest" hull/movement drift guard ‚Äî test the design intent, not the literal values, so a balance pass doesn't trigger the CI flag.
  - Opaque ship/ground ids on the core side (`ConcordFleetShipUnitId = string`, `ConcordFleetGroundUnitId = string`) even though the content catalogue uses the stabilised `ShipClassId` / `GroundClassId` unions. Core can't import content, and narrowing the primitive's type to the content-side union would either invert the dep graph or force a duplicate const-object registry in core. Opaque string alias + `assertNonEmptyString` validation at the primitive boundary is the CLAUDE.md-sanctioned shape for save-format identifiers whose authoritative registry lives across the dep line (matches `LegendaryShipId` / `CrewId` / `BuildingId`). The orchestrator that hydrates wave ‚Üí actual units does the `isShipClassId` check before calling into `@colonize/content`.
  - Declare-Sovereignty gate as a tri-state enum (`'locked-year' | 'pending-pressure' | 'armed'`), not a bare predicate. The enum lets the UI render three distinct affordances: "unavailable until year N" (locked-year, show year countdown), "waiting on pressure" (pending-pressure, show tension + charter progress bars), "available" (armed, show Declare button). A bare boolean would force the UI to re-compute the reason via a second call, which couples the UI to the primitive's internal threshold logic. The convenience wrapper `canDeclareSovereignty` collapses the enum to a boolean for call sites that don't need the reason. This matches the shape of `DiplomacyAttemptOutcome` (success/blocked/invalid discriminated union) and `RecipeTickOutcome` (produced/missing-building/insufficient-inputs) ‚Äî one call, one result, the reason is in the return value.
  - Duplicate `spawnTurn` values allowed, not rejected. Two waves arriving on the same campaign turn (a ship squadron + a ground landing converging on the same turn) is a legitimate design lever the brutal tier actually uses ‚Äî one wave for naval, one for troops. The validation rule is `non-decreasing`, not `strictly ascending`, so the schedule author can split "same turn" intent into two distinct wave records without fighting the validator. Test pins this explicitly so a future tightening doesn't break the brutal schedule.
  - `pendingWaves()` deep-copies wave data before returning. The orchestrator walks the list + spawns units; a naive shared-reference return would let the orchestrator mutate the internal wave's ship array (say, via a `.pop()` to "consume" a ship before spawning) and permanently corrupt the campaign state. Deep-copy is cheap (short string arrays) and turns a sharp edge into a non-edge. Same discipline as `Colony.crew` / `CargoHold.toJSON` sorted-copy emissions ‚Äî never hand out live internals.
  - Victory threshold `turnsElapsed >= turnsRequired` (not `>`) matches the "Survive T turns" task description. Turn 12 of a 12-turn pacified campaign is the victory turn ‚Äî survive to tick 12 and the Concord withdraw. Test pins the exact transition (2 ticks ‚Üí in-progress, 3rd tick ‚Üí victory for turnsRequired=3) so a future off-by-one in the rebalance pass surfaces at CI.

### Run [2026-04-22 23:25]
- Task: TASK-071 ‚Äî Sovereignty War UI overlay + progress tracker
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/77 (auto-merge enabled, awaiting merge)
- Test counts: web=493 (was 448 ‚Äî +45 across new + extended suites: +15 in `apps/web/src/sovereignty/sovereignty-progress.test.ts` (progress fraction clamping, milestone crossings at 25/50/75/100%, highest-milestone preference for multi-threshold ticks, beat-copy table completeness + distinct titles); +11 in `apps/web/src/store/game.test.ts` (sovereigntyWar/sovereigntyBeat defaults, start/tick/end/show/dismiss actions, tick auto-fires milestone beat at 25% and 100%, no-op tick without active campaign, dismissSovereigntyBeat leaves campaign intact, reset clears both slices); +8 in `apps/web/src/sovereignty/SovereigntyBeatModal.test.tsx` (null-mount no-campaign, 25% + 100% copy, dismiss-on-click clears slice, per-milestone distinct-title each-table); +7 in `apps/web/src/sovereignty/SovereigntyWarOverlay.test.tsx` (null-mount, tint + banner mount, turns label, progressbar ARIA values, rounded percent, clamping past turnsRequired, act-wrapped unmount after endSovereigntyWar); +3 new App-level wiring tests (`apps/web/src/App.test.tsx` sovereignty-war-overlay suite) + +1 net offset from pre-existing suite growth), core=893 (unchanged), content=148 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged)

- Regression alert: false (apps/web 448 ‚Üí 493, every other count steady)
- Review proposed: true ‚Äî https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/78 (5 consecutive successes since PR #72 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-065 ‚Üí TASK-066 ‚Üí TASK-067 ‚Üí TASK-070 ‚Üí TASK-071 ‚Äî threshold hit; /autonomous-review drafted 3 refinements covering per-access defensive copies on pending-state getters (TASK-065 + TASK-070 evidence), relational invariants over literal numbers in balance-tunable registry tests (TASK-065 + TASK-066 + TASK-067 + TASK-070 evidence), and FIFO-queue + re-fire-guard Set pattern for threshold-crossing accumulators (TASK-065 + TASK-067 evidence))
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (multi-stage docker, manifest list sha256:8d574d6a7f3f84c994ad265240bbb23062c72b08526a160d22da07ea1efcaee7, config sha256:18bac69550c843d3e818809483d6b1bfe7bff6094f0a2ae677f556b282be5fd7). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Web-only change ‚Äî no server / Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Slice-driven self-mounting overlay pattern applied twice in one PR ‚Äî the red-tint+progress banner AND the beat modal ‚Äî both mount unconditionally in `App.tsx`'s game-stage block and branch internally on their own store slices (`sovereigntyWar`, `sovereigntyBeat`). Neither adds a new `Screen` literal. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Slice-driven self-mounting overlays for happens-during-an-action events": the Sovereignty War is an *ongoing* campaign that persists through pause/colony/diplomacy screens (you can check your cargo mid-siege), and the narrative beats fire *unbidden* as a consequence of ticking the campaign counter. Gating either on `screen === 'sovereignty-war'` would force the orchestrator to remember+restore the prior screen value and block the pause overlay from opening during the siege ‚Äî both wrong. Two slices, two unconditional mounts, two `return null`s when the slice is null.
  - Auto-fire the highest milestone only when a single tick crosses multiple thresholds. On a short (pacified=12-turn) campaign a catch-up orchestrator could replay several ticks in a burst; a naive "fire every crossed milestone" would stack four modals and force the player through four dismiss clicks in a row. The detector walks `SOVEREIGNTY_MILESTONES` and returns the *highest* threshold crossed in the `(prev, next]` interval, so the player sees only the most dramatic beat. Reason: same discipline as `Colony.tickProductionQueue` returning just the `completed` array per tick (not one callback per item) ‚Äî collapse parallel events into a single user-visible notification to preserve cadence.
  - Pure-sibling shape for `sovereignty-progress.ts`: progress fraction + milestone detector + beat copy table ‚Äî no React/Phaser in its import closure. The store's `tickSovereigntyWar` imports the milestone detector directly so store-logic tests can assert "tick at 19/20 fires the 100% beat" without mounting any component. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Pure-sibling pattern also applies to non-trivial React component logic" ‚Äî the branching logic (which milestone was just crossed) survives without the component and the direct-call test surface is a lot cheaper than "start campaign, tick, re-render, assert modal-testid-in-DOM".
  - Concord Fleet visibility is a non-task here ‚Äî the existing GameScene unit layer already renders any `UnitJSON` that shows up in the `units` slice. The follow-up orchestrator task (declare-sovereignty action + per-turn `tick()` wiring + map-edge spawn placement turning `pendingWaves()` into `UnitJSON` entries) is what makes ships appear; no renderer change belongs in this PR. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection" + "Only implement exactly what is requested": TASK-070 explicitly deferred the spawn wiring, and TASK-071's ask is the *UI overlay + progress tracker*. Adding spawn logic here would couple the HUD PR to the orchestration PR and violate the one-task-per-PR convention.
  - Progress bar ARIA values clamp `aria-valuenow` to `aria-valuemax` when a save-file with stale `turnsElapsed` lands past the finish line (a balance tweak that trimmed the campaign length can produce this; the fraction-clamp in `sovereigntyProgressFraction` already handles the visual fill). Reason: `aria-valuenow > aria-valuemax` is a screen-reader-invalid state, and the roll-back story for a rebalanced-down campaign should be "progress bar pegged at 100%, percent label reads 100%, ARIA reads the max value" ‚Äî not a flash of garbage in the accessibility tree. Test pins this (`aria-valuenow` with turnsElapsed=25, turnsRequired=20 ‚Üí returns 20).
  - Beat copy lives inside the pure sibling, not in `@colonize/content`. The four milestone beats are short enough (~2 lines each) that the pure sibling owning the `SOVEREIGNTY_MILESTONE ‚Üí entry` table avoids a cross-workspace hop for a three-string fetch. A later per-faction override layer (matching the OTK-specific `LegendaryWreck` flavour branch in `RumourRevealModal`) can promote the table into `@colonize/content` then, with a save-version migration if any beat id changes ‚Äî but the baseline copy is UI-side seed data until that pressure arrives. Reason: "Don't design for hypothetical future requirements" ‚Äî one consumer, one module, no cross-workspace coupling for the first version.
  - `tickSovereigntyWar` no-ops when no campaign is active rather than throwing. The orchestration task hasn't shipped yet and tests drive the store from many entry points; a `throw` from the end-turn flow on a "normal" game (no sovereignty declared yet) would be a regression the moment the follow-up task wires `tickSovereigntyWar` into the TurnPhase hook and the hook fires unconditionally. Silent no-op leaves the slice null, which is the correct post-condition for "there's nothing to tick". Same shape as `cancelQueueItem` / `reorderQueueItem` returning `{}` for out-of-range indices ‚Äî store-boundary validation is defence-in-depth, not a contract the caller must honour.
  - Pointer-events:none on every overlay layer (`.root`, `.tint`, `.banner`) ‚Äî the red vignette covers the entire game stage but must not eat Phaser map clicks. The banner intentionally does not flip `pointer-events: auto` since it's a *passive* progress display with no interactive children (unlike the `.hud > *` pattern where every child *is* interactive). Reason per CLAUDE.md "HUD overlays stay click-through where empty": an always-mounted overlay that blocks the canvas beneath it is ergonomically broken even when the overlay is decorative. Future "click progress bar for campaign details" interactivity is a layer flip on one element, not a redesign.

- Regression alert: false (core 893 ‚Üí 895, content 148 ‚Üí 158, every other count steady)
- Lessons learned:
  - `sightRadius` is a rule-relevant stat and therefore lives on `UnitTypeDefinition` in `@colonize/core`, not on the content-side `SpecialistClassEntry` alone. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Rule-relevant stats live in `@colonize/core`; descriptive / flavour stats live in `@colonize/content`": the future visibility-wiring task will call `getUnitTypeDefinition(u.type).sightRadius` from the turn loop ‚Äî which is core territory ‚Äî and a content-only field would force that call to cross the dep line. The content-side SpecialistClassEntry *mirrors* the number (like TASK-027's duplicated baseMovement) so a single HUD tooltip gets the whole stat block in one read, with a local test pinning the baseline (2√ó sloop's 2 = 4) to guard drift.
  - Ship the entity's primitive; leave the iterator to the task that owns the collection. Added the `sightRadius` field but deliberately did NOT wire a turn-loop hook that iterates every unit and calls `FactionVisibility.reveal` with the per-type radius. The future task that owns the per-faction reveal iteration can choose eager-vs-lazy, include-vs-exclude colonies, per-faction-vs-global; baking that choice in here would either couple TASK-036 to whichever iteration shape is convenient today or force a rewrite once the real collection arrives. Same discipline as TASK-026's `Unit.resetMovement()` primitive + TASK-024's `TurnManager.on/off` hooks that didn't auto-register a reset-all-units hook.
  - Cartographer + Explorer registered on the core-side UnitType const AND on a *separate* `SPECIALIST_CLASSES` registry in content, not appended to `SHIP_CLASSES`. The existing SHIP_CLASSES test suite pins a hard invariant ‚Äî "sloop and privateer share the fastest baseMovement, which is >= max across all SHIP_CLASSES" ‚Äî and folding specialist ships in at baseMovement 5 would have either broken that invariant or forced specialists down to 4 MP (losing the "higher MP than normal" design intent from the task description). A parallel `SpecialistClassEntry` lets specialists outrun the base classes without churning the canonical base-ship drift guard, and the ship-vs-specialist split matches the existing SHIP/GROUND shape on the content side. New `SPECIALIST_CLASSES` invariants lock in the design intent (faster than every base ship, fewer guns than every base ship) without pinning literal numbers that a balance pass may later tweak ‚Äî same "relationships not literals" discipline as TASK-072's Concord fleet tier ladder.
  - The exhaustive `groundBaseSpeed` switch in `packages/core/src/combat/ground-resolve.ts` picks up the two new members as a compile error the moment they're added to the UnitType const ‚Äî exactly the compile-time tripwire the CLAUDE.md "switch with no default" rule promises. Added the two Cartographer + Explorer cases to the defensive "unreachable" branch (these types are gated out by `isGroundUnitType` before the switch is reached; the return is 1 only to keep the exhaustiveness check happy). The alternative ‚Äî a `default: throw` ‚Äî would convert a caught-at-CI typecheck error into a runtime crash with no call-site pin, which is exactly the anti-pattern CLAUDE.md warns against.
  - Record<UnitType, ‚Ä¶> maps in the web workspace (`UNIT_VISUAL_SPECS` in `apps/web/src/game/unit-visuals.ts` + `UNIT_TYPE_NAMES` in `apps/web/src/hud/Hud.tsx`) are *also* compile-time exhaustive ‚Äî adding a new UnitType member fails the web typecheck until every such table has an entry. Extended both tables in this PR so typecheck stays clean without new tests (the existing table-shape tests cover the new entries by construction). This is the web-side echo of the core-side switch discipline: the type system catches the tables that need extending, so missed spots become a CI failure instead of a runtime `undefined` at render time.
  - Flavour text respects the `[ESTABLISHED]` / `[DRAFT]` / `[OPEN]` canon tiers by staying grounded in the Sparrow reference voice (first-person / close-third diary-style, salt-and-rum register with nautical metaphor + practical-edge idioms per `lore/OTK.md` ¬ß13). The Cartographer blurb names Sparrow as the narrator ("Sparrow's old craft, by her own account"); the Explorer blurb drops a diary quote without inventing a specific voyage or date so no `[OPEN]` canon gets filled in. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Lore canon is authoritative": flavour that preserves fragmentary-diary framing lets the art + narrative epics expand it later without a retcon.
  - Recruitment is flavour-only in this PR ‚Äî the task description mentions "Recruitable from tavern in a starting colony" but no recruitment registry exists yet (the Tavern building's summary is "Draws rumours; lifts crew morale between voyages"). Adding a recruitment hook here would either invent a placeholder system that the real recruitment task has to rework (violating "Don't design for hypothetical future requirements") or couple this unit-type PR to a nonexistent building system (violating "One task per PR"). The flavour text itself carries the narrative weight until the recruitment epic lands.

### Run [2026-04-23 01:30]
- Task: TASK-072 ‚Äî Victory/loss engine + game-over screen
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/80
- Test counts: core=910 (was 895 ‚Äî +15 in `packages/core/src/endgame/endgame.test.ts` covering discriminator + result-to-kind exhaustiveness, sovereignty-victory precedence, defeat only when BOTH colonies and fleet are 0, and input-validation throws for non-positive / non-integer / negative inputs), content=164 (was 158 ‚Äî +6 in `packages/content/src/epilogues.test.ts`: combinatorial 4 factions √ó 2 results = 8 entries all present with no extras, unique per-pair titles, non-empty title + body, happy-path + error-path `getEpilogue`), web=510 (was 493 ‚Äî +17: +9 in `apps/web/src/gameover/` (5 GameOverScreen DOM tests + 4 pure-sibling `computeGameOverStats` tests), +3 in `apps/web/src/store/game.test.ts` endgame block (declareEndgame atomic flip, no-op-once-declared idempotence, reset-clears-slice), +4 in `apps/web/src/game/turn-controller.test.ts` (sovereignty-victory fires on End-exit hook, annihilation when empty, no-fire while ships or colonies remain, single-fire guard), +1 in `apps/web/src/App.test.tsx` (game-over terminal screen unmounts stage + main-menu)), shared=2 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged)
- Files changed: packages/core/src/endgame/endgame.ts (new ‚Äî pure EndgameKind/EndgameResult const-object unions + checkEndgame(inputs) + endgameKindForResult exhaustive switch), packages/core/src/endgame/endgame.test.ts (new), packages/core/src/endgame/index.ts (new), packages/core/src/index.ts (re-export new symbols), packages/content/src/epilogues.ts (new ‚Äî 8-entry EPILOGUES table keyed by (factionId, result), per-faction title + body in the faction's tonal register), packages/content/src/epilogues.test.ts (new), packages/content/src/index.ts (re-export new symbols), apps/web/src/store/game.ts (new `endgame: EndgameOutcome | null` slice, `'game-over'` Screen literal, atomic `declareEndgame` action with no-op-once-declared guard; EndgameOutcome imported as a type), apps/web/src/store/game.test.ts (+endgame suite), apps/web/src/gameover/GameOverScreen.tsx (new ‚Äî terminal-screen React component reading `endgame`/`faction`/`colonies`/`units`/`factionCharters` slices, rendering epilogue copy + stats grid + Return-to-menu button), apps/web/src/gameover/GameOverScreen.module.css (new), apps/web/src/gameover/GameOverScreen.test.tsx (new), apps/web/src/gameover/gameover-stats.ts (new ‚Äî pure-sibling `computeGameOverStats` that filters colonies + units by player faction and counts charters), apps/web/src/gameover/gameover-stats.test.ts (new), apps/web/src/App.tsx (dispatch to GameOverScreen when `screen === 'game-over'`), apps/web/src/App.test.tsx (+game-over terminal-screen suite), apps/web/src/game/turn-controller.ts (register `TurnPhase.End` exit hook that calls `checkEndgame` with player-faction-filtered counts + sovereigntyWar victory predicate, dispatches `declareEndgame` when resolved), apps/web/src/game/turn-controller.test.ts (+endgame hook suite), roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (core 895 ‚Üí 910, content 158 ‚Üí 164, web 493 ‚Üí 510, shared + server steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=2 since PR #78 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-036 ‚Üí TASK-072; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (manifest list sha256:12186d962ab3bd6d0c9423f40aff6c73951068acf7a80a06e9a0a1d07ec20142, config sha256:4fa230402c87718609b05818d50d11d9e6316d20810273bfb7fdb4854ec5b010). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Web-only surface plus new core/content modules ‚Äî no server / Dockerfile / compose change needed.
- Lessons learned:
  - Victory/defeat engine ships as a pure `checkEndgame(inputs)` evaluator in `@colonize/core` ‚Äî no TurnManager coupling, no store reach-through, no per-turn scheduler baked into the primitive. The caller (apps/web's turn-controller) is the orchestrator that reads the store, filters by player faction, composes the `sovereigntyWarVictorious` boolean, calls the evaluator, and dispatches `declareEndgame`. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection": the per-turn *check-loop* is orchestration (one of several places a turn-tick could call in from ‚Äî headless server simulation, replay tooling, AI preview) and hard-wiring it into the primitive would couple every one of those callers to the turn-controller's quirks. Same discipline as `TurnManager.on/off` hooks (TASK-024) deliberately not serializing their hook registrations, and `Unit.resetMovement()` (TASK-026) deliberately not auto-registering a Start-enter reset-all hook.
  - Defeat fires ONLY when BOTH `colonyCount === 0` AND `fleetCount === 0` (annihilation), not on "no colonies" alone. Reason: a fleet with no colonies is still playable (the player can found a new one next turn), and a naive `colonyCount === 0` defeat would trigger at the very first end-turn of a brand-new game before the founding action fires. Pinned as an explicit test ("does NOT declare defeat while the faction still has a single ship") so the guard survives future rebalance work. Future defeat shapes (e.g. all-ships-captured while blockaded, bankruptcy after coin-ledger lands) plug in as additional branches in the same evaluator; the annihilation branch stays the terminal-condition backstop.
  - Victory takes precedence over defeat within a single `checkEndgame` call ‚Äî sovereignty-war-won on the same tick as "every colony fell" resolves to victory, not defeat. Reason: the endgame is a single-shot transition (the `declareEndgame` action is no-op once set), so *which* outcome fires first is the outcome the player sees forever. The narratively correct read is that winning the Sovereignty War is the campaign-defining achievement; losing the last colony on the same turn is a footnote. Pinned as a test (colony=0, fleet=0, sovereigntyWarVictorious=true ‚Üí victory, not defeat).
  - `'game-over'` joined the *terminal-screen* family in the `Screen` literal union per CLAUDE.md's terminal-vs-overlay dichotomy ‚Äî App.tsx returns `<GameOverScreen />` alone with no `GameCanvas` / `Hud` underneath. Reason: a player on the game-over screen is not *resuming* the run (the Phaser game state is gone once this PR's `reset()` fires), so the overlay pattern's "underlying canvas stays mounted" invariant would be dead weight. Also: game-over is *event-driven* (fires unbidden from the turn-controller's End-exit hook rather than from a menu button like Pause / Colony / Diplomacy), but the terminal-vs-overlay distinction is about *lifecycle* not *trigger* ‚Äî an event-triggered screen that unmounts the stage IS a terminal screen, not an overlay-screen or an unbidden-event-modal. The slice-driven self-mounting overlay pattern (`combatOutcome` / `rumourReveal`) was the wrong fit specifically because those overlays return the player to the mid-game state they came from; game-over explicitly does not.
  - `declareEndgame` flips `endgame` + `screen` in a *single* `set((state) => ‚Ä¶)` call with a "no-op once already declared" guard baked into the store. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Multi-slice zustand mutations commit in a single `set(...)` call": a race where one subscriber observes `screen='game-over'` while `endgame` is still null would render `<GameOverScreen />` with no outcome, tripping the early-`null` return and painting an empty stage for one frame. The atomic flip + the no-op-once-set guard together mean (a) a concurrent double-trigger (victory AND defeat hooks in the same tick) leaves the first-fired outcome intact, and (b) a replay / re-tick can't accidentally reset the outcome mid-game. Mirrors the `commitTrade` / `commitCargoTransfer` atomic-multi-slice precedent.
  - Pure-sibling `computeGameOverStats` lives in `apps/web/src/gameover/gameover-stats.ts` with its own test file, separate from the React component. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Pure-sibling pattern also applies to non-trivial React component logic": the stats derivation (filter colonies/units by player faction, read `factionCharters[faction]?.selected.length`, clamp malformed turn values) is the kind of small-but-not-trivial logic that's easier to test with plain JSON inputs than via render-and-walk-the-DOM. The component file shrinks to wiring + JSX and the sibling test pins the faction-filter + non-finite-turn-clamp defences directly. Same shape as TASK-048's `trade-math.ts` and TASK-049's `transfer-math.ts`.
  - Epilogue copy lives in `@colonize/content`, not alongside the endgame primitive in `@colonize/core` ‚Äî content has the factions registry and the tonal-register metadata the narrative needs, and a descriptive field like epilogue body belongs there per the "Rule-relevant stats in core; descriptive / flavour stats in content" split. The result discriminator is *duplicated* as `EndgameResultId` in the content workspace (a plain string-literal union) because the workspace dependency direction forbids content ‚Üí core imports; a combinatorial-completeness test in `epilogues.test.ts` pins `ALL_ENDGAME_RESULT_IDS` against the core-side `EndgameResult` count (indirectly via `FACTIONS.length * ALL_ENDGAME_RESULT_IDS.length === EPILOGUES.length`) so adding a new result in core surfaces here as a missing-entry failure on the next CI run.
  - Four factions √ó two results = eight epilogue entries, each respecting its faction's tonal register from `FACTIONS[].register` ‚Äî OTK epilogues lean into the eldritch/bloodline-oath voice, Ironclad into salvaged-futurism/ledger metaphor, Phantom into salt-and-rum flagless-lane imagery, Bloodborne into salt-and-rum pike-discipline bravado. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Lore canon is authoritative" + "Three tonal registers (tag flavour-text surfaces)": the UI copy is one of the narrative-contact surfaces where tonal drift would be most visible, and keeping each faction's epilogue in its own voice avoids the trap of writing generic "you won" / "you lost" copy that reads identical across four supposedly distinct factions. Also kept every epilogue under ~2 sentences ‚Äî the screen is a coda, not a synopsis.
  - Exhaustive `switch` with no `default` in `endgameKindForResult` is the writer-half of the save-format const-object rule ‚Äî adding a new EndgameResult to the const object fails the build in this function until the consumer-side branch lands, catching the "forgot to map it" class of bug at compile time rather than as a runtime `undefined` or a thrown "unreachable" error. Could have written this as a `Record<EndgameResult, EndgameKind>` lookup table of equivalent size, but the `switch` form reads as "here is the decision rule, branch by branch" and keeps the option open for per-case non-trivial branches (e.g. a future `ConquestVictory` result whose kind depends on whether the conqueror is a valid player faction); the table form locks in single-expression-per-case and forces a second helper once the first rule gets non-trivial.
  - Turn-controller exit-hook on `TurnPhase.End` is registered inside the same `bindManagerToStore` scope as the existing phase-mirroring enter hooks ‚Äî rebound by `turnController.reset()` alongside the others so the hook set stays symmetric with the manager's lifecycle. The hook itself is defensive: it reads the store *fresh* (not via a closed-over reference), no-ops when `state.endgame !== null` (double defence with `declareEndgame`'s own guard), and uses `state.faction` to filter the global unit + colony rosters to the player's own. Mirrors the `tickSovereigntyWar` store action's no-op-when-inactive shape ‚Äî store-boundary defence-in-depth against mis-fires from a future iteration pass.
  - Stats displayed on the game-over screen (turnsPlayed / colonyCount / fleetCount / charterCount) are deliberately *minimal* ‚Äî no "resources earned" / "rumours resolved" / "charters available" / "ships built vs lost" columns. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Don't add features beyond what the task requires": the task asks for "stats" (plural, but no specifics) and the four chosen rows cover the primary 4X axes (turns as pacing, colonies as territory, fleet as military, charters as narrative-progression) without committing to a stats-tracking infrastructure the rest of the game doesn't yet have. A future epilogue-beautification task can expand this with a history-tracker slice ‚Äî out of scope here.

  - Prologue joined the *terminal-screen* family in the `Screen` literal union per CLAUDE.md's terminal-vs-overlay dichotomy ‚Äî `App.tsx` returns `<Prologue />` alone with no `GameCanvas` / `Hud` underneath.   - Diary copy is hand-authored excerpts *dramatising* lore beats, not invented canon. Every beat ‚Äî Port Royal Stranger, Barataria Bay marked contingent + Dragon Mark tattoo, five-day storm with Mr. Paulson lost, doldrums mutiny-rumble with Mr. Jackson's cat, fog + Red Tide with Woodhall attending the ill, the "sacrifice to the Kraken" incident, first confirmed land since the Collapse, the Archive's Pirata Codex + family-tree recovery, the wreck, Sparrow's wounds, 250 Talisman survivors ‚Äî is [ESTABLISHED] in `lore/OTK.md`. [OPEN] items (the Stranger's identity, the Dragon Mark's full significance, the Kraken's literal relationship to the Red Tide) stay [OPEN] in the diary text ‚Äî the entries treat them as fragmentary/mysterious rather than resolving them. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Lore canon is authoritative" + "Narrative/UI text must respect [ESTABLISHED] / [DRAFT] / [OPEN] tiers ‚Äî never invent canon to fill [OPEN] gaps".
  - Subtle BGM reuses the existing `bgm-menu` stem via an HTMLAudio element rather than standing up a Phaser AudioManager for a canvas-less screen. Reason: the Phaser AudioManager is bound to the game's `SoundManager`, which only exists while `GameCanvas` is mounted ‚Äî on a terminal screen with no canvas, spinning one up would mean importing Phaser into a prologue-only code path, which per CLAUDE.md's "Browser-only libraries under jsdom" rule would drag Phaser into every test that mounts `<Prologue />` through `<App />`. A plain `<audio>` element sidesteps the canvas requirement, respects the store's `settings.muted` + `settings.bgmVolume` slices already wired up for pause-menu sliders, and swallows autoplay-block promise rejections (browsers may still reject even after the menu-click gesture if the element wasn't present at gesture time).
  - Begin + Skip both route to `'faction-select'` ‚Äî same destination, different narrative framing. Reason: Skip is for the returning player who has already read the prologue and doesn't want to sit through 17 pages; Begin is for the first-time player who read to the end and is ready to commit. There's no "Back to menu" button from the prologue because the prologue is part of the New Game flow, not a menu branch ‚Äî the player can always `Esc` to pause during gameplay and return to menu from there. Keeping Skip + Begin semantically distinct (but functionally equivalent) leaves room for a future "skip prologue on subsequent New Game" preference to override only the Skip path.
  - Linear nav (Previous / Next, Previous disabled on page 1) rather than keyboard-arrow binding. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Only implement exactly what is requested": the task asks for "Page-by-page diary presentation‚Ä¶ Skip button present" and doesn't ask for keyboard shortcuts, jump-to-page, or scroll-through-all. Explicit buttons also mean the UI is usable on mobile (Capacitor wrapper is the second deploy target) where a keyboard isn't assumed. The final-page Next-to-Begin swap is a two-branch conditional in the JSX rather than a mode flag ‚Äî the distinction *is* structural (Begin exits the screen, Next advances a counter) so the JSX conveys it directly.

- Task: TASK-079 ‚Äî Tutorial campaign trigger + step engine
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/82
- Test counts: content=179 (was 169 ‚Äî +10 in `packages/content/src/tutorial-steps.test.ts`: at-least-one-step, unique ids, trigger-turn positive-integer + non-decreasing-across-authored-ordering relational invariant, non-empty title+body copy, `targetTestId` kebab-case shape when present; plus isTutorialStepId narrow-accept/reject + getTutorialStep happy-path/throw matrix), web=534 (was 519 ‚Äî +15: +7 in `apps/web/src/tutorial/tutorial-trigger.test.ts` covering earliest-pending selection, `null` before triggerTurn reached, skip-fired-set, drain-one-per-call for save-reload case, non-finite-turn guard, empty-step-list guard; +8 in `apps/web/src/App.test.tsx` tutorial-engine suite for welcome-fires-on-game-mount, no-fire-when-disabled, no-fire-on-menu, dismiss-advances-to-next after turn ticks, no-re-fire-of-already-fired, skip-button-disables-engine, highlight-arrow-when-targetTestId-set, no-highlight-when-absent), core=910 (unchanged), shared=2 (unchanged), server=8 (unchanged)
- Files changed: packages/content/src/tutorial-steps.ts (new ‚Äî TutorialStep const-object union + registry + isTutorialStepId narrow + getTutorialStep; 4 bootstrap steps ‚Äî welcome / end-turn / menu / complete ‚Äî with TASK-080 to extend to the full authored set), packages/content/src/tutorial-steps.test.ts (new), packages/content/src/index.ts (re-export new symbols), apps/web/src/tutorial/tutorial-trigger.ts (new ‚Äî pure-sibling `nextTutorialStep(currentTurn, fired, steps)` picking earliest un-fired step with triggerTurn ‚â§ currentTurn, single-fire-per-call drain pacing), apps/web/src/tutorial/tutorial-trigger.test.ts (new), apps/web/src/tutorial/TutorialStepModal.tsx (new ‚Äî slice-driven self-mounting overlay reading `tutorialStep` slice, rendering title+body+two buttons (Got it / Skip tutorial), optional pulsing highlight outline + bobbing SVG arrow over the HUD target looked up by `data-testid`), apps/web/src/tutorial/TutorialStepModal.module.css (new), apps/web/src/store/game.ts (+`tutorialEnabled` boolean, +`tutorialStep: TutorialStepId | null`, +`firedTutorialSteps: readonly TutorialStepId[]` with +`setTutorialEnabled` / `showTutorialStep` / `dismissTutorialStep` / `skipTutorial` actions; `TutorialStepId` imported from @colonize/content), apps/web/src/menu/FactionSelect.tsx (+"Enable tutorial guidance" checkbox under the faction grid bound to `tutorialEnabled`), apps/web/src/menu/FactionSelect.module.css (+`.tutorialToggle` + `.tutorialToggleHint` styles), apps/web/src/App.tsx (orchestrator useEffect fires `nextTutorialStep(currentTurn + 1, ‚Ä¶)` on screen-to-game + turn-change + tutorialEnabled + tutorialStep transitions; mounts TutorialStepModal alongside the other slice-driven modals), apps/web/src/App.test.tsx (+tutorial-engine suite), roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md
- Regression alert: false (content 169 ‚Üí 179, web 519 ‚Üí 534, core + shared + server steady)
- Review proposed: false (streak=4 since PR #78 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-036 ‚Üí TASK-072 ‚Üí TASK-074 ‚Üí TASK-079; threshold = 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî colonize:latest rebuilt (manifest list sha256:cd9e25ab900583ffade9841dbd4f019c777af25fc9e0d96235f97c783711e5a7, config sha256:4b63d23b5b6a0cce57344bb21eaeba42a1f24b6ded90d7f754db05b5f2cc18a8). Rolling recreate of colonize-app-1; healthcheck 200 on attempt 2 at http://localhost:3000/health. Web-only + content surface ‚Äî no server / Dockerfile / compose change.
- Lessons learned:
  - Tutorial trigger policy lives in a pure-sibling `nextTutorialStep` under `apps/web/src/tutorial/tutorial-trigger.ts` that imports only `TutorialStep`/`TutorialStepId` types from `@colonize/content` ‚Äî no React, no zustand, no DOM. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Pure-sibling pattern also applies to non-trivial React component logic": the selection rule (walk the authored list, pick the earliest un-fired step whose triggerTurn ‚â§ currentTurn, single-fire per call so save-reload mid-game drains one step per tick instead of bursting a stack of stacked modals) has real edge cases (save-reload, tutorial-toggled-on-mid-game, out-of-range turn inputs) that are cheap to test with plain `Set<TutorialStepId>` + `readonly TutorialStep[]` inputs and expensive to exercise through the React orchestrator. The React side then shrinks to wiring + `showTutorialStep(step.id)`.
  - Slice-driven self-mounting for TutorialStepModal, NOT a new `Screen` literal. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Slice-driven self-mounting overlays for 'happens-during-an-action' events, NOT new Screen literals": the tutorial callouts fire mid-game during whatever the player was doing (moving a ship, reading a colony overlay, opening diplomacy), so hard-binding them to `screen === 'tutorial'` would force the orchestrator to remember the previous screen and route back on dismiss ‚Äî redundant, because an overlay that `return null`s on a null slice leaves the underlying screen mounted and interactive. Mirrors the `combatOutcome` / `rumourReveal` / `councilPickSession` / `sovereigntyBeat` precedent; distinct from `'colony'`/`'trade'`/`'transfer'`/`'diplomacy'` which ARE `Screen` literals because the player opens those *via a button*.
  - Trigger orchestrator is a React useEffect in `App.tsx`, NOT a TurnManager Start-enter hook. The TurnManager constructs at turn=1/phase=PlayerAction and does NOT fire `Start-enter` for the first turn ‚Äî a hook-based trigger would miss the welcome step on the very first render, requiring a second trigger site for game-mount and careful coordination to avoid double-fire. A React effect with deps `[screen, currentTurn, tutorialEnabled, tutorialStep, firedTutorialSteps]` catches *both* the initial `screen ‚Üí 'game'` transition and every subsequent `currentTurn` bump in one place, and the `tutorialStep !== null` guard inside the effect prevents re-enqueue while a modal is already mounted. The store's `currentTurn` is 0-indexed (ctx.turn - 1 per `bindManagerToStore`), so the orchestrator passes `currentTurn + 1` into the pure sibling ‚Äî the step's `triggerTurn: 1` matches TurnManager turn 1 even though the store shows currentTurn 0.
  - Engine scope is deliberately TASK-079-only: 4 bootstrap steps (welcome, end-turn, menu, complete) validate the trigger + modal + highlight-arrow end-to-end without claiming authorship of the full 12-15 step set that TASK-080 explicitly owns. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Only implement exactly what is requested. Do not add extra systems, abstractions, or features beyond the scope of the ask": TASK-080 lives right next to this task in `roadmap.yml` under the same STORY-46 and scopes "step authoring (12-15 steps)" as its own body of work. Authoring the full 15 here would either pre-empt TASK-080's scope or force TASK-080 into a no-op ‚Äî both wrong answers. The 4 bootstrap steps demonstrate target-and-no-target shapes (welcome + complete have no targetTestId, end-turn + menu target `hud-end-turn` + `hud-menu-button`), unblock TASK-080 to extend by appending to `TUTORIAL_STEPS`, and keep the engine's invariants (non-decreasing triggerTurn ordering, kebab-case targetTestId) locked from day one.
  - Relational invariants in `tutorial-steps.test.ts` pin design intent (trigger turns non-decreasing, ids unique, targetTestId kebab-case when present) without locking *literal* trigger-turn values ‚Äî a balance pass that shifts welcome from turn 1 to turn 2, or inserts a new step at turn 1.5 (after turn 1), passes as long as the ordering invariant holds. Reason per CLAUDE.md "Relational invariants over literal numbers in balance-tunable registry tests": the whole point of shipping TASK-079 + TASK-080 as separate tasks is to let product/design iterate on step ordering and copy without code churn. Same discipline as `packages/content/src/concord-campaign.test.ts` pinning pacified < standard < brutal rather than `pacified.turnsRequired === 12`.
  - Highlight target lookup uses `data-testid` attribute, not CSS class or id. Reason: CSS Modules hash class names deterministically but opaquely (`.topRight` becomes `._topRight_95d9c4`), and binding the highlight to a hashed class means a Vite cache bust / Tailwind refactor / CSS-in-JS swap silently breaks every tutorial callout. `data-testid` is already the test-harness identification convention for every HUD element (per CLAUDE.md "Tests identify components via `data-testid` rather than class names so CSS-Module hashing stays transparent"), so every existing HUD element already has one, and the testid survives CSS refactors. The callout target registry is therefore an implicit contract between the tutorial content and the HUD's testid naming ‚Äî documented by the kebab-case invariant in `tutorial-steps.test.ts`.
  - Pulsing outline + bobbing SVG arrow rendered as sibling absolute-positioned elements, NOT as a Phaser-side graphics overlay. Reason: the highlight target is a DOM element (HUD button / chip / year display), not a game-canvas sprite ‚Äî Phaser has no concept of a React-rendered DOM child's bounding box and would need a cross-side bus message every resize to stay in sync. An absolute-positioned React element measured via `useTargetRect(testId)` + `getBoundingClientRect()` + `resize` listener tracks the HUD reflow automatically, costs zero bus plumbing, and renders at CSS-layer z-index rather than the Phaser canvas layer (so it also survives `screen === 'pause'` / `screen === 'colony'` / etc. if a future step wants to fire an overlay-screen callout). Distinct from the rarer case of pointing at a *map tile* ‚Äî if TASK-080 authors a step targeting a specific tile coord, THAT callout would need a Phaser-side graphics overlay + bus emission. The two surfaces can coexist under the same `TutorialStep` shape: `targetTestId` for DOM, a future `targetCoord` for tiles.
  - The "Skip tutorial" button disables the engine (`tutorialEnabled = false`) but leaves `firedTutorialSteps` intact. Reason: if the player re-enables the tutorial later (menu setting, debug command, next-game start ‚Äî once `setTutorialEnabled(true)` is wired to a setting), they probably don't want to re-see steps they already dismissed *within the same game session*. Keeping the fired ledger intact gives the "resume where I left off" behaviour for free; only `setTutorialEnabled(true)` clears the ledger (fresh tutorial run at new-game time). Same pattern as `declareEndgame`'s no-op-once-declared idempotence ‚Äî the state machine has explicit invariants about which transitions clear which slices, documented in the action body rather than spread across callers.
