- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/83
- Test counts: shared=12 (was 2 ‚Äî +10 in `packages/shared/src/index.test.ts` covering User round-trip + invalid-email/non-ISO-createdAt rejection, MagicLinkRequest/Response round-trip + ok=false rejection, VerifyRequest/Response round-trip + empty-token rejection, MeResponse round-trip, ErrorResponse round-trip + missing-fields rejection), server=32 (was 8 ‚Äî +24: +13 in `apps/server/src/auth/routes.test.ts` (POST /auth/magic-link create-on-first / reuse-existing-by-case-insensitive-email / 400-on-invalid-email / 400-on-missing-body; POST /auth/verify happy-path-sets-session-cookie / 400-unknown-token / 400-replay-of-consumed-token / 400-after-expiry / 400-on-missing-token; GET /me 401-no-cookie / 401-unknown-cookie / 200-with-valid-cookie / 401-after-session-expiry), +9 in `apps/server/src/auth/in-memory-repository.test.ts` (users: case-insensitive email find + null-on-unknown + duplicate-email rejection; magic-links: consume-once-then-null + reject-expired + null-on-unknown; sessions: active-then-null-after-expiry + delete + null-on-unknown), +2 in `apps/server/src/db/migrate.test.ts` (loadMigrationsFromDir resolves the initial migration in lexical order with the expected DDL substrings, MIGRATION_TABLE_DDL declares schema_migrations with PRIMARY KEY)), web=534 (unchanged), content=179 (unchanged), core=910 (unchanged)

registers fastifyCookie + auth-routes plugin scope when `auth` provided; DEFAULT_SESSION_COOKIE_NAME + DEFAULT_SESSION_TTL_MS + DEFAULT_MAGIC_LINK_TTL_MS exports), apps/server/src/index.ts (production startup builds DrizzleAuthRepository when DATABASE_URL set, runs pending SQL migrations at boot, falls back to InMemoryAuthRepository otherwise; constructs ConsoleMagicLinkSender bound to console.info), apps/server/src/auth/repository.ts (new ‚Äî `AuthRepository` interface combining users + sessions + magic-links surface plus UserRecord/SessionRecord/MagicLinkRecord row types), apps/server/src/auth/in-memory-repository.ts (new ‚Äî Map-backed implementation with case-insensitive email normalisation, atomic consume-or-null on magic links, expiry-bounded session lookup), apps/server/src/auth/in-memory-repository.test.ts (new), apps/server/src/auth/drizzle-repository.ts (new ‚Äî postgres-js + drizzle-orm implementation; Zod-validated bodies, ErrorResponse-shaped failures, httpOnly+SameSite=Lax+secure-in-prod cookie via @fastify/cookie type augmentation), apps/server/src/auth/routes.test.ts (new ‚Äî 13 endpoint tests using app.inject + InMemoryAuthRepository + RecordingMagicLinkSender + deterministic newToken/newUserId/now overrides), apps/server/src/db/schema.ts (new ‚Äî drizzle-orm pgTable declarations for users + sessions + magic_links matching the SQL migration; uniqueIndex on users.email + index on sessions.user_id + index on magic_links.user_id), apps/server/src/db/migrate.ts (new ‚Äî forward-only file-based migration runner; reads numbered .sql files in lexical order, records applied ids in schema_migrations bookkeeping table, runs each pending file inside sql.begin transaction), apps/server/src/db/migrate.test.ts (new), apps/server/migrations/0001_init.sql (new ‚Äî CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS for users + sessions + magic_links with FK ON DELETE CASCADE + supporting indexes), docker/Dockerfile (+COPY apps/server/migrations into runtime image so the boot-time runner finds the SQL files), package-lock.json, roadmap/roadmap.yml, ROADMAP.md

- Review proposed: true ‚Äî https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/84 (5 consecutive successes since PR #78 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-036 ‚Üí TASK-072 ‚Üí TASK-074 ‚Üí TASK-079 ‚Üí TASK-082 ‚Äî threshold hit; /autonomous-review drafted 1 refinement patching `scripts/deploy.sh` to start dependent compose services before the rolling app recreate, driven by THIS run's deploy outcome where the missing postgres `db` container forced a manual recovery step before the second deploy attempt succeeded)
- Deploy: success (after one rollback + manual recovery) ‚Äî first attempt rebuilt colonize:latest (manifest list sha256:dd2a6e27dff2b2efdd280a067a8662b2f169dfab0e7908204beabf9b56c8e4c0) but the rolling recreate of colonize-app-1 timed out healthcheck after 90s (46 attempts) and `scripts/rollback.sh` restored the previous image. Root cause: this PR's startup wires `DrizzleAuthRepository` whenever `DATABASE_URL` is set (which it is in `.env`), but `scripts/deploy.sh`'s `docker compose up -d --no-deps --force-recreate app` deliberately omits dependent services to avoid db churn ‚Äî and on this host the `colonize-db-1` postgres container had never been started, so the migration runner's first connect failed and the Node process exited before listening on /health. Recovered by manually `docker compose up -d db` to bring the postgres service online (postgres:16-alpine pulled fresh, healthy in ~10s) then re-running `bash scripts/deploy.sh` ‚Äî second build (manifest list sha256:7b515ed1d3e75eaee13cbeb2d0c642b2d7721616fa8cf01a66a01fc40df67f9d, config sha256:e850eaf59e043893010d1ee0a263b0169669bbfdb72fdaf5d31ecad7370767cf) succeeded, healthcheck 200 on attempt 2, app log shows `[server] applied migrations: 0001_init` confirming the tables landed. End-to-end smoke tests against the live container: `POST /auth/magic-link {"email":"deploytest@otk.example"}` returned `{"ok":true}` + log line `magic-link issued for deploytest@otk.example` (with the verify-link in the log payload), `GET /me` without cookie returned 401 as expected. Follow-up: a separate task should patch `scripts/deploy.sh` (or docker-compose) to bring the `db` service up before `up -d --no-deps app` so first-time-postgres deploys don't need the manual recovery step ‚Äî this is deploy-infrastructure scope, not auth scope.
- Lessons learned:
  - Picked Drizzle over Kysely for the ORM. Reasons: schema-as-TypeScript via `pgTable` declarations gives `db.select().from(users).where(eq(users.email, ‚Ä¶))` autocomplete + return-type inference without a separate type-generation step (Kysely needs `kysely-codegen` against a live DB or a hand-maintained Generated interface), the wire payloads stay zod-shaped at the HTTP boundary (Drizzle plays well with that since both libs are Zod-friendly), and the `consumeMagicLink` atomicity case wants a `UPDATE ‚Ä¶ WHERE consumed_at IS NULL AND expires_at > now RETURNING user_id` ‚Äî Drizzle's chained `.update().set().where().returning()` reads as that single SQL statement. Kysely would have been equally valid; the choice is reversible because routes.ts only sees the `AuthRepository` interface.
  - One AuthRepository covering users + sessions + magic-links rather than three separate repositories. Reason: every consumer (the verify endpoint, the magic-link endpoint, the /me endpoint) coordinates across at least two of the three tables, so wiring three handles into every call-site doubles the boilerplate without buying isolation. The combined interface is one type wide at the buildApp boundary, and each implementation (in-memory or Drizzle) stays small enough to read end-to-end. If a future task needs to swap *just* the sessions backend (e.g. Redis-backed sessions), splitting will still be a one-time refactor ‚Äî the current routes don't depend on the combined-ness, only on the interface presence.
  - Magic-link consume is *atomic* on both backends ‚Äî InMemoryAuthRepository checks `consumedAt !== null` THEN sets `consumedAt = now` in a single async tick (no await between read and write), and DrizzleAuthRepository uses a single `UPDATE ‚Ä¶ WHERE consumed_at IS NULL AND expires_at > now RETURNING user_id` (Postgres MVCC handles the read-modify-write atomicity). Reason: a verify request is the most-likely place for a duplicate-submit race (browser back button, double-click on the verify link), and a non-atomic check-then-set would let two concurrent verifies both observe `consumedAt === null` and both create sessions. The interface contract on `consumeMagicLink` documents this requirement so future repository implementations (Redis, edge-cached) inherit the obligation.
  - Session token = 32-byte random hex stored server-side; cookie value is the opaque token. NOT a signed JWT or HMAC-encoded payload. Reasons: (a) server-side storage means revocation is one DELETE FROM sessions WHERE token = ‚Ä¶ rather than a token-revocation list bolted onto an otherwise-stateless JWT path, (b) the cookie carries no user-identifying payload so a leaked cookie in a server log is bounded to one session not the userId itself, (c) JWT's main appeal (stateless verification across N services) doesn't apply when there's exactly one Fastify instance; the DB lookup per /me is a single indexed primary-key fetch. Trade-off acknowledged: every authed request hits the sessions table ‚Äî fine at 1 RPS, will need a read-through cache long before it hits 1000 RPS, deferred until measured.
  - Email lookup is case-insensitive (`email.toLowerCase()` on every read AND write) on both backends. Reason: typing "Captain@OTK.example" on first login then "captain@otk.example" on second login should land the same user, not create two accounts. The normalization happens at the repository boundary (not in the route handler) so every code path that ever creates a user gets the invariant for free; the SQL migration backs this up with `users_email_unique` over the column with the route's normalized casing as the contract. (A future deploy could harden this further with `CREATE UNIQUE INDEX ‚Ä¶ ON users (lower(email))` to defend against a buggy code path bypassing the normalization, but the current single-call-site design makes that defence-in-depth rather than load-bearing.)
  - Three-tier Drizzle + SQL + migration-runner triad rather than `drizzle-kit migrate`. Reason: `drizzle-kit` is a separate generation toolchain that adds a build step (`drizzle-kit generate`), a journal file format, and a generated migrations folder ‚Äî all follow-up cost we don't need yet for one table-set. Hand-writing `0001_init.sql` keeps the wire format obvious (a SQL reviewer reads exactly what runs against Postgres), the bootleg runner in `migrate.ts` is ~30 lines and applies any future numbered files in lexical order, and the bookkeeping table (`schema_migrations`) is the same shape Drizzle would produce. If schema changes ever become frequent enough that hand-writing the SQL is annoying, swapping in `drizzle-kit` is a one-time follow-up that takes the existing migrations folder as its starting point.
  - Magic-link delivery is `ConsoleMagicLinkSender` for v1 (`logger.info(message, {email, link})`). Reason per CLAUDE.md "Only implement exactly what is requested": the task body specifies the three endpoints + session cookie + Postgres-backed users table, NOT email delivery ‚Äî adding SMTP / Resend / SES integration here would either double the dependency surface or pull in a half-baked stub I'd rather a future task own deliberately. Console-logged delivery is still end-to-end exercisable on a fresh deploy (the operator copies the link out of `journalctl -u claude-colonize.service` and pastes it into a browser), and the `MagicLinkSender` interface is the single swap-point for the future provider ‚Äî registers with `RecordingMagicLinkSender` in tests today.
  - Repository tests run against InMemoryAuthRepository, NOT Postgres. Reason: CI's `ci.yml` job is a single `ubuntu-latest` runner with `npm ci` + `npm test` ‚Äî there's no Postgres service spun up in the matrix, and adding one for this task would fork the test infrastructure without a clean revert path if the trade-off doesn't pan out. The in-memory repo mirrors the Drizzle repo's contract closely enough (case-insensitive email, atomic consume-or-null, expiry-bounded session lookup) that route tests stay representative; the DrizzleAuthRepository code path will be exercised in CI once a follow-up task brings up the docker-compose Postgres service in the test matrix. Runtime behaviour in production is still validated end-to-end via the deploy healthcheck (the / route hits the migration runner before the /health route is registered, so a broken SQL migration trips the rollback automatically).
  - `BuildAppOptions.auth` is *optional* ‚Äî when omitted, the auth routes are not registered at all (rather than registered with a default in-memory wiring). Reason: the static-only existing test suite (`apps/server/src/app.test.ts`) doesn't want auth routes leaking into its 404 + SPA-fallback assertions, and the in-memory default would force every static-serving test to also reason about cookie behaviour. Making the option opt-in keeps the existing test surface frozen while letting the production startup (`apps/server/src/index.ts`) construct the wiring deliberately based on `DATABASE_URL` presence. Mirrors `BuildAppOptions.staticRoot` ‚Äî also opt-in, also constructed by the production startup.
  - `@fastify/cookie` type augmentation is imported as a side-effect (`import '@fastify/cookie'`) in `routes.ts`. Reason: the cookie plugin augments `FastifyRequest.cookies` and `FastifyReply.setCookie` via TypeScript declaration merging, but the augmentation only takes effect in files that import the package ‚Äî `routes.ts` doesn't *use* the runtime export (the plugin is registered in `app.ts`), so a value-import would be a stale-import lint error and a type-only import wouldn't trigger the augmentation. The bare side-effect import is the documented pattern for picking up the type extension without a runtime dependency in the routes module.

### Run [2026-04-23 05:21]
- Task: TASK-083 ‚Äî Cloud save endpoints + client sync
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/85
- Test counts: shared=18 (was 12 ‚Äî +6 in `packages/shared/src/index.test.ts` covering `SaveSlotId` valid (`auto`, `slot-1`, `quick_save_2`) / invalid (uppercase `Auto`, space `slot 1`, empty, 33-char overflow), `PutSaveRequest` round-trip with opaque payload + non-positive / non-integer version rejection, `PutSaveResponse` round-trip, `GetSaveResponse` round-trip), server=48 (was 32 ‚Äî +6 in `apps/server/src/saves/in-memory-repository.test.ts` covering first-write for (user, slot), strictly-greater-version overwrite, stale-version rejection with `current` surface, same-version rejection (no clobber), (user, slot) isolation across three pairs, missing-slot null; +10 in `apps/server/src/saves/routes.test.ts` covering PUT happy-path (authenticated writes with `updatedAt` echo), PUT overwrite with subsequent GET, PUT 409 stale-version body matches current record, PUT 401 no-session, PUT 400 invalid slot id (regex rejection), PUT 400 invalid body (version=0), GET 404 missing, GET 200 with payload, GET 401 no-session, forged-session cross-user 404 isolation), web=551 (was 534 ‚Äî +17 in `apps/web/src/save/cloud-sync.test.ts` covering debounced-flush burst coalescing (3 emits ‚Üí 1 PUT), snapshot captured at flush time (not at request time), version-bump-per-success, storage-persisted-until-ack, offline buffer + `online`-emit replay, coalesce-while-offline (version stays v=1 across retries until server acks), startup-restore of pending snapshot from storage, stale-version rebase to currentVersion+1 and retry, unauthenticated stop-and-buffer, dispose unsubscribes both lifecycles, `createLocalStorageBackedStorage` round-trip + corrupt-blob-discard-and-rescue, `createFetchBackend` 200-‚Üí-ok / 409-‚Üí-stale_version / 401-‚Üí-unauthenticated / TypeError-‚Üí-network_error mapping), content=179 (unchanged), core=910 (unchanged)
- Files changed: packages/shared/src/index.ts (new `SaveSlotId` / `SavePayload` (`z.unknown()`) / `PutSaveRequest` / `PutSaveResponse` / `GetSaveResponse` Zod schemas), packages/shared/src/index.test.ts (6 new cases), apps/server/src/saves/repository.ts (new ‚Äî `SaveRepository` interface + `SaveRecord` + `PutSaveResult` union), apps/server/src/saves/in-memory-repository.ts (new ‚Äî Map-backed; same last-writer-wins semantics as Drizzle impl), apps/server/src/saves/in-memory-repository.test.ts (new), apps/server/src/saves/drizzle-repository.ts (new ‚Äî `db.transaction` with `SELECT ... FOR UPDATE` on the (user_id, slot) PK to serialise concurrent PUTs on the same slot, then conditional UPDATE vs INSERT depending on row presence), apps/server/src/saves/routes.ts (new ‚Äî PUT + GET gated on session cookie via shared `AuthRepository.findActiveSession`), apps/server/src/saves/routes.test.ts (new ‚Äî 10 cases), apps/server/migrations/0002_saves.sql (new ‚Äî `saves (user_id, slot, version, payload jsonb, updated_at)` with composite PK on (user_id, slot) and ON DELETE CASCADE against `users`), apps/server/src/db/schema.ts (new `saves` pgTable + import expansion for `integer`, `jsonb`, `primaryKey`), apps/server/src/app.ts (new `BuildAppOptions.saves` block ‚Äî requires `auth` to be wired so the save plugin inherits the session-cookie name), apps/server/src/index.ts (wire `DrizzleSaveRepository` or `InMemorySaveRepository` symmetric to the auth path; include `saves` in the drizzle schema map), apps/web/src/save/cloud-sync.ts (new ‚Äî `CloudSync` class + `createLocalStorageBackedStorage` + `createFetchBackend` helpers), apps/web/src/save/cloud-sync.test.ts (new ‚Äî 17 cases)

- Review proposed: false (1 consecutive success since PR #84 review checkpoint; threshold is 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî `scripts/deploy.sh` rebuilt `colonize:latest` (manifest list sha256:2537b8a67b1db139fddfb5339f00f5fef3e678a88e67fb9ac2f9cb6d0d189458, config sha256:79ce87a1294000694f1d9a0673f2a97f770ad2ab6b471d486df18c1db9bf26b2), the rolling recreate of `colonize-app-1` came up healthy on attempt 2 (`http://localhost:3000/health` 200 OK within 90s), and postgres (`colonize-db-1`) was already running from the prior TASK-082 recovery so no manual DB bring-up was needed this cycle. The `0002_saves.sql` migration would have applied on first boot if `DATABASE_URL` is set ‚Äî confirmed the startup code path wires `DrizzleSaveRepository` whenever `repository` is `DrizzleAuthRepository`. End-to-end verification of the save endpoints against live Postgres deferred until an authenticated smoke test (no magic-link delivery target yet ‚Äî `ConsoleMagicLinkSender` still writes the link to `journalctl`, so a manual verify would require pulling the token out of systemd logs and is not part of the autonomous cycle).
- Lessons learned:
  - Save payload is `z.unknown()` at the shared-schema boundary. Reason: the server never introspects save contents ‚Äî it only tracks a monotonic `version` + the last-written JSON blob ‚Äî and the web client's `GameState` serialization format isn't yet unified (no `serialize/deserialize` export in `@colonize/core`, just per-primitive `toJSON`/`fromJSON` pairs). Narrowing the payload now would either force a premature unified save format (which `@colonize/core`'s EPIC-07 rosters are supposed to own) or lock the server to whatever partial snapshot ships first. `unknown` keeps the wire contract stable across future save-format migrations ‚Äî the only failure mode is a client sending structurally-broken JSON, which fails at `JSON.stringify` on the way out and at `res.json()` on the way in, both before the server's business logic runs.
  - Last-writer-wins is implemented as "incoming version MUST be strictly greater than stored version" with a 409 rejection carrying the server's current record in the `GetSaveResponse` shape. Reason: "last-writer-wins" as a merge strategy can mean two things ‚Äî (a) "whichever PUT the server processes last wins, regardless of version" (client's version is advisory) or (b) "the write with the highest version wins, stale writes bounce" (server is authoritative about ordering). (b) is what the task description implies with "a version counter" ‚Äî a stale tab that was offline for 20 minutes shouldn't silently clobber the 50 moves that happened on the player's other device in the meantime. The 409 body echoes the full current record so the client's `CloudSync.flushIfPending` can rebase its pending payload onto `currentVersion + 1` and retry in-loop without a separate GET ‚Äî saves one RTT per stale-conflict.
  - `DrizzleSaveRepository.put` uses `db.transaction` + `SELECT ... FOR UPDATE` instead of a single `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE ... WHERE version < excluded.version`. Reason: `setWhere` on `onConflictDoUpdate` is new enough that verifying it across `drizzle-orm@0.45.2` and the runtime's Postgres 16 needed a live integration run, and the task's DB coverage is still in-memory-only (the Postgres docker-compose service isn't in the CI test matrix yet). The transaction path is obviously-correct to any reader without consulting the drizzle changelog, the perf delta is nil at 1 RPS (the transaction is three statements against a primary-key row, all local), and the escape hatch if we do observe deadlocks under load is to switch back to an `ON CONFLICT` path ‚Äî the `SaveRepository` interface shields every call-site from that choice.
  - Save routes live in `apps/server/src/saves/` (a new sibling module to `apps/server/src/auth/`), not inside the auth module. Reason: the two subsystems share *only* the session-cookie lookup (`AuthRepository.findActiveSession`), and folding save routes under `auth/` would blur the "auth is about who you are; saves are about what you're doing" seam. The save-routes plugin explicitly takes the `AuthRepository` as a dep (not a reimplementation) ‚Äî keeps the session-lookup path single-source while letting each module grow its own concerns (save slot governance, auth throttling, etc.) without cross-file coupling. The `app.register(scope)` block is reused so both plugins share the same cookie-parsing context.
  - `CloudSync` is a pure-TS primitive with six injected dependencies (`backend`, `storage`, `snapshot`, `timer`, `subscribeTurn`, `subscribeOnline`), NOT a React component or a zustand hook. Reasons: (a) tests run under jsdom without touching Phaser *or* React ‚Äî the Phaser-isolation rule applies symmetrically (even though CloudSync doesn't import Phaser, the tests that would exercise it as a hook would have to mount `GameCanvas` to get the bus subscription for `turn:advanced`, which pulls Phaser in via module graph), (b) the timer + storage + fetch seams are all non-deterministic in the browser and deterministic in tests via `createFakeTimer` / in-memory storage / `fakeFetch` ‚Äî injection keeps the same primitive running in both worlds, (c) the wiring task that mounts CloudSync into the running React tree will know the auth state (skip when unauthenticated), the snapshot format (which parts of `useGameStore` to include), and the slot selection (`auto` for auto-save, `quick-N` for manual), none of which CloudSync should have an opinion about. The sibling pattern matches the `tile-atlas.ts` / `fog-overlay-state.ts` precedent ‚Äî publish the logic; leave the mount-time decisions to the orchestrator.
  - Pending snapshot version is "captured once, held until acknowledged" rather than "bumped per turn event". Reason: if we incremented version on every `turn:advanced` and PUT the latest, a burst of turns-while-offline would fire 20 PUTs at versions 1 through 20 once the network came back, all of which are stale from the server's perspective (only the v=20 payload matters) and the intermediate 19 would bounce with 409. The "one pending slot; version frozen until ack" design means an offline burst coalesces into *one* PUT carrying the freshest payload at whatever version the server expects ‚Äî server-side load stays O(1) per player regardless of the offline-burst length. The version-bump happens only on a successful ack OR on a 409-rebase, both of which are rare relative to turn emits.
  - `createFetchBackend` maps HTTP responses to a discriminated-union `PutResult` rather than throwing. Reason: CloudSync's `flushIfPending` already has a retry loop driven by the result discriminant ‚Äî `ok: true` bumps ack + clears pending, `reason: 'stale_version'` rebases + retries in-loop, `reason: 'network_error' | 'unauthenticated' | 'server_error'` buffers + returns so a later `online` event or `requestSync` picks back up. Throwing would force the loop to wrap every call in `try/catch` and then re-translate exceptions into the same union ‚Äî redundant. The only exception channel that survives is a hard thrown `fetch` (network unreachable before the request is dispatched) which the backend converts to `{ ok: false, reason: 'network_error' }` via its own try/catch.

- Deploy: success ‚Äî `scripts/deploy.sh` rebuilt `colonize:latest` (manifest list sha256:097be4f6ae8f8431b9631b0c20ffa97e247459de5258fd724aac1df59973cedf, config sha256:eab5efcdb7624f28e04b1e45b6033ad7957d35121377ccfa236631329e70448c), rolling recreate of `colonize-app-1` came up healthy on healthcheck attempt 2 (`http://localhost:3000/health` 200 OK within 90s); `colonize-db-1` was already running from prior cycles so no manual DB bring-up needed. TASK-046 is pure `@colonize/core` + `@colonize/content` primitives with no DB-migration or server-route impact, so no end-to-end smoke test beyond `/health`. Post-deploy `curl /health` returned 200.
- Lessons learned:
  - The task description lists "School" and "Archive-study Hall" as two buildings but the current core registry (TASK-040) only had `BuildingType.StudyHall` named "Archive & Study Hall". Read as "Study Hall was already the rare-profession track; School is the missing common-profession gate" rather than as "rename StudyHall to School and invent Archive-study Hall from scratch" ‚Äî this keeps the save-format-bound `study-hall` id stable (no migration needed) and the flavour-text already aligns. `BuildingType.School` is added as a new member keyed to `'school'`, costed cheaply (timber + fibre, same as Tavern) with the `Tavern` prerequisite so it slots into the early-game colony path before the Chapel-gated StudyHall.
  - TrainingOrder ships as an opaque-crewId primitive *because the Crew entity hasn't landed yet*. Per CLAUDE.md "Opaque string aliases bridge pre-registry save-format identifiers", the order carries `crewId: CrewId` (re-exported from `packages/core/src/colony/colony.ts` as `string` today) and leaves the crew‚Üíprofession binding to the Crew-roster task that doesn't yet exist. TASK-045's description mentioned "Crew has current profession; can have training-in-progress" but that shipment didn't land ‚Äî profession-type is a pure scalar-lookup registry today, no Crew entity. Resisting the temptation to invent the Crew entity *here* keeps TASK-046's diff narrow to what the task names (buildings + training mechanism + 1-shot conversion) and avoids front-running a future task's design choices about roster shape, per-faction vs global collection, or how profession changes ripple through yield bonuses.
  - "Captured crew can be 'learned from' ‚Äî 1-shot conversion" is published as `TrainingOrder.instant(crewId, target)` returning an already-complete (`turnsRemaining: 0`) order. Reason: the gameplay intent is "apply the profession change without the multi-turn wait"; the orchestrator drains completed orders the same way regardless of source, so piping the 1-shot conversion through the same primitive means the capture-crew task (which doesn't yet exist) gets the same save-format + application pathway for free. A separate "apply profession change directly" API would duplicate the validation + apply logic.
  - Training durations live in `training-building.ts` as per-building tables, not pinned as top-level literals in tests. Per CLAUDE.md "Relational invariants over literal numbers in balance-tunable registry tests", the test suite asserts `max(SCHOOL_DURATIONS) < min(STUDY_HALL_DURATIONS)` and `duration >= 1` but does NOT lock `ProfessionType.Scholar` to 5 turns ‚Äî product/design will rebalance these as colony turn-counts settle, and a test that pins literal `5` would fire per-rebalance for no load-bearing reason. Reader of the durations only needs to know "rare track > common track" to write correct pathing logic.
  - `durationTable(building)` uses an exhaustive `switch` with every non-training `BuildingType` case listed explicitly returning `undefined`, rather than a `default: return undefined`. Per CLAUDE.md "Consume save-format const-object unions via an exhaustive `switch` with no `default` case", this forces the compile to fail when a new `BuildingType` lands in the registry ‚Äî the author has to *explicitly* decide whether the new building is a training building or not, rather than silently inheriting the `default` non-training fallthrough. Adds one line per new building but gains compile-time correctness at every training-aware consumer.
  - Ship the primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the owning task. TrainingOrder exposes `tick()` as a verb on the entity, but does NOT register any `TurnManager` hook ‚Äî the orchestrator that owns the collection (whether that's a per-colony `TrainingOrder[]` or a faction-wide `Map<ColonyId, TrainingOrder[]>`) decides when the turn-tick fires and in what phase (Start, End, WorldEvents all legal). Matches the `ChimesLedger` / `ConcordTensionMeter` precedent ‚Äî publish the accumulator, let the orchestration task wire it.
  - Study Hall's summary was expanded to include "Trains rarer Scholars and Loremasters" (it was previously only "Unlocks lore recovery and codex entries from salvage"). Reason: without the training mention, a player browsing the building tooltip would have no indication that Study Hall is the Scholar / Loremaster gate; the original summary covered only the codex-unlock angle. This is flavour-text drift toward the task's design intent, not a semantic change ‚Äî the save-format id `study-hall` and the cost / prerequisite tuple are untouched.

- Files changed: packages/core/src/route/merchant-route.ts (new ‚Äî `MerchantRoute` class + `MerchantRouteActionKind` save-format const-object + `MerchantRouteAction` + `MerchantRouteStop` + `MerchantRouteId` / `ColonyId` opaque string aliases; constructor validates non-empty ids, positive-integer qty, known kind, non-empty stops; `nextStopIndex` wraps via modulo; toJSON/fromJSON with defensive copy of action arrays), packages/core/src/route/auto-route.ts (new ‚Äî mutable per-ship progress tracker with `AutoRouteStatus` const-object ('active' | 'broken'); `advanceTo(index, totalStops)` with range + active-status guards; `markBroken(reason)` is sticky; toJSON/fromJSON round-trip), packages/core/src/route/tick-merchant-route.ts (new ‚Äî `tickMerchantRoute(input)` single-ship executor returning discriminated-union `TickMerchantRouteResult` with `already-broken` / `broken` / `arrived` / `travelling` / `idle` arms; - Regression alert: false (core 938 ‚Üí 1002, rest steady)
- Review proposed: false (3 consecutive successes since PR #84 review checkpoint ‚Äî TASK-083 + TASK-046 + TASK-050; threshold is 5)
- Deploy: success ‚Äî `scripts/deploy.sh` rebuilt `colonize:latest` (manifest list sha256:44c9d7e13be082ac42b1b8988fa4563b0b8f4475d35278e097110a1b491ec05f, config sha256:98eef01822849b87a04bf1fc620a8e2ccf45d9c8826d4ea9e74b16096bd58f6c), rolling recreate of `colonize-app-1` came up healthy on healthcheck attempt 2 (`http://localhost:3000/health` 200 OK within 90s); `colonize-db-1` was already running from prior cycles so no manual DB bring-up needed. TASK-050 is pure `@colonize/core` primitives with no DB-migration or server-route impact, so no end-to-end smoke test beyond `/health`. Post-deploy `curl /health` returned 200.
- Lessons learned:
  - The route + auto-route split follows the "template vs instance" seam naturally ‚Äî `MerchantRoute` is player-authored content (a route blueprint the UI lets the player assemble from existing colonies) and is immutable after construction; `AutoRoute` is the mutable per-ship progress tracker that points back at the route by id. Binding 1:1 to a ship via `unitId` keeps ship roster and route catalog independently serialisable ‚Äî when the ship is captured or destroyed, the orchestrator can drop the AutoRoute entry without touching the route template, and the same route template can be assigned to a new ship. Alternative designs (cramming currentStopIndex onto Unit, or carrying a snapshot of the route inside AutoRoute) would either grow `Unit.toJSON` with a field most ships don't use OR duplicate the route definition between template storage and per-ship state. The string-id indirection costs nothing at runtime and makes the route-builder UI's edit operation (TASK-051) a template-only change that every ship following the route inherits on next tick.
  - The executor is single-ship by design ‚Äî there is no "iterate every ship that has an AutoRoute" helper in this task. Per CLAUDE.md "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection", the roster orchestration (which Map holds the AutoRoutes, which phase of the turn they tick in, whether multiple ships tick in parallel or round-robin, what happens when two routes share a target colony and both want to load the same resource in the same turn) belongs to TASK-051 (route-builder UI) or a later roster task that owns the Map<unitId, AutoRoute> collection. This matches the ChimesLedger / ConcordTensionMeter / TrainingOrder precedent. Tests drive the executor by calling `tickMerchantRoute(input)` with synthetic fixtures, which is how the orchestrator will call it too.
  - At-colony detection uses Chebyshev-‚â§-1 not equality. Reason: colonies sit on `TileType.Island` OR `TileType.FloatingCity`. Islands are impassable for ships (`tileCost` returns `Infinity`), so a ship physically cannot stand on an island-colony tile ‚Äî it has to dock at an adjacent ocean tile. FloatingCity is passable, so the ship *can* sit on that tile. Requiring exact-equality would mean island-colony routes never complete; requiring within-1-Chebyshev handles both cases with one predicate. The pathfinder scaffold in `closestReachableTile` corresponds ‚Äî it first tries `findPath(ship, colony)` (succeeds for FloatingCity, fails for Island) then scans the 8 neighbour tiles picking the cheapest reachable one (succeeds for Island whenever any adjacent ocean tile exists).
  - Load/unload actions clamp per-line and continue the batch rather than throw-on-over-draw. Per CLAUDE.md "Clamp-and-skip out-of-range qty at the zustand store boundary" ‚Äî which actually applies symmetrically at *any* user-input-adjacent seam, not just the store ‚Äî an action carrying `qty: 10 load timber` when the colony has only 3 timber applies 3 and reports `appliedQty: 3` rather than throwing or zeroing. Reason: the route author's intent is "do as much of this as is legal"; a partial apply advances the player's goal, a thrown exception leaves the AutoRoute stalled mid-stop for no recoverable reason, and a zero-apply skips the only load the colony could supply. The per-action outcome carries both `requestedQty` and `appliedQty` so the UI can surface "took 3 of 10 requested" without re-deriving the clamp.
  - `MerchantRouteActionKind` is a save-format const-object union ('load' | 'unload') ‚Äî not an ergonomic `type X = 'load' | 'unload'` alias. Per CLAUDE.md "String-literal const-objects for save-format-bound kinds" the const-object + derived type alias + `ALL_MERCHANT_ROUTE_ACTION_KINDS` array + `isMerchantRouteActionKind` narrowing guard is the canonical shape for any union whose values round-trip through the save format. `fromJSON` uses the guard to validate untrusted input; adding a future action kind (`wait`, `drop-off-passenger`) shows up as a red squiggle at every exhaustive-switch consumer via the `Kind` exhaustive switch in the executor.
  - Movement along the path rounds fractional `sailingStepCost` results up via `Math.max(1, Math.ceil(step))`. Reason: without wind/current flags, every ocean step is cost 1; with flags, costs can be 0.25‚Äì2.25 thanks to `MIN_SAILING_STEP_COST`, but `Unit.spendMovement` is integer-only (`Number.isInteger(cost)` assertion). Rounding up is conservative ‚Äî it ensures movement budget is never over-spent ‚Äî and matches the design-intent that "favourable wind = more tiles per turn, headwind = fewer" rather than introducing a fractional movement ledger. The round-up affects only fractional-cost cases; default ocean step stays at 1. A future task that introduces per-ship fractional movement (floating-point movement points, partial-tile commits) would change this line, but that work is not in scope for TASK-050.
  - The route executor validates `autoRoute.unitId === unit.id` and `autoRoute.routeId === route.id` at the top and THROWS on mismatch (not marks-broken). Reason: those two invariants are internal contracts between the orchestrator and the executor ‚Äî "you promised this AutoRoute belongs to this ship following this route". A mismatch is a bug in the caller, not a game-state event the player should recover from. markBroken is for *game-state* invalidation (ship captured, colony destroyed) where a reasonable player response exists; mismatched ids are never reachable through normal gameplay and silently marking broken would hide the orchestrator bug. Per CLAUDE.md "Trust internal code and framework guarantees. Only validate at system boundaries" ‚Äî but the route executor IS the system boundary between orchestrator and primitive, so the id-match check belongs here with the throwing shape.

- Lessons learned:
  - Scoping the "save/name route" UX around MerchantRoute's existing `id` field instead of adding a separate `name` slot to the save format avoided a save-version migration and kept the core unchanged. The player types a name, the UI slugs it to kebab-case via `slugifyRouteName`, and that becomes the route id ‚Äî display = id round-trip. Renames during edit mode are explicit (slug ‚âÝ editingId triggers the collision check against the rest of the catalogue); renames would technically delete-then-create at the id level, but the UI surfaces it as "rename this route" which is the mental model that matters. If a future task needs a human-readable name distinct from the id (e.g. rune characters in the name for flavour), it's a ColumnAddition on MerchantRouteJSON with the same save-version-migration pattern as the other content registries ‚Äî but avoided speculatively per CLAUDE.md "Trim consumer-specific fields off save-format registries."
  - The pure-sibling pattern (routes-math.ts / route-layout.ts) was the tight-budget way to land a UI-heavy task without fighting jsdom. The RouteScreen.test.tsx suite exercises the rendered component end-to-end (click ‚Üí store read) but only for the integration contract ‚Äî the 26 routes-math tests exercise every branch of the draft‚ÜíJSON validator, the 7 route-layout tests pin the segment-emission ordering. Without the siblings these branches would have required the slow slider-drag ‚Üí DOM-text pattern that CLAUDE.md "Pure-sibling pattern also applies to non-trivial React component logic" warns against. Direct calls to `draftToRouteJSON(draft, faction, existingIds)` make every edge case a one-line assertion.
  - Merging main into the feature branch (not rebasing) was the right call when the PR came up BEHIND from PRs #88/#89 landing between branch and push. Per CLAUDE.md "Do not take destructive git actions without explicit user approval," `git merge origin/main` + push is non-destructive and the squash-merge on auto-merge collapses the whole feature branch (including the merge commit) into one commit on main ‚Äî the feature-branch history before squash is transient and nobody else is tracking it.

### Run [2026-04-23 11:14]
- Task: TASK-052 ‚Äî Price-drift tick + event-triggered shocks
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/91
- Test counts: core=1021 (was 1002 ‚Äî +19 across `packages/core/src/homeport/homeport.test.ts` (drift: no-op on zero, positive/negative nudge by PRICE_DRIFT_STEP, no-overshoot snap-to-zero, multi-resource independence in one tick, 100-tick return-to-baseline convergence, zero-entry purge from sparse map, insertion-order-independent determinism; shock: crash lowers mid, spike raises mid, MIN_MID_PRICE / MAX_MID_PRICE clamp holds on huge deltas, compose-additively with prior player volume, shock + opposite shock clears, tick-reversibility; rejects: zero/fractional/NaN volumeDelta, untraded resource)), content=194 (was 181 ‚Äî +13 across `packages/content/src/price-shocks.test.ts` (table non-empty; ids unique; every shock references a known ResourceEntryId; every resource covered by ‚â• 1 shock; every resource has ‚â• 1 spike AND ‚â• 1 crash; direction label matches volumeDelta sign; every |volumeDelta| a non-zero integer multiple of PRICE_VOLUME_STEP; flavour copy non-empty; every register tag is a known ToneRegister; getPriceShock/isPriceShockId by id; rejects unknown id; listPriceShocksForResource scope + synthetic-id empty)), web=617 (unchanged), server=56 (unchanged), shared=18 (unchanged)
- Files changed: packages/core/src/homeport/homeport.ts (+PRICE_DRIFT_STEP const, +`tickPriceDrift()` method nudging every non-zero entry toward 0 by PRICE_DRIFT_STEP per call, +`applyPriceShock(resourceId, volumeDelta)` method reusing `_mutateVolume` with positive-delta = crash / negative-delta = spike sign convention and rejecting zero/fractional deltas), packages/core/src/homeport/index.ts (+PRICE_DRIFT_STEP re-export), packages/core/src/index.ts (+PRICE_DRIFT_STEP re-export), packages/content/src/price-shocks.ts (new ‚Äî PriceShockDirection 'spike'|'crash' literal union, PriceShockEvent interface {id, resourceId, direction, volumeDelta, flavour, register}, PRICE_SHOCKS 12-entry readonly table covering all 6 resources √ó both directions with salt-and-rum / eldritch / salvaged-futurism register tags, getPriceShock lookup, isPriceShockId guard, listPriceShocksForResource filter), packages/content/src/price-shocks.test.ts (new, 13 relational-invariant cases), packages/content/src/index.ts (+6 re-exports), packages/core/src/homeport/homeport.test.ts (+19 cases)
- Regression alert: false (core 1002 ‚Üí 1021, content 181 ‚Üí 194, rest steady)
- Review proposed: <filled below if triggered>
- Deploy: success ‚Äî `scripts/deploy.sh` rebuilt `colonize:latest` (manifest list sha256:2ed5602d3774c618cf5ff04d365e4c7e671b2943b62da0ec50e6fa4e5da74897, config sha256:172917d06daf47089550fe99b9787273f978482a9208ea6b94157ea51d402efb), rolling recreate of `colonize-app-1` came up healthy on healthcheck attempt 2 (`http://localhost:3000/health` 200 OK within 90s); `colonize-db-1` was already running from prior cycles so no manual DB bring-up needed. TASK-052 is pure `@colonize/core` + `@colonize/content` primitives with no DB-migration or server-route impact, so no end-to-end smoke test beyond `/health`.
- Lessons learned:
  - Split the primitive between two axes ‚Äî `tickPriceDrift` (periodic equilibrium pull, orchestrator-scheduled) and `applyPriceShock` (one-shot event mutator, trigger-driven) ‚Äî rather than collapsing both into one `advancePrices(deltaMap)` call. Reason: they have fundamentally different cadences (drift fires every turn unconditionally; shock fires sporadically on a trigger like a world event / random roll / faction-specific narrative beat) AND different sign patterns (drift always moves toward zero regardless of current sign; shock moves the magnitude further from zero in whichever direction the content event specifies). A combined signature would either lose information (one `deltaMap` can't encode "drift toward zero by this much while also spiking this resource by that much") or force callers to pre-resolve the sum (duplicating the toward-zero logic in every caller). Two primitives keep each one minimal and the caller composes by calling both in sequence in whatever order the orchestrator prefers.
  - Shock sign convention follows the existing `recordPlayerSale` / `recordPlayerPurchase` axis rather than introducing a new "shock magnitude" concept. Positive `netVolume` = glut (player has been a net seller = market is flooded = mid-price drops); shock `volumeDelta > 0` = crash (same direction). Negative `netVolume` = scarcity (player has been a net buyer = market is starved = mid-price rises); shock `volumeDelta < 0` = spike. This reuse means `applyPriceShock` delegates to the same `_mutateVolume` as player trades with no branching ‚Äî the bound clamping, zero-purge, and emit-sort rules all apply uniformly. Alternative was a magnitude-and-direction pair (`applyPriceShock(resource, 'spike'|'crash', magnitude)`) but that's two parameters carrying one signed integer's worth of information; the signed-delta shape is both simpler and more composable.
  - Content event table carries a `direction: 'spike'|'crash'` *label* field even though `Math.sign(volumeDelta)` encodes the same thing. Reason: narrative copy pairs resolution (the flavour line reads as either "prices plummet" or "prices climb" ‚Äî not as a signed-integer fact), and content authors think in terms of the story-side direction, not the engine-side sign. Test invariant (`direction === 'crash' ‚Üî volumeDelta > 0`) catches drift between the two fields at CI time so the narrative-side label never diverges from the mechanical-side effect. This is a soft form of the "Trim consumer-specific fields off save-format registries" rule inverted ‚Äî the label is *not* consumer-specific, it's dual-audience (content author + UI formatter), so pinning both sides earns its keep.
  - Test magnitudes pin relational invariants (direction-sign match, divisibility by PRICE_VOLUME_STEP, per-resource coverage of both directions) rather than literal volumeDeltas. Reason: shock magnitudes ARE balance-tunable ‚Äî a TASK-052 spike at `-15` today might move to `-10` or `-20` after a balance pass, and a test locking the literal value would break on every such tweak. The "Relational invariants over literal numbers in balance-tunable registry tests" rule applies symmetrically to every content registry the engine reads (ships, buildings, resources, now price shocks): future rebalance PRs change numbers but not shapes, and the suite should fail only on shape regressions.
  - `PRICE_VOLUME_STEP` is duplicated in content's price-shocks test rather than imported from core. Reason: the dependency-direction rule (`web/mobile/server ‚Üí core/shared/content`, never the other way) forbids content importing core, and the same rule applies to content tests. The existing `homeport-prices.test.ts` precedent mirrors `MIN_MID_PRICE` / `MAX_MID_PRICE` the same way. The drift-risk cost is one line in the test file plus a comment pointing at the core source; a cross-workspace import would cost a circular dependency check every CI run.

- Task: TASK-056 ‚Äî Privateer raid action + merchant-route vulnerability
- Outcome: success
- PR: https://github.com/g-chappell/colonize/pull/92
- Test counts: core=1038 (was 1021 ‚Äî +17 across `packages/core/src/raid/resolve-raid.test.ts`: success path with floor(qty * 0.5) per resource (timber 4‚Üí2, provisions 6‚Üí3, gold qty 1 unstolen because floor(0.5)=0); cargo-stolen events emit in alphabetical resource-id order (gold, provisions, timber) for cross-machine replay parity; artifacts transfer wholesale (kraken-talisman + tide-shard moved in full); BASE_RAID_LOOT_FRACTION=0.5 constant; Phantom Corsairs floor(qty * 0.75) (timber 4‚Üí3, provisions 8‚Üí6, gold 2‚Üí1) via existing factionRaidLootMultiplier(1.5); phantom out-loots ironclad on identical victim (6 vs 4 timber); escortPresent=true returns blocked-by-escort with empty loot + zero events beyond raid-blocked-by-escort + zero cargo movement; empty target (no cargo) returns empty-target with raid-empty-target event; sub-fractional-only target (every resource qty=1) also returns empty-target leaving cargo intact; throws TypeError on non-Privateer attacker (Sloop), non-ship victim (Settler), self-raid, non-boolean escortPresent; throws plain Error on same-faction raid; victim hull-equivalent (position + movement) untouched after raid; non-phantom playable factions (otk, ironclad, bloodborne) all use base 0.5; non-playable faction id ('npc-pirates') defaults to 0.5), web=617 (unchanged), server=56 (unchanged), content=194 (unchanged), shared=18 (unchanged)
- Files changed: packages/core/src/raid/raid-outcome.ts (new ‚Äî RaidResult string-literal union 'success'|'blocked-by-escort'|'empty-target' + ALL_RAID_RESULTS array; RaidLootSnapshot {resources: Readonly<Record<ResourceId, number>>, artifacts: readonly ArtifactId[]}; RaidEvent discriminated union {raid-blocked-by-escort | cargo-stolen w/ resourceId+stolenQty | artifact-stolen w/ artifactId | raid-empty-target}; RaidOutcome {result, loot, events}), packages/core/src/raid/resolve-raid.ts (new ‚Äî pure resolveRaid(privateer, victim, opts) function with BASE_RAID_LOOT_FRACTION=0.5 const + ResolveRaidOpts {escortPresent: boolean}; runtime-validates UnitType.Privateer attacker, isShipUnitType(victim.type), no self-raid, no same-faction, opts shape; escort path returns blocked-by-escort with empty loot pre-mutation; loot path snapshots victim.cargo.entries() sorted alphabetically + iterates resources stealing min(qty, floor(qty * effectiveFraction)) and skipping zero-stolen sub-unit cases; artifacts iterate via cargo.artifacts (already sorted defensive copy) and transfer wholesale; effectiveLootFraction multiplies by factionRaidLootMultiplier when isPlayableFactionId(faction) else defaults to 0.5; events array emits cargo-stolen + artifact-stolen in deterministic order for cross-machine replay parity; result computed as 'empty-target' when nothing stolen, 'success' otherwise; mutates both ship cargo holds in-place via removeResource/addResource and removeArtifact/addArtifact), packages/core/src/raid/index.ts (new barrel re-exports), packages/core/src/raid/resolve-raid.test.ts (new, 17 cases), packages/core/src/index.ts (+5 re-exports: ALL_RAID_RESULTS, BASE_RAID_LOOT_FRACTION, resolveRaid + RaidEvent, RaidLootSnapshot, RaidOutcome, RaidResult, ResolveRaidOpts types)
- Regression alert: false (core 1021 ‚Üí 1038, rest steady)
- Review proposed: <filled below if triggered>
- Deploy: success ‚Äî `scripts/deploy.sh` rebuilt `colonize:latest` (manifest list sha256:f11dc44f5513204227ee28bdfe231021874c9308723a382305a86c446cfb7fbf, config sha256:9bf3c2809d2566e0d279f054bb0744f9d21efc12f30aed68c7e25890b8d898d7), rolling recreate of `colonize-app-1` came up healthy on healthcheck attempt 2 (`http://localhost:3000/health` 200 OK within 90s); `colonize-db-1` was already running from prior cycles so no manual DB bring-up needed. TASK-056 is pure `@colonize/core` (new `packages/core/src/raid/` module + 5 re-exports from the core barrel) with no DB-migration or server-route impact, so no end-to-end smoke test beyond `/health`.
- Lessons learned:
  - Skipped storing ambush state on Unit (no `ambushTile?: Coord` field) and skipped wiring into `tickMerchantRoute` (no executor changes). Per CLAUDE.md "Ship the entity's primitive; leave iteration / scheduling to the task that owns the collection": the resolver takes the two ships involved + an explicit `escortPresent` flag and resolves a single raid event. The orchestrator (a future task ‚Äî likely paired with the world-events / per-turn AI scheduler that decides which privateer is "ambushing" which tile) iterates units, pairs privateer+victim by position, and calls this once per raid. Saving an `ambushTile` field now would force every Unit save-format consumer to handle a field used only by Privateers, and wiring into tickMerchantRoute would couple raid policy to the executor that owns its own broken/arrived/travelling state machine. The split keeps both modules small.
  - Reused the existing `factionRaidLootMultiplier(faction)` from `packages/core/src/faction/faction-bonus.ts` (which already returned 1.5 for Phantom and 1.0 for everyone else) rather than introducing a new "raid bonus" axis. The resolver multiplies BASE_RAID_LOOT_FRACTION by that scalar to produce the effective per-faction fraction. This is the "Scalar seams for pre-registry axis values" pattern in its mature form: `faction-bonus.ts` shipped the lookup ahead of any consumer (TASK-053-era), TASK-056 is the first consumer, and the per-faction tuning never leaked into the resolver. A future event-tuning system or rumour-modifier system can extend the multiplier without touching `resolveRaid`.
  - Faction validation degrades gracefully via `isPlayableFactionId(faction)` ‚Äî non-playable factions (NPC pirates, future neutral merchants) get the base 0.5 fraction with no error. Reason: Unit.faction is the open `FactionId = string` alias, not a closed PlayableFactionId union, so a privateer could in principle belong to a non-playable faction (e.g. an NPC raider). Throwing on that case would have made the resolver brittle to a concept that core deliberately keeps loose (per the CLAUDE.md "Opaque string aliases bridge pre-registry save-format identifiers" rule). Defaulting to base fraction is the right shape: the resolver still resolves, the faction bonus simply doesn't apply.
  - Resource theft is fractional-and-floored (stolen = floor(qty * fraction), capped at qty), and qty=1 is uncatchable for both base (floor(0.5)=0) and Phantom (floor(0.75)=0). The "every resource qty=1" test pins this as a deliberate property ‚Äî the resolver returns 'empty-target' rather than 'success' with empty loot when nothing actually moves. Reason: this matches the player's mental model ‚Äî a successful raid moves *something*, not just a "we tried" event. The combat resolver uses the same shape (a flee attempt that does no damage and fails returns Inconclusive, not AttackerFled). Distinguishing 'empty-target' from 'success' lets the future UI render different copy ("nothing to steal") vs the standard success spinner.
  - Resource event ordering is alphabetical-by-id (sorted at snapshot time). Reason: per CLAUDE.md "Map/Set-backed save-format emitters sort entries in `toJSON` for byte-parity determinism", an orchestrator that replays raid logs across machines depends on identical event sequences for the same input. The CargoHold's internal Map has insertion-order semantics, so a sloop that loaded {timber, provisions, gold} would produce a different event order from one that loaded {gold, provisions, timber} ‚Äî visually identical state but a different replay log. Sorting at snapshot time costs O(N log N) on a ~6-resource hold (effectively free) and removes a class of cross-machine flakes.
  - Tests pin the relational invariant "phantom out-loots non-phantom on the same victim cargo" (6 vs 4 timber) alongside the literal value (timber 4‚Üí3 for phantom, 4‚Üí2 for base). The literal test would break on a balance pass that drops BASE_RAID_LOOT_FRACTION to 0.4 or pushes phantom's multiplier to 1.6; the relational test would survive any rebalance that preserves the design intent (phantom > non-phantom). Per CLAUDE.md "Relational invariants over literal numbers in balance-tunable registry tests" the balance-tunable scalar gets pinned via the RELATIONSHIP, with one literal test alongside as a regression tripwire on the current value. Both kinds of tests earn their keep here.
  - Artifacts transfer in full regardless of faction multiplier ‚Äî they are unique items, not fungible. A "fractional artifact theft" rule (e.g. phantom steals 1.5 ‚Üí 2 artifacts, base steals 0.5 ‚Üí 0 artifacts) would either be confusing for the player ("which artifact?") or trivialise the bonus (phantom always steals 1, base often steals 0). The current shape is the simplest interpretation of "cargo stolen" that reads cleanly to the player. A future "selective theft" mechanic (privateer chooses which artifacts to steal up to a hold capacity) is an orchestrator concern, not a resolver one.

- Regression alert: false
- Review proposed: false (will check at Step 15)
- Deploy: success (colonize:latest deployed via rolling strategy; healthcheck 200 OK on attempt 2 ‚Äî http://localhost:3000/health)
- Lessons learned:
  - "Trim consumer-specific fields off save-format registries" applied symmetrically here: BuildingDefinition does NOT carry a defenseBonus field ‚Äî the combat axis owns its own lookup in `combat/fortification.ts`. The training-axis pattern (`training-building.ts`'s exhaustive switch over BuildingType, returning a per-table opaque scalar) is the model; fortification.ts is the second consumer to follow it, which is good evidence the shape generalises across "consumer N reads BuildingType to derive a per-tier scalar" axes.
  - "Scalar seams for pre-registry axis values" applied to `defenderFortificationBonus` on GroundCombatContext: the resolver doesn't import building/colony at all, the orchestrator (the future raid-against-colony task) will call `getFortificationDefenderBonus(colony.buildings)` and pass the scalar. Edge validation lives at the resolver boundary (positive finite); no migration cost when the orchestration task lands.
  - "Pure-sibling module pattern for Phaser game code" extended to a cosmetic axis: colony-fortification.ts derives `{ tier, strokeColor, strokeWidth }` from a ColonyJSON in 75 lines with zero Phaser in its closure; game-scene.ts just calls it and applies via `body.setStrokeStyle`. Container stores the body ref via `setData('body', body)` so syncColonyContainers can re-apply the style on every diff (a stockade built mid-game refreshes the colony stroke without rebuilding the container).
  - "Relational invariants over literal numbers" pinned across THREE files for one feature: combat-bonus ladder (Stockade < Bastion < Citadel), content-cost ladder (sum-of-cost ascending), and visual stroke-width ladder (none < stockade < bastion < citadel). Future balance pass can retune any of the three multipliers (combat bonus 1.20/1.40/1.65, cost totals, stroke-widths 2/3/4/5) without touching tests as long as the ordering survives.
